Elijah immediately decreed a drought, and God granted it to him. Elijah had to run away to the desert, where ravens brought him bread and meat, and he drank from a brook. Eventually, the brook dried out, and Elijah was commanded to go live in Tsarfat. When the son of his hostess died, Elijah wanted to revive him, but God said, “I have three keys – from childbirth, rain, and resurrection. It is not proper for Me to have one, and for you – two. Elijah had to give up the key to rain, and the drought ended.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yose called Elijah an irascible person. Elijah hid from him for three days. When Elijah came, Rabbi Yose asked, “Why were you hiding?” Elijah answered, “You called me irascible!” Rabbi Yose said, “So you are irascible again!”<br />
<br />
Art: Rain Storm, Union Square by Childe Hassam</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/12.txt
<a id="src-00041"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/12.txt`

Sanhedrin 12 – When to Declare a Leap Year
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEht9p1_4lB83Efs54S-CH-fg8FxYlM8fXn76XnTjM7sPkh-qPOapHTybAWBS_im23eTIV05FgirrczXZoKqMzqWahsCE2TLNTfo8fTNLpPz14hRqv5XD0fHFUvHVxWEqYWumExvB57pdks/s1600-h/Joseph+Mallord+William+Turner+-+Jerusalem+from+the+Latin+Convent.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEht9p1_4lB83Efs54S-CH-fg8FxYlM8fXn76XnTjM7sPkh-qPOapHTybAWBS_im23eTIV05FgirrczXZoKqMzqWahsCE2TLNTfo8fTNLpPz14hRqv5XD0fHFUvHVxWEqYWumExvB57pdks/s320/Joseph+Mallord+William+Turner+-+Jerusalem+from+the+Latin+Convent.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">It may be necessary to proclaim a leap year if the grain is too young by Passover, if the ovens for Passover sacrifices became ruined in the rain, or because the Jews in the Diaspora started on their journey to Jerusalem but will not reach it on time. Additionally, the sheep and goats may be too young by Passover, or the doves may be too tender.<br />
<br />The extra month of the leap year is always inserted before the month of Passover; thus, it becomes the Second month of Adar, when Purim is celebrated.<br />
<br />
However, a leap year is never proclaimed before Rosh HaShanah, for if it were, people might forget about it by the time the Second Adar comes six months later. Then, they might mistakenly celebrate Passover on the Second Adar and consequently transgress the prohibition of eating leavened bread during actual Passover.<br />
<br />
Art: Jerusalem from the Latin Convent by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Joseph Mallord William Turner</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/13.txt
<a id="src-00042"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/13.txt`

Sanhedrin 13 – Semichah of the Sages
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjBHf9EZItaLcvaBVkyHRAK3DiSrYRZ0hQAUl0dqVLGhsUGCtGkGxW71sZR06430PXLTLvrWkpnhmrg4oSp8tJ1CfjUhP65mXiN8UePDnhEJQZOqLv3lCwLT5ltYDpDMwqmFH6BlXY4bFU/s1600-h/Jean-Honore+Fragonard+-+Jeroboam+Offering+Sacrifice+for+the+Idol.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjBHf9EZItaLcvaBVkyHRAK3DiSrYRZ0hQAUl0dqVLGhsUGCtGkGxW71sZR06430PXLTLvrWkpnhmrg4oSp8tJ1CfjUhP65mXiN8UePDnhEJQZOqLv3lCwLT5ltYDpDMwqmFH6BlXY4bFU/s320/Jean-Honore+Fragonard+-+Jeroboam+Offering+Sacrifice+for+the+Idol.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the majority of the Jews transgressed and worshiped an idol because the Sanhedrin mistakenly ruled that this was permitted, and then they realized their mistake, the Sages of that Sanhedrin bring a bull, lean their hands on it, and confess. This is called Semichah, and three Sages are required for that. <br />
<br />
Semichah can also mean Rabbinical ordination in an unbroken chain since Moses. Once the Romans enacted that anyone who confers ordination is killed, anyone who accepts ordination is killed, and the nearest town is destroyed. Yehudah ben Bava placed himself between two mountains and ordained five Sages there. When the enemies discovered them, he told his students, "My sons, run! I will be like a rock that cannot be turned." The soldiers drove three hundred spears through him and made him like a sieve. Three Sages are required for ordination, but Yehudah ben Bava alone is mentioned because of his importance.<br />
<br />
Art: Jeroboam Offering Sacrifice for the Idol by Jean-Honore Fragonard</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/14.txt
<a id="src-00043"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/14.txt`

Sanhedrin 14 – The Decapitation of the Calf
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiXnTIqOWwYNSqJ3jlik4dp7yPCtc4hrE8BmDstI7QwKuTizTQ520BfXeNIcH24b_tHMQyjySFqRMzFkVnsf5rUVgN_T9oLyTql4L7S6Sv80TjOTC074Q6-1lbTzKvltQlGwRTGxkl5yBQ/s1600-h/Honor%C3%A9+Daumier+-+The+Stomach+of+the+Legislature+the+Ministerial+Benches+of+1834.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiXnTIqOWwYNSqJ3jlik4dp7yPCtc4hrE8BmDstI7QwKuTizTQ520BfXeNIcH24b_tHMQyjySFqRMzFkVnsf5rUVgN_T9oLyTql4L7S6Sv80TjOTC074Q6-1lbTzKvltQlGwRTGxkl5yBQ/s320/Honor%C3%A9+Daumier+-+The+Stomach+of+the+Legislature+the+Ministerial+Benches+of+1834.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Suppose the body of a murder victim is discovered outside a town in the Land of Israel, and it is not known who killed him. The city nearest to where the body was found has to take a calf that was never worked and bring it to a valley of unworked ground, <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/21-1.htm">where it is decapitated</a>. <br />
<br />
Measuring which town is nearest has to be carried out by three judges, members of the Great Sanhedrin. The decapitation of the calf is then performed by the court of the town that is nearest.<br />
<br />
However, the members of the Sanhedrin do not generally leave the Chamber of Hewn Stones in the Temple since "<a href="http://bible.cc/songs/7-2.htm">Your navel is like a moon-shaped basin; let not the strength of the blend diminish</a>." is allegorically referring to</span><span style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;the members of the Sanhedrin, who sat in a semicircle.<br />
<br />
Art: The Stomach of the Legislature the Ministerial Benches of 1834 by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Honore Daumier</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/15.txt
<a id="src-00044"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/15.txt`

Sanhedrin 15 – Appraisals
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmChUZXMLOKO0E8tx0baYyGuBsAB_qdU7pPDqIiaUrVr2VXQHJ6M343ew5faZzfeQzH-fx2QG9KGo3VzKY50kgzRV7vBJrpC22KKAazE2pvICw-qMpNYGwZ8kRjWFXMcH2mzOyKi25MrQ/s1600-h/Vincenzo+Guarana-+Portrait+of+three+lawyers.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmChUZXMLOKO0E8tx0baYyGuBsAB_qdU7pPDqIiaUrVr2VXQHJ6M343ew5faZzfeQzH-fx2QG9KGo3VzKY50kgzRV7vBJrpC22KKAazE2pvICw-qMpNYGwZ8kRjWFXMcH2mzOyKi25MrQ/s320/Vincenzo+Guarana-+Portrait+of+three+lawyers.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Produce grown in the Land of Israel must have tithes separated from it, with the second tithe taken to Jerusalem and consumed there. If one wants to redeem it for money and its value is unknown, three people must estimate it. Three merchant appraisers are required for this and can even be partners.<br />
<br />
Items consecrated to the Temple need three appraisers to be redeemed; consecrated lands need nine appraisers and a Kohen.<br />
<br />
All cases of capital crimes require the Small Sanhedrin of twenty-three judges. If an animal is involved, like in the cases of sodomy, or when an animal kills a human, the animal is judged by the court of twenty-three, similar to human cases.<br />
<br />
Art: Portrait of Three Lawyers by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Vincenzo Guarana</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/16.txt
<a id="src-00045"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/16.txt`

Sanhedrin 16 – Judging the Tribe, the Prince, the High Priest
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNeAJlF5TZQ8nyHFHwv3x_dxU8-iB2ERuviis91qnGyIJN7PkUPrGy1tQOD-VCGr4BuUdzcTHKqI0oOJWU9miRWnUxDoy72FyGjUQS9Ch5_guF7eSjhaJ8KvOkSIVnopyjPlgZZfGtASk/s1600-h/Henry+Courtney+Selous-+Jerusalem+in+her+Grandeur.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNeAJlF5TZQ8nyHFHwv3x_dxU8-iB2ERuviis91qnGyIJN7PkUPrGy1tQOD-VCGr4BuUdzcTHKqI0oOJWU9miRWnUxDoy72FyGjUQS9Ch5_guF7eSjhaJ8KvOkSIVnopyjPlgZZfGtASk/s320/Henry+Courtney+Selous-+Jerusalem+in+her+Grandeur.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A tribe is judged by the Great Sanhedrin of seventy. An entire tribe could be judged when all its members serve idols and stand to be stoned, when it has a territorial dispute with another tribe, or when a prince has committed a capital offense.<br />
<br />
The High Priest is judged by the Great Sanhedrin, according to "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/18-22.htm%20">and every great matter you will bring to me</a>."&nbsp; What about an ox of the High Priest? Is it judged by the Great or Minor Sanhedrin? - remains unresolved.<br />
<br />
The boundaries of the city of Jerusalem or the Courtyard in the Temple can only be extended with the help of the Great Sanhedrin, and a subverted town – one, most of whose inhabitants served idols – can be so designated only by the Great Sanhedrin.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Jerusalem in her Grandeur by Henry Courtney Selous<br /><br /></span></div>

---

### content/sanhedrin/17.txt
<a id="src-00046"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/17.txt`

Sanhedrin 17 – The Great Sanhedrin
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhi8U0gsfgg02vGg-yJ3sxgYpvzP5PAkKBCvudc4cygz78gAQNyUXV5RJNlZVL2VekqQA732L8yTauZPyUxu6zCoiRGopqGNBnrdCRZyYobcq8yubAV4_uvzSURmjjxSAKU6SQ1c5D_SVc/s1600-h/Lucas+The+Elder+Cranach-+Self-portrait.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhi8U0gsfgg02vGg-yJ3sxgYpvzP5PAkKBCvudc4cygz78gAQNyUXV5RJNlZVL2VekqQA732L8yTauZPyUxu6zCoiRGopqGNBnrdCRZyYobcq8yubAV4_uvzSURmjjxSAKU6SQ1c5D_SVc/s320/Lucas+The+Elder+Cranach-+Self-portrait.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Great Sanhedrin comprised seventy-one judges since Moses is counted as part of it. Rabbi Yehudah, however, says that the Sanhedrin had only seventy judges since Moses was not counted among them.<br />
<br />
Moses selected six judges from each of the twelve tribes. Then, he used lottery tickets that either said “Sage” or were empty. However, Eldad and Meidad remained in the camp because they thought themselves unworthy (alternatively, they were afraid not to be selected). Instead, they were granted prophesy.<br />
<br />
The members of the Sanhedrin must be men of height, wisdom, moderate old age, acquainted with witchcraft, and who know seventy languages so that they hear the testimony directly and not through an interpreter. They should be able to prove from the Torah that an obviously non-kosher thing is kosher.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Self-portrait by Lucas The Elder Cranach<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/sanhedrin/18.txt
<a id="src-00047"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/18.txt`

Sanhedrin 18 – Size of a Town Fit to Have a Sanhedrin
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh72dVXNbEmiy-N6gkeBbMknjvuy_IMB-ft6fQ7mMKhxgN-Ff8Y1RuNDsiSnwItC35d_JloUIzuspAWRJBN274JCzZBWeIHjTgcD0pAHkvexz8EVbhazPVjzGXK3V581EA-qYGCLDcTusA/s1600-h/Grigori+Grigorevich+Chernetsov+-+Parade+on+the+Field+of+Mars.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh72dVXNbEmiy-N6gkeBbMknjvuy_IMB-ft6fQ7mMKhxgN-Ff8Y1RuNDsiSnwItC35d_JloUIzuspAWRJBN274JCzZBWeIHjTgcD0pAHkvexz8EVbhazPVjzGXK3V581EA-qYGCLDcTusA/s320/Grigori+Grigorevich+Chernetsov+-+Parade+on+the+Field+of+Mars.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The town fit for a Sanhedrin must have at least 120 residents: 23 replacements, in case the acting members should all die and need to be replaced, three rows of 23 scholars, ten unoccupied men in the synagogue, two court stenographers, two court officers, two litigants, two witnesses, two people who can discredit the witnesses, and two who can discredit those who discredited the witnesses. Add to this charity collectors, a doctor, a butcher, and a teacher of children.<br />
<br />
The High Priest may judge and be judged. But that is obvious!? You might think that if the High Priest kills inadvertently, he does not go into exile since accidental killers return from their exile upon the death of the High Priest, and he himself cannot thus benefit. Therefore, the rule says that he is judged nevertheless.<br />
<br />
Art: Parade on the Field of Mars - Grigori Grigorevich Chernetsov
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/19.txt
<a id="src-00048"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/19.txt`

Sanhedrin 19 – The King
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi8A5WjSMoOBNjUmiIOTs0uysOr4rTXqTYHuKS0fpiPUZ0-HY7yrXhwn7LARYE5oPUQ1JQ41F6kxRppJfa47v0QYv3y8aDDwVxB6GRaN21vTyMHmPOA5US-NRxeHUl9ZY3w45Cmp5SmlRs/s1600-h/El+Greco+-+St+Louis,+King+of+France.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi8A5WjSMoOBNjUmiIOTs0uysOr4rTXqTYHuKS0fpiPUZ0-HY7yrXhwn7LARYE5oPUQ1JQ41F6kxRppJfa47v0QYv3y8aDDwVxB6GRaN21vTyMHmPOA5US-NRxeHUl9ZY3w45Cmp5SmlRs/s320/El+Greco+-+St+Louis,+King+of+France.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A king may neither judge nor be judged. This applies to later kings, but kings of the Davidic line may judge and, therefore, be judged; as Resh Lakish explained, "First correct yourself, and then correct others"— only a person subject to correction may correct others.<br />
<br />
But why may the other kings not judge or be judged? Because of an incident that once occurred. A slave of King Yannai killed a person, and Shimon ben Shetach called King Yannai to court - because "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-29.htm">its owner had been warned by witnesses</a>" that the king, the owner of the slave, had to be in court. Yannai came and sat down. Shimon ben Shetach told him to stand up, but the king said, "I will do as your colleagues will say." All the members of the Sanhedrin were looking into the ground. Shimon ben Shetach said, "You are men of deep thought! May the Master of thoughts exact retribution from you!" -" and they died. The Sages then decreed that a king may neither judge nor be judged.<br />
<br />
Art: St Louis, King of France by El Greco
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/2.txt
<a id="src-00049"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/2.txt`

Sanhedrin 2 – Monetary Cases are Judged by Courts of Three (Criminal)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjet-pEeSiQAMaY8hhEaD5IyTuxugGsNygaraR5kcNXs2gR1cB5i56VmRo_rPIPx98DoGG09xBmeZpFCwhc8RdcRZFM0e1hIOZAm3JYIzdUtLylvDUC77eRCzew2X5nPt8Y2j5W67WBTOs/s1600-h/Anthony+Van+Dyck+-+Charles+I+in+three+positions.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjet-pEeSiQAMaY8hhEaD5IyTuxugGsNygaraR5kcNXs2gR1cB5i56VmRo_rPIPx98DoGG09xBmeZpFCwhc8RdcRZFM0e1hIOZAm3JYIzdUtLylvDUC77eRCzew2X5nPt8Y2j5W67WBTOs/s320/Anthony+Van+Dyck+-+Charles+I+in+three+positions.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Monetary cases cover most areas of civil dispute. Such cases are judged by the courts of three qualified judges. Judges act based on the testimony given by two qualified witnesses. There is no concept of a jury and, in general, no concept of circumstantial evidence.<br />
<br />
Cases of robbery and bodily injury are also monetary cases, adjudicated by courts of three qualified judges. Qualified in this context means that besides knowing relevant Torah law and scientific discovery, they must also possess "semicha," an uninterrupted chain of ordination going back to Moses.<br />
<br />
However, loan cases can be adjudicated even by judges without semicha. This was an additional enactment made to " not close doors for the would-be borrowers" so lenders would find it easy to resolve loan questions and wouldn't always require ordained judges in loan disputes.<br />
<br />
Art: Charles I in Three Positions by Anthony Van Dyck
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/20.txt
<a id="src-00050"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/20.txt`

Sanhedrin 20 – Privileges of a King
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj49UUP78s898UwM-RM_MyU-zpVPww956HjOAsbecBxAYrDLoMwTmnrkHAHXP-uWdupc0vxsx1RoaG8_v0KVTv-ErVyIEYOVcNK-4ycf5EvC5zpL_N6BKYi9aKSH4JfASVoLsHtHtI624k/s1600-h/Felix+Edouard+Vallotton+-+Sleeping+Woman.php" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj49UUP78s898UwM-RM_MyU-zpVPww956HjOAsbecBxAYrDLoMwTmnrkHAHXP-uWdupc0vxsx1RoaG8_v0KVTv-ErVyIEYOVcNK-4ycf5EvC5zpL_N6BKYi9aKSH4JfASVoLsHtHtI624k/s320/Felix+Edouard+Vallotton+-+Sleeping+Woman.php" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The triumph of self-control of Joseph was modest compared to that of Boaz, for “<a href="http://bible.cc/ruth/3-8.htm">In the middle of the night Boaz was startled, he turned (vayalfet), and there was Ruth lying at this feet</a>." The word 'turned (vayalfet)" tells that his flesh became as hard as the head of a turnip (lefet). Palti ben Layish was even more remarkable, for he never touched Michal, whom Shaul had given him as a wife.&nbsp;<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">Why, then, did he&nbsp;<a href="#" target="_blank">cry when returning her to David</a>?</span>&nbsp;Because of the loss of the opportunity to exercise willpower.<br />
<br />The king does not join the funeral procession when his close relative dies. When they feed him the mourner's meal, all the people recline on the floor, and the king sits on a chair of distinction. He may lead his army to fight a discretionary war with the consent of the Sanhedrin. He may break the fences to make a path for himself.<br />
<br />
Art: Sleeping Woman by Felix Edouard Vallotton<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/21.txt
<a id="src-00051"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/21.txt`

Sanhedrin 21 – Laws of the King
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEje9NmqLbsE6ga4HVn64t4QXEv_pvtI03VYYO_aYZdq5sU2aQBqI-ZXSTomFn0b97ghSaPMd8Uw08cgI2-lvQ5yK7WthV-zwhR4tjijPDQVrWXT1uIG_lKNrO89LqN88jjQCwvB9NZ1Dv0/s1600-h/Juan+Gimenez+y+Martin+-+The+Harem.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEje9NmqLbsE6ga4HVn64t4QXEv_pvtI03VYYO_aYZdq5sU2aQBqI-ZXSTomFn0b97ghSaPMd8Uw08cgI2-lvQ5yK7WthV-zwhR4tjijPDQVrWXT1uIG_lKNrO89LqN88jjQCwvB9NZ1Dv0/s320/Juan+Gimenez+y+Martin+-+The+Harem.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">"<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-17.htm">He (king) shall not multiply wives</a>" - only up to eighteen - "... <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-17.htm">so that his heart is not turned away</a>." Rabbi Yehudah says, "He may multiply wives beyond eighteen, provided that they do not turn his heart away from God." Rabbi Shimon says, "Even if one can turn his heart away, he may not marry her."<br />
<br />
The king may, however, have concubines. Tamar was David's daughter from a beautiful concubine captured in war. Amnon violated her and "<a href="http://bible.cc/2_samuel/13-15.htm">hated her with a very great hatred</a>." Why? Because she entangled her pubic hair around&nbsp;<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/23-1.htm">his member and cut it</a>. But Jewish women were renowned for not having pubic hair!? - Tamar was different.<br />
<br />
"<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-16.htm">The king may not multiply horses</a>..." - only enough for his chariots. "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-17.htm">And silver and gold he shall not accumulate overmuch</a>" – only enough to pay his soldiers' wages.<br />
<br />
He writes a personal Torah scroll for himself and always carries it with him.<br />
<br />
Art: The Harem by Juan Gimenez y Martin<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/22.txt
<a id="src-00052"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/22.txt`

Sanhedrin 22 – One's First Wife
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEii-yOl-ENiSiTLgTHkqPjALpC-Wd8U-IOAPSj2BBVejCJyyUwrHLTYRJ-0qbLiek9dzo2zWrmhUiRk7HoKXbZN3n5-iXIEhpRQKNgO3CNz_NmZpfaxcwKnFt1bHcA5KGgkli8cZF6FeT4/s1600-h/Konrad+Witz+-+King+Solomon+and+the+Queen+of+Sheba.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEii-yOl-ENiSiTLgTHkqPjALpC-Wd8U-IOAPSj2BBVejCJyyUwrHLTYRJ-0qbLiek9dzo2zWrmhUiRk7HoKXbZN3n5-iXIEhpRQKNgO3CNz_NmZpfaxcwKnFt1bHcA5KGgkli8cZF6FeT4/s320/Konrad+Witz+-+King+Solomon+and+the+Queen+of+Sheba.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Every Jew has to write (or hire a scribe to write) a Torah scroll for himself, following "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/31-19.htm">And now, write for yourself this song</a>..." – but a king writes a second, small one, to carry around.<br />
<br />
No one may ride on the king's horse, no one may sit on his throne, and no one may use his scepter. No one may observe the king when he is getting a haircut (every day), when he is undressed, or when he is in the bathhouse, following "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-15.htm">You shall surely place upon yourself a king</a>" - the awe of the king must be upon you.<br />
<br />
Nobody but another king can marry a king's wife. Thus, Avishag, whom David never married, was permitted only to Solomon. Why did David not marry Avishag? Because for that he would have to divorce one of his eighteen wives, and divorce is harsh. Whenever anyone divorces his first wife, <a href="http://bible.cc/malachi/2-13.htm">even the Altar sheds tears on his account</a>. <br />
<br />
Art: King Solomon and the Queen of Sheba by Konrad Witz
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/23.txt
<a id="src-00053"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/23.txt`

Sanhedrin 23 – Selecting Judges for Monetary Cases
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi0F19j9SUnNtt1BLS4rg8jW96eccgZiLJXrZG_nMNcnuoRucqh0NJiR9Zmvbr0WhKrP3evk6_D0ZbTLw_ewbUTrt0D9I0HTjmE_PU1LtMQNjPuIGRoaSf8lWZc1GVTD4xOgUXpmrfgBVg/s1600-h/Gerrit+van+Honthorst+-+Old+woman+examining+a+coin.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi0F19j9SUnNtt1BLS4rg8jW96eccgZiLJXrZG_nMNcnuoRucqh0NJiR9Zmvbr0WhKrP3evk6_D0ZbTLw_ewbUTrt0D9I0HTjmE_PU1LtMQNjPuIGRoaSf8lWZc1GVTD4xOgUXpmrfgBVg/s320/Gerrit+van+Honthorst+-+Old+woman+examining+a+coin.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Monetary cases are judged by a court of three judges. This includes cases of disputed loans, theft, bodily injury, and monetary damage. <br />
<br />
If the defendant is unwilling to come to trial, any court of three can impose its authority. Moreover, if the defendant resides in a city with an established official court, he cannot choose a new court for judgment. However, if he is willing to be judged but does not agree to the suggested court because it is either too far or is not qualified, they can use the following procedure:<br />
<br />Rabbi Meir says that one litigant selects a judge, the other selects a judge, and both litigants select one more judge. However, the Sages say, "The two judges selected by the litigants select a third one." The judge chosen by each litigant will ensure that his position is clearly represented.<br />
<br />
Art: Old woman examining a coin by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Gerrit van Honthorst&nbsp;</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/24.txt
<a id="src-00054"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/24.txt`

Sanhedrin 24 – Retraction of Judge Selection
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiyDG40LUlkVrx6CpTVq67kkZcjlCl7_b6tQHrTx6AmoR3Ug3MXrUn__6Or9BEd4py4MAkqUOJqhEwVHJe8J-L2XViYDLP6vHYmrbDs7ysABNEHIceA0-qHnfOw-3foDvzJm_dbZjIkg6M/s1600-h/Pietro+Ligari+-+Portrait+of+the+Artists+Father.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiyDG40LUlkVrx6CpTVq67kkZcjlCl7_b6tQHrTx6AmoR3Ug3MXrUn__6Or9BEd4py4MAkqUOJqhEwVHJe8J-L2XViYDLP6vHYmrbDs7ysABNEHIceA0-qHnfOw-3foDvzJm_dbZjIkg6M/s320/Pietro+Ligari+-+Portrait+of+the+Artists+Father.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Relatives and those guilty of certain misdeeds are ineligible to serve as judges. However, if both litigants agree to accept their verdict, they can even preside at a trial.<br />
<br />
If a litigant declared to his opponent, "My father is acceptable to me to act as a judge," or "Your father is acceptable to me to act as a judge," or "Three cattle herders are acceptable to me to act as judges," but afterward changes his mind and wants to retract, then Rabbi Meir says that indeed he may retract. Still, the Sages say that he may not.<br />
<br />
If he wants to retract before the verdict is reached, all agree that he may. The argument is only after the verdict is reached, and the law in this case follows the Sages – that he may not retract.<br />
<br />
Art: Portrait of the Artist by Pietro Ligari
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/25.txt
<a id="src-00055"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/25.txt`

Sanhedrin 25 – Those Ineligible to be Judges or Witnesses
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgZNH-B8Xy_AQzyrC4Ul_V13SwAqiAtxVW6OWjhlnJpb43CoGj8SRg3Clndhxdedf1Y5XYeRZrLRFztMfH2wgzhdcBb8_SStTvU988XNFw4tfgt-eKfYGD_H7VIiQwwBtb8CMMnc_ACfFU/s1600-h/Michelangelo+Caravaggio+-+The+Gamblers.JPG" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgZNH-B8Xy_AQzyrC4Ul_V13SwAqiAtxVW6OWjhlnJpb43CoGj8SRg3Clndhxdedf1Y5XYeRZrLRFztMfH2wgzhdcBb8_SStTvU988XNFw4tfgt-eKfYGD_H7VIiQwwBtb8CMMnc_ACfFU/s320/Michelangelo+Caravaggio+-+The+Gamblers.JPG" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following are ineligible to be judges or witnesses: one who rolls dice (a gambler), one who lends on interest, one who bets on pigeon races, and one who does business with the produce of the seventh year. Rabbi Yehudah says, "When are the dice-players ineligible to adjudicate or testify? When they have no trade but this, but if they also have another trade, they are eligible."<br />
<br />
Those who put personal gain above the law are suspected of accepting bribes, but what is the problem with gamblers? Rabbi Yehudah supposes that if all he does is gamble, he is not knowledgeable in the law or the ways of commerce. Therefore, if he has another trade, he is eligible. The first Sage considers gambling a form of theft: his customers don't really expect to lose, so when the gambler collects his wins, he is a robber.<br />
<br />
Art: The Gamblers by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Michelangelo Caravaggio</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/26.txt
<a id="src-00056"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/26.txt`

Sanhedrin 26 – Seventh-year (Shmita) Merchants
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDou147F57LLvVHIP3EItiIcCOPLK1kXA38ZrhpjojzKGwY_WjGOhHnVtf0DG-oMztoi4eHq8Khy4VeoKVq1r0DdDppo_YjryMAOf5Ru4Jfp3JnLUcqDajce5DgeHZoxtVi9ss4MclOdo/s1600-h/Carl+Larsson+-+Plowing.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDou147F57LLvVHIP3EItiIcCOPLK1kXA38ZrhpjojzKGwY_WjGOhHnVtf0DG-oMztoi4eHq8Khy4VeoKVq1r0DdDppo_YjryMAOf5Ru4Jfp3JnLUcqDajce5DgeHZoxtVi9ss4MclOdo/s320/Carl+Larsson+-+Plowing.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One is allowed to gather produce from the seventh year (Shmita) but not trade in it. Initially, both </span><span style="font-size: medium;">Shmita </span><span style="font-size: medium;">gatherers and traders were disqualified from serving as witnesses. However, when the ruling power began to collect tax in the seventh year, Rabbi Yannai allowed to plant on Shmita, since Shmita today is only a decree of the Sages. After this,s only merchants remained disqualified.<br />
<br />
Once, during Shmita Resh, Lakish joined Rabbi Chiya and Rabbi Shimon to observe the procedure for calculating a leap year. He saw a man plowing and said, "This man is a Kohen, and he is plowing." (Kohanim were especially suspect.) They answered, "He might say that he is just a worker." He then saw a man pruning and said, "Kohen is pruning." They answered, "He may say that he needs the branches."<br />
<br />
They said, "This fellow is argumentative." When they reached the meeting place, they ascended and pulled the ladder up to prevent him from joining.<br />
<br />
Art: Plowing by Carl Larsson
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/27.txt
<a id="src-00057"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/27.txt`

Sanhedrin 27 – Disqualified Witness
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBSGQ7JqM6mKMzBLpL__UK8UK6bJl3y4Ayyx_STIyTZC6Of2jl9dpTvQtSCmAt5rlO25Ml2oVMHVuVjMtDN61BzXf4DueHnWztdoOnKmmokga4Lb-PsTHncRvyZ3NtP6XlRdk6cd78ONk/s1600-h/Thomas+Sully+-+Gossip.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBSGQ7JqM6mKMzBLpL__UK8UK6bJl3y4Ayyx_STIyTZC6Of2jl9dpTvQtSCmAt5rlO25Ml2oVMHVuVjMtDN61BzXf4DueHnWztdoOnKmmokga4Lb-PsTHncRvyZ3NtP6XlRdk6cd78ONk/s320/Thomas+Sully+-+Gossip.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">Witnesses can be refuted and become false witnesses in the following way: a second set of witnesses comes and testifies that the first witnesses could not have possibly seen the incident to which they testified, since they were with them (the second set) in a different place at that very time. Refuted false witnesses get the same punishment as what they wanted to inflict on the one about whom they testified.<br />
<br />
If witnesses testified in January but were later exposed as false witnesses in July, then what happens to their unrelated testimony given in March?&nbsp;Abaye says that they are disqualified retroactively since <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/23-1.htm">they are evildoers</a>. Rava says that the law of false witnesses is such a novelty that it cannot be analyzed logically; they are false only from now on, and their March testimony is unaffected.<br />
<br />
This is the "A" in the six cases abbreviated <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/05/bava-metzia-21-lost-objects-that-finder.html">Y</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">A</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/04/eruvin-15-abaye-wins.html">L</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-51-should-betrothal-allow.html">K</a> G <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">M</a>, where the law follows Abaye against Rava.<br />
<br />
If a witness eats non-kosher meat because it is cheaper, he cannot testify because he can be bribed. What if he eats it to make a point? Abaye says that he is an evildoer, thus, disqualified. Rava says that for disqualification, he needs to be an evildoer in money matters, not ritual.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span>
<span style="font-size: medium;">This is the "M" in the six cases abbreviated&nbsp;</span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/05/bava-metzia-21-lost-objects-that-finder.html" style="font-size: large;">Y</a><span style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;</span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html" style="font-size: large;">A</a><span style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;</span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/04/eruvin-15-abaye-wins.html" style="font-size: large;">L</a><span style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;</span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-51-should-betrothal-allow.html" style="font-size: large;">K</a><span style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;G&nbsp;</span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html" style="font-size: large;">M</a>,<span style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;where the law follows Abaye against Rava.</span><span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
<br />
Art: Gossip by Thomas Sully</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/28.txt
<a id="src-00058"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/28.txt`

Sanhedrin 28 – Relatives Disqualified as Judges or Witnesses
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVZAcarF6tgAmLDYv82eoY2PNgdaQdWAigVW3v6IGgp3qVSsYEXSj-YB80HFoUlSv_0vm5hFllEdtCeM44joObIB4OvETQHtcUITY2McOMFY1-GZl4amrm4f0Wm0Oet9h1xIpgFj6A96w/s1600-h/Isaac+Oliver+-+The+Browne+Brothers.JPG" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVZAcarF6tgAmLDYv82eoY2PNgdaQdWAigVW3v6IGgp3qVSsYEXSj-YB80HFoUlSv_0vm5hFllEdtCeM44joObIB4OvETQHtcUITY2McOMFY1-GZl4amrm4f0Wm0Oet9h1xIpgFj6A96w/s320/Isaac+Oliver+-+The+Browne+Brothers.JPG" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Relatives are disqualified absolutely: They may not testify whether their testimony is favorable or detrimental. Relatives include one's brother, uncle, sister's husband, aunt's husband, father-in-law, brother-in-law, and sons and sons-in-law.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehudah says, "One's close friend and one's enemy are also disqualified." However, the Sages say that Jewish people are not suspected of bearing false witness about someone because of love or animosity.<br />
<br />
How does one understand "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/24-16.htm">Fathers shall not be put to death because of their sons nor shall sons be put to death because of their fathers</a>..."? We already know that "...<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/24-16.htm">each man shall be put to death only because of his own sin</a>." Therefore, we have to understand that "Fathers shall not be put to death because of the testimony of their sons."<br />
<br />
Art: The Browne Brothers by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Isaac Oliver</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/29.txt
<a id="src-00059"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/29.txt`

Sanhedrin 29 – Courtroom Proceedings and Hearsay
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhPyF9O0U1eZUtoHntu2yfNpZnpB3EOIMPvlSHH2YKkxogTn3x52f0_DB7pmydf3hPaODe6esGMlRTArASQrQWwVsei8whJGtCAQUGK6ghy47TBLCRnpZq6kvWB1TlTdTupbbMxpgQnH0Q/s1600-h/Nikolaj+Alekseevich+Kasatkin+-+%2522In+the+Corridor+of+the+District+Court%2522.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhPyF9O0U1eZUtoHntu2yfNpZnpB3EOIMPvlSHH2YKkxogTn3x52f0_DB7pmydf3hPaODe6esGMlRTArASQrQWwVsei8whJGtCAQUGK6ghy47TBLCRnpZq6kvWB1TlTdTupbbMxpgQnH0Q/s320/Nikolaj+Alekseevich+Kasatkin+-+%2522In+the+Corridor+of+the+District+Court%2522.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">They bring the witnesses into the courtroom and intimidate them against testifying falsely, telling them that perjurious witnesses are contemptible even in the eyes of those who hire them. Then they send out everyone but the most prominent witness and the litigants and ask, "Tell us how do you know that this one owes money to that one." <br />
<br />
If he says, "He told me, 'I owe him,'" or says, "So-and-so told me that he owes him," - it is as if he said nothing. Only direct observations are admissible, such as a loan taking place, whereas his statements constitute hearsay. However, it is acceptable if he says that the defendant appointed them as witnesses and then admitted his debt to the plaintiff. Then, they bring in the second witness. The testimonies should correspond.<br />
<br />
The ruling of the majority of judges is accepted, but if one says, "I don't know," they add two more judges at a time. After the verdict is announced, the judges cannot reveal individual opinions because "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/19-16.htm">Do not be a gossipmonger</a>..." <br />
<br />
Art: In the Corridor of the District Court by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Nikolaj Alekseevich Kasatkin</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/3.txt
<a id="src-00060"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/3.txt`

Sanhedrin 3 – Dissenting Views on the Number of Judges
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEic4rp28NniY8xIP4H4pX9GhUsfc49lgY3hsAs06S_wQiuXK75xFo3rwafVcro-PgRsYqDFdOsksUHNsWYAd5mnrkZcBB9t37sDIeLOmsFYtZnzY7Oew2Wnyl6JItf4QNa91KlwXMeSiOg/s1600-h/Barthel+Bruyn+-+Portrait+of+a+Man+with+Three+Sons.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEic4rp28NniY8xIP4H4pX9GhUsfc49lgY3hsAs06S_wQiuXK75xFo3rwafVcro-PgRsYqDFdOsksUHNsWYAd5mnrkZcBB9t37sDIeLOmsFYtZnzY7Oew2Wnyl6JItf4QNa91KlwXMeSiOg/s320/Barthel+Bruyn+-+Portrait+of+a+Man+with+Three+Sons.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Acha says  that according to Biblical law, one judge is qualified to adjudicate loan cases because "...<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/19-15.htm">with justice shall thou judge your fellow</a>” is expressed in the singular form "thou." However, because of the concern that a solitary judge might be chosen from commoners who are not knowledgeable in monetary law, the Sages decreed that three judges are necessary even in loan cases. <br />
<br />
But could three judges not be all commoners, not knowledgeable in monetary law? - No, at least one of them will have picked some knowledge. If so, they should not be liable for errors, like professional judges? If they were exempt, there would be even more ignorant corner dwellers.<br />
<br /><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">In the verse "...<a href="#" target="_blank">the master of the house shall approach a judge</a>..." the word "judge: is mentioned three times, so three judges are needed.</span>&nbsp;However, Rebbi says that five judges are required to start, so that at least three reach the same conclusion.<br />
<br />
Art: Portrait of a Man with Three Sons by Barthel Bruyn</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/30.txt
<a id="src-00061"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/30.txt`

Sanhedrin 30 – Are Court Proceedings Public?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjOFHn64mgLpbX04nNknCioSvCb8FMcimYHs8OkyJjjQHGficzcTrbCOJP2gZR-PAEG-d-0GOlD_FldMQnfKEO8FDaX97TbYBkOY1kryCRFOOM0I_31BfAgcvLPjUVQXDK3zmUXKYsPBX0/s1600-h/Louis+Grosclaude-+The+Three+Gossips.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjOFHn64mgLpbX04nNknCioSvCb8FMcimYHs8OkyJjjQHGficzcTrbCOJP2gZR-PAEG-d-0GOlD_FldMQnfKEO8FDaX97TbYBkOY1kryCRFOOM0I_31BfAgcvLPjUVQXDK3zmUXKYsPBX0/s320/Louis+Grosclaude-+The+Three+Gossips.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Ordinarily,  <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-29-courtroom-proceedings-and.html">the verdict is handed down orally</a>.  However, the losing litigant is entitled to a written verdict record. Rabbi Yochanan says that the verdict reads, "He is not liable," and individual opinions of the judges are not recorded because of "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/19-16.htm">Do not be a gossipmonger</a>..." Resh Lakish holds that the names of the judges are recorded with their opinions of "liable" or "not liable" because otherwise, the verdict appears to be a lie. Rabbi Elazar finds a compromise: "Through their words, so-and-so was found not liable," implying that the verdict was not unanimous.<br />
<br />
The testimonies of the two witnesses are not combined unless they witness the event together. Rabbi Yehoshua ben Korchah says that even if they witness two separate events that occur one after another, their testimonies may be combined. The first teacher maintains that one testimony's maneh (100 shekels) is not the maneh of the other. But Rabbi Yehoshua ben Korchah says that they testify about a maneh in general.<br />
<br />
Art: The Three Gossips by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Louis Grosclaude</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/31.txt
<a id="src-00062"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/31.txt`

Sanhedrin 31 – Limitations on Submitting Evidence
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj3tlBMBDMAcue_cczLlZcRRTddt0DYGrUSfd53kcA6kzcb_KJJiP0YRcTKWRXIohLCb8QMsomkRw_RLPrUVBJQv_nbHB-PA2vduBY7TI4XsND8ocih31Ksiet2u1oAagdGers8147p5lg/s1600-h/Jan+Cornelisz+Vermeyen+-+Portrait+of+Judge+John+More.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj3tlBMBDMAcue_cczLlZcRRTddt0DYGrUSfd53kcA6kzcb_KJJiP0YRcTKWRXIohLCb8QMsomkRw_RLPrUVBJQv_nbHB-PA2vduBY7TI4XsND8ocih31Ksiet2u1oAagdGers8147p5lg/s320/Jan+Cornelisz+Vermeyen+-+Portrait+of+Judge+John+More.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There is no statute of limitations on the submission of evidence. Even after the verdict has been issued, a litigant can nullify the verdict when he brings evidence to support his claim.<br />
<br />
If the judges found it necessary to impose a time limit and told the litigant, after issuing a verdict against him, "All evidence that you may have to support your claim, you must produce within the next thirty days," then the rule is: if the litigant finds evidence within thirty days, he can nullify the verdict, but if he finds it after thirty days, he cannot nullify the verdict.<br />
<br />
Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel says, "What should this person do? Rather, he may present the evidence even after thirty days." The law follows Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel.<br />
<br />
If a litigant saw that he was about to be found liable and then produced witnesses, he is not believed because it is a desperate attempt to win the case.<br />
<br />
Art: Portrait of Judge John More by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jan Cornelisz Vermeyen</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/32.txt
<a id="src-00063"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/32.txt`

Sanhedrin 32 – Inquiry and Questioning in Monetary and Capital Cases
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgAB1rYfnohJdwQnf6f9Tu5I-xM_6CSIkX7OXL1rWZhQVnXL6SYLfmBq0rG4Vq2fLLw-MqRTtMqWk8NocqG_M3hg7XlFpY7p4Pw77gLzLDmNAFBcZCN9i5XOjiuwSAb-ky-f9vuftYYXIA/s1600-h/Fritz+Sonderland+-+Ver+Den+Richter+%28The+Judge%29.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgAB1rYfnohJdwQnf6f9Tu5I-xM_6CSIkX7OXL1rWZhQVnXL6SYLfmBq0rG4Vq2fLLw-MqRTtMqWk8NocqG_M3hg7XlFpY7p4Pw77gLzLDmNAFBcZCN9i5XOjiuwSAb-ky-f9vuftYYXIA/s320/Fritz+Sonderland+-+Ver+Den+Richter+%28The+Judge%29.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Both monetary and capital cases are subject to the requirement of inquiry and questioning. Inquiry refers to time and place, questioning to the particulars of the testimony. That the court proceedings should be uniform is required by "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/24-22.htm">There shall be one law for you</a>."<br />
<br />However, in the cases of loans, the Sages waived this requirement in order to make it easier for the borrowers to obtain funds. How could the Sages abrogate a Torah law? They utilized the power that the Torah gives to the court, allowing it to confiscate property and then award it to the winner without complete interrogation. If the court sees a possibility of fraud, the questioning is required. <br />
<br />In general, one should try to take his case to the court of more prominent Sages because in doing so, he will learn additional Torah laws.<br />
<br />
Art: The Judge by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Fritz Sonderland</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/33.txt
<a id="src-00064"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/33.txt`

Sanhedrin 33 – Reversing Court Verdict
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjQ65_dnWLUNfLy7yNe3yvRghlOUlW4GH79pQn10Hk5DSq9Ot8SWiLr42BFpWp1aJzeTeufjb53RLHhyn9__ReH6q6Qrm6rNUAd81b-MIpJOLcrkwvfamVjOqq-akYlDzrK9L-HyDjkS78/s1600-h/Gabriel-Germain+Joncherie+-+Cashier+Counter+with+coins.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjQ65_dnWLUNfLy7yNe3yvRghlOUlW4GH79pQn10Hk5DSq9Ot8SWiLr42BFpWp1aJzeTeufjb53RLHhyn9__ReH6q6Qrm6rNUAd81b-MIpJOLcrkwvfamVjOqq-akYlDzrK9L-HyDjkS78/s320/Gabriel-Germain+Joncherie+-+Cashier+Counter+with+coins.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In monetary cases, if the judge realizes that the verdict was in error, it may be reversed. This is true whether the verdict declared the defendant liable or not liable. However, in capital cases, a verdict handed down in favor of the accused may not be reversed. <br />
<br />
What kind of error in judgment is reversible? A clear mistake in any Mishnah or a mistake in any ruling in the Talmud is considered a mistake on the part of the judge, and his ruling based on this can be reversed. What kind of error is not reversible? A matter disagreed upon in the Mishnah, then still disagreed in the Talmud, and currently having a clear consensus of the majority of the judges. If our judge ruled against this consensus, his ruling stands and is not reversible, even though it is considered a "mistake in the weighing of opinions."<br />
<br />
Art: Cashier Counter with Coins by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Gabriel-Germain Joncherie</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/34.txt
<a id="src-00065"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/34.txt`

Sanhedrin 34 – Who Can Advance Arguments Pro and Con?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgreih_7bFqm8GxGdB7GuUEYM62k3iuLh5U6EBjeD27H-OSLWI1ANGZM8N_fTmdax4W8hTAp93Rl19PVwCp67xLCeU6jO0OjIzW_KJ4wSbPS6d02PUd13jiBljOkhz8nqRDwxVe6TfXjTg/s1600-h/Frans+Hals+-+Paulus+Berestey,+judge+at+Haarlem.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgreih_7bFqm8GxGdB7GuUEYM62k3iuLh5U6EBjeD27H-OSLWI1ANGZM8N_fTmdax4W8hTAp93Rl19PVwCp67xLCeU6jO0OjIzW_KJ4wSbPS6d02PUd13jiBljOkhz8nqRDwxVe6TfXjTg/s320/Frans+Hals+-+Paulus+Berestey,+judge+at+Haarlem.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In monetary cases, anyone can advance arguments in favor of either liability or non-liability. In capital cases, however, anyone may advance arguments for acquittal – even the students who are sitting in court to learn the law – but only the judges may advance arguments for conviction.<br />
<br />
In capital cases, one who advanced an argument for conviction may argue for acquittal, but one who advanced an argument for acquittal may not argue for conviction. He needs to keep thinking through his acquittal arguments till the end. In the final vote, however, he may decide on conviction.<br />
<br />
Multiple laws may be derived from one verse, but multiple verses may not be used by the same Sage to derive the same law. Therefore, if two Sages in court  bring the same argument citing different verses, it counts as only one vote.<br />
<br />
Art: Paulus Berestey, Judge at Haarlem by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Frans Hals</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/35.txt
<a id="src-00066"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/35.txt`

Sanhedrin 35 – Capital Cases are not Judged on Fridays
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTN7huFix_WzJEbc8TxV-mjMSvL6KJ8d95Zv1GFlRb5e5ATeC-H2Ygw0hAebFzbOSNE5oDKri04YUtwaR45tF1ZuTBtYJzucGXZrhggs8G_DVP3e2XKIXgJcejr0d1ML0bXailhcdq-3M/s1600-h/Eduard+Frankfort-+A+Theological+Debate.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTN7huFix_WzJEbc8TxV-mjMSvL6KJ8d95Zv1GFlRb5e5ATeC-H2Ygw0hAebFzbOSNE5oDKri04YUtwaR45tF1ZuTBtYJzucGXZrhggs8G_DVP3e2XKIXgJcejr0d1ML0bXailhcdq-3M/s320/Eduard+Frankfort-+A+Theological+Debate.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Monetary cases may be concluded on the same day as they have started. However, capital cases may be concluded on the same day for acquittal but only on the following day for conviction. The judges go home at night and consider the matter further, trying to find more reasons for acquittal. <br />
<br />
Because of that, capital cases may not be tried on Friday. If the verdict is for conviction, the man has to be executed on Saturday, and that is not possible. Waiting with the execution is not allowed so as not to prolong the agony. Concluding the judgment on Sunday is also not possible because the judges may forget the arguments. And even though scribes write down their arguments, they don't write down their thoughts.<br />
<br />
Art: A Theological Debate by Eduard Frankfort</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/36.txt
<a id="src-00067"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/36.txt`

Sanhedrin 36 – Description of the Sanhedrin Trying a Capital Case
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjaWJhFvDK22ag7ot8PYkOKCmde6h0M_9jh4IvknY6d5A-k5UKzzHA3sNFG77spfMKgJlqJOd08KQvjJ1mkEuW6otERyRv32VnTL8Y_WJR1-sXs6MiYCNGmINPPbZHbMZC9GHNTB6DA_og/s1600-h/+Archibald+Henning+-+The+Judge+And+Jury+Society+In+The+Cider+Cellar.aspx" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjaWJhFvDK22ag7ot8PYkOKCmde6h0M_9jh4IvknY6d5A-k5UKzzHA3sNFG77spfMKgJlqJOd08KQvjJ1mkEuW6otERyRv32VnTL8Y_WJR1-sXs6MiYCNGmINPPbZHbMZC9GHNTB6DA_og/s320/+Archibald+Henning+-+The+Judge+And+Jury+Society+In+The+Cider+Cellar.aspx" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A Sanhedrin was seated in the shape of half a circular "threshing floor,} that is, in a semicircle, so that the judges could see each other. Two judicial scribes stand before them, one to the right and one to the left, and they would record the words of those arguing for conviction and the words of those arguing for acquittal. Both scribes record all words so that if one errs, he can be corrected from the other scribe's notes.<br />
<br />
Three rows of disciples of the sages would sit before them so that if the presiding judges were deadlocked, more judges could be added from these disciples. The disciples sit in the order of eminence. If the judges needed to ordain someone, they would ordain one of the disciples from the first row. One disciple from the second row would move to the first, one from the third would move to the second, and one more person from the scholarly community would be put in the third row.<br />
<br />
Art: The Judge And Jury Society In The Cider Cellar by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Archibald Henning</span>

---

<a id="src-00068"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/37.txt`

Sanhedrin 37 – One Should Say, "The World Was Created for My Sake"
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9FiPxUZo3mutzDFxOQwFS01q4LVmO34ROP9MVanTlYpEC5P5vKiO3lLeiqJSBKqmf_qg0QVVrxXC7tqsO5JTuXw320jCpws9YbVmKQrhD97m2IwMZX-wKnxAvdBtLQ3M_Ikb1Ivafm3I/s1600-h/Edvard+Munch+-+The+Murderer+in+the+Lane.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9FiPxUZo3mutzDFxOQwFS01q4LVmO34ROP9MVanTlYpEC5P5vKiO3lLeiqJSBKqmf_qg0QVVrxXC7tqsO5JTuXw320jCpws9YbVmKQrhD97m2IwMZX-wKnxAvdBtLQ3M_Ikb1Ivafm3I/s320/Edvard+Munch+-+The+Murderer+in+the+Lane.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When witnesses would come to court to testify that someone transgressed a capital offense, they would be admonished to discourage them from testifying falsely: "Perhaps you will say your testimony based on conjecture or hearsay, or as witnesses repeating testimony from other witnesses, even though that other witness is a trustworthy person. Perhaps you do not realize we will eventually examine you with inquiries and questions. Know that capital cases are not like monetary cases: in monetary cases, a person may pay back the money he unjustly caused someone to lose and receive atonement, but in capital cases, the blood of the accused and the blood of his descendants are the witness' responsibility until eternity."<br />
<br />Therefore, the first man was created alone.&nbsp;Also, everyone should say, "For my sake, the world was created," - and he should be careful not to bring about his downfall by committing a transgression. Now, perhaps you will say, "What need have we for all this trouble?" - <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/5-1.htm">If you were a witness and saw the event, you must testify</a>.&nbsp;  And perhaps you will say, "What need have we to incur responsibility for this man's blood?" - be secure, for "<a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/11-10.htm">when the wicked perish, there is joy</a>."<br />
<br />
Art: The Murderer in the Lane by Edvard Munch
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/38.txt
<a id="src-00069"></a>

Sanhedrin 38 – Know What to Answer a Heretic
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhWgL68aml9QZvX9SBhvtQ309wd6DXnMzBi1_Eb2v6z1VWUi_G4mKb9daKM3K9j6fY0FI-jSCWxp9LSk9RQDYAUEJVKm6NRjlMAEH19Q7VdjoGvGoju2Xk8OybNuI_-cHNcIJyicAdH8fc/s1600-h/William+Blake+-+Elohim+Creating+Adam.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhWgL68aml9QZvX9SBhvtQ309wd6DXnMzBi1_Eb2v6z1VWUi_G4mKb9daKM3K9j6fY0FI-jSCWxp9LSk9RQDYAUEJVKm6NRjlMAEH19Q7VdjoGvGoju2Xk8OybNuI_-cHNcIJyicAdH8fc/s320/William+Blake+-+Elohim+Creating+Adam.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Said Rabbi Eliezer: "Be diligent in the study of Torah and know what to answer a heretic," so that you can answer the challenges based on Scripture. Said Rabbi Yochanan, "That is only concerning a pagan heretic, but as for a Jewish heretic, do not debate him, for he will become even more heretical."<br />
<br />
Continued Rabbi Yochanan, "Wherever the heretics have used a verse in Scripture as support for their arguments, the rebuttal can be found in a nearby verse." For example, it says, "<a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/1-26.htm">Let us (plural) make man in our (plural) image</a>..." But the next verse says, "<a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/1-27.htm">God created man in His image</a>." Then why is the plural form used at all? To show that The Holy One, Blessed is He, never does anything unless He first consults with the Heavenly Court.<br />
<br />
Art: Elohim Creating Adam by William Blake</span>

---
