Sanhedrin 39 – Questions about Torah and Jews
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9qrT-vGWsjeLYspqYfzu7xvOoGmqo7VOiFXgUo4GzyLIM8FH_4qyHnHArNFmFimLEKU_rS7XuW148G_5Qw2TLDtKLICY3pjHZD9J6NcMw9SslOi7O2JajvlbZDu8ir-lg_96s20oeRd8/s1600-h/Peter+Paul+Rubens+-+Daniel+in+the+Lion%27s+Den.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9qrT-vGWsjeLYspqYfzu7xvOoGmqo7VOiFXgUo4GzyLIM8FH_4qyHnHArNFmFimLEKU_rS7XuW148G_5Qw2TLDtKLICY3pjHZD9J6NcMw9SslOi7O2JajvlbZDu8ir-lg_96s20oeRd8/s320/Peter+Paul+Rubens+-+Daniel+in+the+Lion%27s+Den.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Caesar told Rabbi Tanchum, "Come, let us become one nation." Rabbi Tanchum replied, "Fine! However, we who are circumcised cannot become like you. You, therefore, circumcise yourself and become like us." Caesar said, "You argued well. But whoever bests the king must be thrown into the pen of wild beasts." They threw Rabbi Tanchum into the pen, but the beasts did not eat him. A certain Sadducee said to Caesar, "The reason the beasts did not eat him is that they are not hungry." They threw the Sadducee to the beasts, and they ate him.<br />
<br />
A heretic said to Rabbi Avina: "<a href="http://bible.cc/2_samuel/7-23.htm">Who is like Your people, Israel, one nation in the land...</a>?" But what is unique about them? "<a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/40-17.htm">All the nations are like nothing before Him</a>"&nbsp;- and you are included!&nbsp;<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">Rabbi Avina answered, "Your prophet, Bilaam, has testified about us...<a href="#" target="_blank">And among nations, you are not counted</a>."</span><br />
<br />
Art: Daniel in the Lion's Den by Peter Paul Rubens</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/4.txt
<a id="src-00071"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/4.txt`

Sanhedrin 4 – Written or Pronounced Torah Words
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6NSLrXD9h-u7z_qxpDsaYZ-rFaOvGqiLWMZG5hbUrLtBuZRYnschAzYC8iOSsm-vtkAlpu3FCZAKEoxp7f1CNyxvOzRQX00qbT0ZzrfPaXnVVMwWX8ob_rllDVwpT21Eovfj-7tx5UsI/s1600-h/Jean+Changenet+-+Three+Prophets.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6NSLrXD9h-u7z_qxpDsaYZ-rFaOvGqiLWMZG5hbUrLtBuZRYnschAzYC8iOSsm-vtkAlpu3FCZAKEoxp7f1CNyxvOzRQX00qbT0ZzrfPaXnVVMwWX8ob_rllDVwpT21Eovfj-7tx5UsI/s320/Jean+Changenet+-+Three+Prophets.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Yehudah the Prince requires five judges because in "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-9.htm">whomever the judges condemn</a>...” the word “condemn” ירשיען is plural, which means two judges. Two more judges are mentioned below, and since the court needs an odd number of judges to rule by majority, the total is five.<br />
<br />
The Sages, however, say that since the word "condemn" ירשיען is written defectively, without the usual letter vav ירשיעון that one would expect for plural, it means one judge. Therefore, their count is three judges.<br />
<br />
The basic argument here is whether the pronounced form of the word (Rabbi Yehudah) or its written form (Sages) is more important. Other arguments hinging on the same "written or pronounced" premise include the number of blood applications of a sacrifice needed for atonement, the number of walls in a sukkah, and the amount of blood from two corpses that creates ritual impurity.<br />
<br />
Art: Three Prophets by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jean Changenet</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/40.txt
<a id="src-00072"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/40.txt`

Sanhedrin 40 – Examination of Witnesses in Capital Cases
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUoIlA9SMNn2G7cBaQ2FodV4c-GlqqZ66pfJV-wYvUDBRRzYLHbA7djKsA0KozMuJSZt3HsmGoevvD0s6j-wlg-GRkZFDoPar6FwxJV8gu3Ab04lLtUIdRkl8rYMsZNU9VbrxfFLie-ng/s1600/Lorenzo+Lotto+-+St.+Lucy+Before+the+Judge.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUoIlA9SMNn2G7cBaQ2FodV4c-GlqqZ66pfJV-wYvUDBRRzYLHbA7djKsA0KozMuJSZt3HsmGoevvD0s6j-wlg-GRkZFDoPar6FwxJV8gu3Ab04lLtUIdRkl8rYMsZNU9VbrxfFLie-ng/s320/Lorenzo+Lotto+-+St.+Lucy+Before+the+Judge.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">They would examine the witnesses with seven questions related to the time and place of the incident: which seven-year period did you see the crime, which year, which month, which day of the month, which day of the week, which hour, and in which place. The primary purpose of these questions is to pinpoint the time and place and allow the possibility of making them <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">disqualified (false) witnesses</a>. In fact, if there is no possibility for the witnesses to be disqualified, their testimony is not accepted.<br />
<br />
Then they would ask specific questions: "Did you recognize the victim?” and “Did you warn the accused?” In cases of idol worship, they asked, “What idol did he worship, and how did he worship it?” Whoever increases the number of supplementary questions is praiseworthy. It once happened that Ben Zakkai examined the witnesses concerning the stems of the figs on the fig tree under which the murder allegedly occurred.<br />
<br />
Art: St. Lucy Before the Judge by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Lorenzo Lotto</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/41.txt
<a id="src-00073"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/41.txt`

Sanhedrin 41 – Warning Given to the Murderer
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjuEjbYh_Jnh90KBJHP5fSnCeOZz5Ow9_A7HihqFOdVOG87P3sJuPhOvziKzRLjGcg1FfknNgp0MXh5rNsSipxANHHDr6q4YWBftiPuXeAK_9tQ2v_0nj27acjm-U326IfGbGflzu9sEmc/s1600/Edouard+Manet+-+The+Execution+of+the+Emperor+Maximilian.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjuEjbYh_Jnh90KBJHP5fSnCeOZz5Ow9_A7HihqFOdVOG87P3sJuPhOvziKzRLjGcg1FfknNgp0MXh5rNsSipxANHHDr6q4YWBftiPuXeAK_9tQ2v_0nj27acjm-U326IfGbGflzu9sEmc/s320/Edouard+Manet+-+The+Execution+of+the+Emperor+Maximilian.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The judges asked the witnesses specific questions about the murder: "Did you recognize the victim?" "Did you warn the murderer?" - The witnesses are asked if the accused acknowledged in their presence that he was forbidden to do the action he was performing.<br />
<br />
"Did he accept the warning upon himself?" - The offender must be apprised  of the particular form of execution he will suffer if he commits the prohibited act. Furthermore, he is not executed unless he declares that he plans to do the action, even though he knows that doing so will result in his execution.<br />
<br />
"Did he kill within as much time as needed to say a greeting of peace to one's teacher?" - If he commits the offense after this period has elapsed, he avoids punishment since, perhaps in the interim, he has forgotten the warning.<br />
<br />
Art: The Execution of the Emperor Maximilian by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Edouard Manet</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/42.txt
<a id="src-00074"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/42.txt`

Sanhedrin 42 – Once A Verdict Has Been Reached
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggQXkNjPe4WuJi7GxAeXbxphaIBfzrXbUgjbMxN1sBzki13U0ZXbh2a4LA3agNnWtTv9rYjOIOWarn409MeN-zlpZQsoQZV5nwxineW46v2Suo3GP6Yww8AIYx51c73Fj2wZVzbQS8Qgc/s1600/Edouard+Manet+-+Rue+Mosnier+with+Flags.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggQXkNjPe4WuJi7GxAeXbxphaIBfzrXbUgjbMxN1sBzki13U0ZXbh2a4LA3agNnWtTv9rYjOIOWarn409MeN-zlpZQsoQZV5nwxineW46v2Suo3GP6Yww8AIYx51c73Fj2wZVzbQS8Qgc/s320/Edouard+Manet+-+Rue+Mosnier+with+Flags.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Once a verdict has been reached and the defendant is pronounced guilty, they take him out to stone him. The stoning place was located outside the courthouse. A court that sentences even one person in seven years is called a “destroyer,” and it would have been aggravated if the execution happened nearby.<br />
<br />
While the condemned is being escorted to the execution grounds, one man stands at the courthouse door with a flag in his hand, and another sits astride a horse at a distance. If someone says, “I have grounds to argue for his acquittal,” the flagman waves the flags, and the horse with its rider races to the execution party and halts it. Even if the condemned himself says, “I have grounds for my own acquittal,” they return him to the courthouse to hear his arguments, even four or five times, as long as there is substance to his words.<br />
<br />
Art: Rue Mosnier with Flags by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Edouard Manet</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/43.txt
<a id="src-00075"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/43.txt`

Sanhedrin 43 – Distance Between The Court and the Place of Execution
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiDOqhqge5fWhddPFnoVdejPOSNHi_HCGcLSUpAZmsotk94N1inPjdBEDr1sPjby5Z7PfKAgyuLOxXw7TrgvbtrNTpQg90kegvCjp2ipSQRlDiG0J1QWQykOWc_H_vSe6Ys7ZLQp_GsNLI/s1600/Eugene+Fromentin+-+Arab+Encampment+in+the+Atlas+Mountains.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiDOqhqge5fWhddPFnoVdejPOSNHi_HCGcLSUpAZmsotk94N1inPjdBEDr1sPjby5Z7PfKAgyuLOxXw7TrgvbtrNTpQg90kegvCjp2ipSQRlDiG0J1QWQykOWc_H_vSe6Ys7ZLQp_GsNLI/s320/Eugene+Fromentin+-+Arab+Encampment+in+the+Atlas+Mountains.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"> The execution must be "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/24-14.htm">outside the camp</a>," but how far outside? Should we compare it to the law of bulls brought for communal error, about which it is also stated "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/4-21.htm">outside the camp</a>," and there it means outside the farthest of the three camps, or to forbidden sacrifice "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/17-3.htm">outside the camp</a>," where "outside" means only outside one camp, the Temple proper?<br />
<br />
There are four points of commonality between execution and the law of bulls: removal, outside the camp, preparation (both prepare for something), and atonement (both atone). There are also four points of commonality with the forbidden sacrifices: they apply to a person, a sinner, a life being taken, and sacrificial disqualification does not apply.<br />
<br />
However, we should rather compare those laws that prepare for something, thus execution is compared to the law of bulls, and the place of execution is removed three camps from the courthouse.<br />
<br />
Art: Arab Encampment in the Atlas Mountains by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Eugene Fromentin</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/44.txt
<a id="src-00076"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/44.txt`

Sanhedrin 44 – Achan and Joshua
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhJOvRX8UmIfU1JyowswZ9BZ4uVnOEYU_q_Hd8cZZp5AfWwugBQvxRNf2NaX0TmaAiKkNIoDVSm8EbYzqenIgYcu8NbC5lyRGF_xrFnV4HR7MGVug4sJYK9uYfX3eRw9smX3UVM8GbkN6w/s1600/Abraham+van+der+Hecke+-+A+Philosopher+in+his+Study.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhJOvRX8UmIfU1JyowswZ9BZ4uVnOEYU_q_Hd8cZZp5AfWwugBQvxRNf2NaX0TmaAiKkNIoDVSm8EbYzqenIgYcu8NbC5lyRGF_xrFnV4HR7MGVug4sJYK9uYfX3eRw9smX3UVM8GbkN6w/s320/Abraham+van+der+Hecke+-+A+Philosopher+in+his+Study.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When Joshua inquired why Israel was defeated at the hands of Ai, God replied, "Israel has sinned" - they have taken the items from the ban. Joshua then said, "Master of the Universe, who is the individual who has sinned?" God replied, "Am I your talebearer? Go cast lots!"<br />
<br />
The lot fell on Achan. Achan, however, told Joshua, "A lot is no proof! It had to fall on somebody." "Please," begged Joshua, "acknowledge your guilt, and you will be spared. In the future, Israel is to be divided by casting lots. Please don't cast aspersions on it now." Achan confessed and was executed.<br />
<br />
Joshua then hurled the booty in front of God and told him, "Because of this transgression, the great person, Yair ben Menasheh, who is comparable to the greater part of the Sanhedrin, had to die?" God told Joshua, "Your transgression is even worse. At night, when not fighting, you should not have neglected the Torah study." The next night, Joshua corrected this.<br />
<br />
Art: A Philosopher in His Study by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Abraham van der Hecke</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/45.txt
<a id="src-00077"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/45.txt`

Sanhedrin 45 – Stoning
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2_6iBjeIaVZwgZLj-r68V4DWYIYtyRM8KDvFn0BIh120vUJ8iSECq3kkOq2Hj40h9ERXEumUYWM8R4GyqND4k9Npwbmj9HTuHjqRSmtkBlUGzK2BAM4OKjRtmjcCNOUy7zktJe1Luw0U/s1600/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Purtud,+Alpine+Scene+and+Boulders.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2_6iBjeIaVZwgZLj-r68V4DWYIYtyRM8KDvFn0BIh120vUJ8iSECq3kkOq2Hj40h9ERXEumUYWM8R4GyqND4k9Npwbmj9HTuHjqRSmtkBlUGzK2BAM4OKjRtmjcCNOUy7zktJe1Luw0U/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Purtud,+Alpine+Scene+and+Boulders.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"> When the condemned person was 4 amot (about 6 feet) from the stoning grounds, they would remove his clothing, except for a piece of material to cover his genitals, so as not to prolong his agony by the cushioning effect of the clothes. A woman remains also covered from the back – so says Rabbi Yehudah, but the Sages maintain that a woman is not stoned naked; rather, she is dressed in a single plain garment.<br />
<br />
The elevation of the stoning grounds was twice a man's height. One of the witnesses pushes the condemned man by his hips so that he falls on the side. If he dies from this fall, the court has fulfilled its obligation. If not, the second witness picks up a stone and casts it upon his chest. If he dies from this, it is sufficient; if not, all present throw rocks at him.<br />
<br />
Art: Purtud, Alpine Scene and Boulders by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">John Singer Sargent</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/46.txt
<a id="src-00078"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/46.txt`

Sanhedrin 46 – Hanging After Stoning
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgxG6N_JV5QS288Mdp53o_efG1h3u3fY2XRe5qicwECbYUNHHiFtd-CtbhLWiLzUflkXu9tl3Rx3Qj7kofif30Ti3YJC_LBL-zx7s-3WgrqtkhJCUlWE5TuLXEjWhkzmNDvREmx_pkU4Vc/s1600/Pierre+Luc+Charles+Ciceri+-+The+Gallows.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgxG6N_JV5QS288Mdp53o_efG1h3u3fY2XRe5qicwECbYUNHHiFtd-CtbhLWiLzUflkXu9tl3Rx3Qj7kofif30Ti3YJC_LBL-zx7s-3WgrqtkhJCUlWE5TuLXEjWhkzmNDvREmx_pkU4Vc/s320/Pierre+Luc+Charles+Ciceri+-+The+Gallows.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">All those who are stoned are subsequently hung – these are the words of Rabbi Eliezer, but the Sages say, "Only the blasphemer and the idolater are hung after stoning."<br />
<br />
A man is hung facing the people, and a woman is hung facing the gallows – these are the words of Rabbi Eliezer, but the Sages say, "Only a man is hung; a woman is not hung at all."<br />
<br />
How do they hang a man? They sink a post vertically into the ground, and a beam protrudes from it. The hangman brings together two hands of the corpse, one upon the other, and hangs him by his hands from the beam. Rabbi Yose says, "The post is leaned on an angle against the wall, and he hangs him in the way that butchers do""<br />
<br />
After he is hung, they untie him immediately, remove him from the gallows, and bury him.<br />
<br />
Art: The Gallows by Pierre Luc Charles Ciceri</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/47.txt
<a id="src-00079"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/47.txt`

Sanhedrin 47 – The Honor of the Dead
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXOstAMk40exKqueF9ANL8gSY_FPapLonp4qKM1NW1mfcEH8TQFcpbdbHsBp9eSxvap0uflFmIjYMbERS3YKW02QY1VhcHBz4filKv2iE19yfCtzddLW34PHdKXVopZWHysSKY9G9pHCU/s1600/Caravaggio+-+Burial+of+St.+Lucy.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXOstAMk40exKqueF9ANL8gSY_FPapLonp4qKM1NW1mfcEH8TQFcpbdbHsBp9eSxvap0uflFmIjYMbERS3YKW02QY1VhcHBz4filKv2iE19yfCtzddLW34PHdKXVopZWHysSKY9G9pHCU/s320/Caravaggio+-+Burial+of+St.+Lucy.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Is burial practiced because it avoids disgrace to the deceased and his family, or is it practiced because it gains atonement for the deceased? When would it make a difference? When one declares that after he dies, he does not wish his corpse to be buried. If burial is because of the disgrace to his family, he cannot refuse burial and thus disgrace his family. If it is because of his own atonement – he has clearly stated that he does not want atonement, and there would be no reason to bury him.<br />
<br />
The Talmud does not resolve this question, but the prevailing practice is that if one does not wish to be buried, his wishes are disregarded.<br />
<br />
Is eulogy delivered for the honor of the living, that is, the relatives who survive the deceased, or is it for the honor of the dead? Since the deceased receives atonement through various disgraces if they befall his corpse, it follows that a eulogy is for the honor of the dead person himself.<br />
<br />
Art: Burial of St. Lucy by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Caravaggio</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/48.txt
<a id="src-00080"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/48.txt`

Sanhedrin 48 – Deriving Benefit from a Corpse
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj2WTPR809nIWE9KoQLU0LU_2RxJhP_Hkyg06zkBWP1ZS_dxbFaeFX6NCzEO_YNVgigPP-I-s16taJ_SQNY-rq5ZRHpcB-aymTi_NvG6MA4P0cLw7J9VOdkRo8ctv34ccWaGCkDr8z2N-M/s1600/Howard+Pyle-+Dead+men+tell+no+tales.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj2WTPR809nIWE9KoQLU0LU_2RxJhP_Hkyg06zkBWP1ZS_dxbFaeFX6NCzEO_YNVgigPP-I-s16taJ_SQNY-rq5ZRHpcB-aymTi_NvG6MA4P0cLw7J9VOdkRo8ctv34ccWaGCkDr8z2N-M/s320/Howard+Pyle-+Dead+men+tell+no+tales.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">It is certainly forbidden to use a corpse for anything or to derive benefit from its accessory items. When does this prohibition go into effect? Abaye says that the prohibition applies from the moment the item is designated to serve the needs of the corpse, but Rava maintains that it starts from the time that item is actually used in its new capacity. <br />
<br /><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">Abaye derives his view by comparison with&nbsp;<a href="#" target="_blank">the decapitated heifer</a>: just as the heifer becomes forbidden when it is led into a rocky, uncultivated valley, so too all designated items are already viewed as if serving their purpose.</span>&nbsp;However, Rava compares this with accessories to idolatry, which do not become forbidden through mere designation. What is Rava's reason? - We should derive accessory (for the corpse) from accessory (for idol worship), and not compare to heifer, which is the item in question itself.<br />
<br />
Art: Dead Men Tell No Tales by Howard Pyle</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/49.txt
<a id="src-00081"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/49.txt`

Sanhedrin 49 – Four Methods of Execution
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgCccAc5OesJ1IOGZo_GKLgOMD398YTj_5z2WVvOrfRT8ncQePrY3HXyDCz7AW21HSqPDO3CinznU2m_T5BpnYjeXijo3ceU9tmC2xVdkhwv1aEUo8xiNKKtUaKy5rWVUbkZ_nCby_3QRg/s1600/Paul+Delaroche+-+The+Execution+Of+Lady+Jane+Grey.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgCccAc5OesJ1IOGZo_GKLgOMD398YTj_5z2WVvOrfRT8ncQePrY3HXyDCz7AW21HSqPDO3CinznU2m_T5BpnYjeXijo3ceU9tmC2xVdkhwv1aEUo8xiNKKtUaKy5rWVUbkZ_nCby_3QRg/s320/Paul+Delaroche+-+The+Execution+Of+Lady+Jane+Grey.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The court used four different methods of execution, depending on the various capital offenses that the person committed. In descending order of severity, these are stoning, burning, beheading, and strangulation. <br />
<br />
What difference does the severity of the execution make? In a situation where one has committed several capital offenses, each of which renders him liable to a different type of execution – since one cannot be executed more than once - he receives the more severe execution for which he is liable. Rabbi Shimon lists them in a different order: burning, stoning, strangulation, and beheading.<br />
<br />
Art: The Execution Of Lady Jane by Paul Delaroche -&nbsp; Grey</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/5.txt
<a id="src-00082"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/5.txt`

Sanhedrin 5 – Permission to Judge
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfF5iDSdde4rEahYcfcekrH2Se6iPwE4Aa3kikeIkfQ6WELnf0Boyd3i4Um66KBycu2C3fddkueWm0n4S7ArfD1ujLsSFxj5uF6JjjzH-AJuNzj05lyJzV75E_nE2GIMk4QuhyphenhyphenMtNnIfk/s1600-h/Jean-Louis+Laneuville+-+Portrait+of+the+politician+Bertrand+Bar%C3%A8re+de+Vieuzac.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfF5iDSdde4rEahYcfcekrH2Se6iPwE4Aa3kikeIkfQ6WELnf0Boyd3i4Um66KBycu2C3fddkueWm0n4S7ArfD1ujLsSFxj5uF6JjjzH-AJuNzj05lyJzV75E_nE2GIMk4QuhyphenhyphenMtNnIfk/s320/Jean-Louis+Laneuville+-+Portrait+of+the+politician+Bertrand+Bar%C3%A8re+de+Vieuzac.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Although three judges are required for monetary cases, if the judge is a widely recognized expert who has successfully tried many cases without error, he may adjudicate these cases even alone. If, in addition, he has received authorization to judge from a government authority (The Babylonian Exilarch in the time of the Talmud), then the judge is free from liability if he rules erroneously.<br />
<br />
It is thus understandable why one needs permission to judge monetary cases. But why does he need it when judging the cases of ritual, provided that he is knowledgeable?  Because of a story that happened when one student allowed to make ritually pure dough with egg yolk (מי ביצים, mei beitsim), and the people understood him as saying marsh water (מי בצעים, mei betsaim). After this, it was instituted that one may not render decisions before he gets permission from his teacher, who will ascertain that he has clear diction and that his rulings will be understood properly.<br />
<br />
Art: Portrait of the politician Bertrand Barère de Vieuzac by Jean-Louis Laneuville
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/50.txt
<a id="src-00083"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/50.txt`

Sanhedrin 50 – Comparisons  of Executions' Severity
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjXk3JWu3eK1P6bFxb0Vg7dagBBoMjOwKuUEbdqRnriU8OZn0ZLgAOq4yGQ7ZFjK0bGYaBhHeTb1tWJuh8_mwmrqRGTUOKhdQiTvJjdnMCzg2HxoELP0_VnFrMJl9J8RwOBEh7cl27z9IM/s1600/August+Renoir+-+The+Swing.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjXk3JWu3eK1P6bFxb0Vg7dagBBoMjOwKuUEbdqRnriU8OZn0ZLgAOq4yGQ7ZFjK0bGYaBhHeTb1tWJuh8_mwmrqRGTUOKhdQiTvJjdnMCzg2HxoELP0_VnFrMJl9J8RwOBEh7cl27z9IM/s320/August+Renoir+-+The+Swing.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Stoning is a more severe form of execution than burning, for it is administered to a blasphemer and an idol worshiper. And what is the particular strictness of their transgression? - They attack the fundamentals.<br />
<br />
Stoning is more severe than beheading, as can be derived from the law of the subverted city. If most of the residents of a town in the Land of Israel followed the instigation of evil men and worshiped idols, then the residents guilty of idolatry are beheaded, but the subverters themselves are stoned. Since the subverters' transgression is greater, stoning is more severe than beheading.<br />
<br />
Perhaps strangulation is just as severe as stoning, since it is administered to one who strikes his father or mother, and the honor of parents is compared to the honor of God? - No, stoning is more severe since it is applied to an adulterous betrothed girl, whereas for adultery with a fully married adulterous woman, one only receives strangulation.<br />
<br />
Art: The Swing by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">August Renoir&nbsp;</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/51.txt
<a id="src-00084"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/51.txt`

Sanhedrin 51 – Irrelevant Laws
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhdQqdprhD2L3iC8_zz3M9GqALHZKIDK5k8wbxUL7f65bwNspzSFcvh8cX9EloptNH7nv9OwyfzECT5jeQIOD4kylEHmwnxxCrFiViEYntPw1SSsBfui9-7lMsejGsY52cppJNrfNFI4U/s1600/Thomas+De+Keyser+-+A+Musician+and+His+Daughter.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhdQqdprhD2L3iC8_zz3M9GqALHZKIDK5k8wbxUL7f65bwNspzSFcvh8cX9EloptNH7nv9OwyfzECT5jeQIOD4kylEHmwnxxCrFiViEYntPw1SSsBfui9-7lMsejGsY52cppJNrfNFI4U/s320/Thomas+De+Keyser+-+A+Musician+and+His+Daughter.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">"<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/21-9.htm" target="_blank">If a daughter of a Kohen starts being promiscuous, her father she profanes</a>..."  Said Rabbi Eliezer in explanation of this, "With her father by burning; with her father-in-law by stoning."<br />
<br />
Suppose a daughter of a Kohen who is either betrothed or fully married commits adultery. In that case, her punishment is correspondingly more significant than that of her lover, who is punished by strangulation. But what is the meaning of Rabbi Eliezer's cryptic statement? If he meant that she commits adultery with either her father or her father-in-law, then his ruling is correct even for a daughter of Yisrael, and he did not have to state it. Instead, "with her father" means "in the domain of her father," that is, betrothed, and "with her father-in-law" means "in the domain of her father-in-law," that is, fully married.<br />
<br />
There were other explanations, but Rav Nachman said, "The law is like the first explanation." Said Rav Yosef, "The law?!? There are no capital punishments today!" Said Abaye, "Should we not learn the laws of sacrifices because they are not relevant today? We do learn them and receive a reward for learning!" And Rav Yosef meant that when the Messiah comes and resurrects the dead, we will ask Rabbi Eliezer himself.<br />
<br />
Art: A Musician and His Daughter by Thomas De Keyser</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/52.txt
<a id="src-00085"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/52.txt`

Sanhedrin 52 – Burning, Beheading
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgbFpOGMHGtOFQRJ7T96-n0dERX-D2AOvD_q4Wc5JtkcinMFicLLt6fe_lbDO0Bh7RXRrsGyyaTuR5C0P-vNKRNGYQPRTYj1svDFBvCxs5Hj2CCCuGtO7hGxxkCz1nGYtjFoNZKAdD5XXk/s1600/Edouard+Manet-+Boy+with+a+Sword.png" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgbFpOGMHGtOFQRJ7T96-n0dERX-D2AOvD_q4Wc5JtkcinMFicLLt6fe_lbDO0Bh7RXRrsGyyaTuR5C0P-vNKRNGYQPRTYj1svDFBvCxs5Hj2CCCuGtO7hGxxkCz1nGYtjFoNZKAdD5XXk/s320/Edouard+Manet-+Boy+with+a+Sword.png" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following is the procedure for those who are burned. They would place a hard scarf inside a soft one and wind it around his neck. One witness pulls toward himself, the other one pulls toward himself, until the executed opens his mouth, and then they pore molten lead inside. The lead descends into his stomach and burns his intestines.<br />
<br />
This procedure is for those who are beheaded: they would decapitate him with the sword, cutting off his head from the front. Said Rabbi Yehudah, "It is a disgrace for him since the Roman government does the same. Rather, they chop it off with an ax." Answered the Sages, "That would be even more disgraceful."<br />
<br />
But how do we know to cut off the head and not, say, stab him? - Because it says, "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/13-15.htm">by the edge of the sword</a>." Then let's cut him in half!? - Said Rab Nachman, "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/19-18.htm">And you shall love your fellow as yourself</a>," which means choosing a favorable death for him.<br />
<br />
Art: Boy with a Sword by Edouard Manet</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/53.txt
<a id="src-00086"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/53.txt`

Sanhedrin 53 – Who is Stoned
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEicWjLaqGHhk5eGoLcN18Ozj9b_qi_VTmDDSewk7RkBkQXlaneOvI7fA_7vHhDt-F0djAkNMMuTMDgeB7jfZ-tLVyj3OqjQhFRBudkWgUa_nWeKA2E_mCHt2nwSROiXtgI5fl2OsAlBw1Y/s1600/James+McNeill+Whistler-+The+Artist%27s+Mother.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEicWjLaqGHhk5eGoLcN18Ozj9b_qi_VTmDDSewk7RkBkQXlaneOvI7fA_7vHhDt-F0djAkNMMuTMDgeB7jfZ-tLVyj3OqjQhFRBudkWgUa_nWeKA2E_mCHt2nwSROiXtgI5fl2OsAlBw1Y/s320/James+McNeill+Whistler-+The+Artist%27s+Mother.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Following is the procedure for those who are strangled: they would submerge him in manure up to his knees to prevent jumping and to shorten the agony. They would place a hard scarf inside a soft one and wind it around his neck. One witness pulls toward himself, and the other witness pulls to himself until his soul departs.<br />
<br />
The following are executed by stoning: one who cohabits with his mother, or with his father's wife, or with his daughter-in-law, or with a male, or with an animal, or a woman who brings an animal upon herself, a blasphemer, one who serves idols, one who desecrates the Sabbath, one who curses his mother or father using the Name of God, one who cohabits with a betrothed young girl, a subverter of an entire city, a sorcerer, and a wayward and rebellious son.<br />
<br />
Art: The Artist's Mother by James McNeill Whistler</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/54.txt
<a id="src-00087"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/54.txt`

Sanhedrin 54 – Why is the Animal Also Stoned?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6fNac_Yb_F0Ap7Z_Q6j5lcLSpSHdmPsC_llwt-JbQ10DmImmCWzrMQnJXsqERJSV2RoUMPHSiqwmhhyphenhyphenTIZPQkfoojDdbJCETYKAWP3WUwIZV3jKZbqszw4VVmIS6Ba3s7pn-JyRQqgV0/s1600/Jacopo+BASSANO+-+Sheep+and+Lamb.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6fNac_Yb_F0Ap7Z_Q6j5lcLSpSHdmPsC_llwt-JbQ10DmImmCWzrMQnJXsqERJSV2RoUMPHSiqwmhhyphenhyphenTIZPQkfoojDdbJCETYKAWP3WUwIZV3jKZbqszw4VVmIS6Ba3s7pn-JyRQqgV0/s320/Jacopo+BASSANO+-+Sheep+and+Lamb.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The law is that <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/20-15.htm">the animal with whom bestiality was committed is also stoned</a>. What is the reason for this strange law? If the person sinned, in what way did the animal sin? - Since the downfall came upon a man through it, it is also stoned so that others should not come to sin through it as well. Another explanation is so that it should not occur that an animal passes in the street, and people say, "This is the one that caused So-and-so to be stoned."<br />
<br />
But how do we know that the punishment is indeed stoning? This is derived from the use of the same words, "You shall surely kill him," concerning this man and concerning one who instigates others to idolatry, about whom it says, "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/13-10.htm">You shall pelt him with stones</a>."<br />
<br />
Art: Sheep and Lamb by Jacopo BASSANO</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/55.txt
<a id="src-00088"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/55.txt`

Sanhedrin 55 – Self-Copulation
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhx2xDOEH1DGYZrMQFz-2XdZdVCWRQOdDozgcU2-88fjS2dnFBMYaXqdoF3iAo73aNUYUVWymlwSQOeoWmMwbXPe16q0PYAv6xeY72WJy3x-iINQbYpJGnhShiKaXXTmk_Fkva5uXc0ryk/s1600/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Young+Man+in+Reverie.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhx2xDOEH1DGYZrMQFz-2XdZdVCWRQOdDozgcU2-88fjS2dnFBMYaXqdoF3iAo73aNUYUVWymlwSQOeoWmMwbXPe16q0PYAv6xeY72WJy3x-iINQbYpJGnhShiKaXXTmk_Fkva5uXc0ryk/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Young+Man+in+Reverie.jpg" /></a></div>
Rav Achadboi bar Ami asked Rav Sheshet, "If one copulates with himself, what is the law?" In other words, if one bends his organ underneath himself until it touches his orifice, is he liable for sodomy? Rav Sheshet answered him, "You upset us with impossible questions!"<br />
<br />
In discussing this, Rav Ashi said to Ravina, "What point is in question to you?" You should be able to resolve the inquiry on your own, as follows. In a state of erection, you cannot find such a case. Therefore, you can only find such a case when the organ is limp. According to the view which says that one is not liable when he copulates with a woman forbidden to him by using a limp organ - here, too, he is not liable. On the view that one IS liable for such copulation in the case of a forbidden woman, here, too, he is obviously liable to two sin offerings: one for committing the copulative act and one for submitting to the copulative act.<br />
<br />
Art: Young Man in Reverie by John Singer Sargent

---

### content/sanhedrin/56.txt
<a id="src-00089"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/56.txt`

Sanhedrin 56 – The Blasphemer
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_FXsE9c5hlvl8taKPvi3GeGEEk1G2gtXmEtw11aGHyXGSCh-Fl5P925L64DlAWPucJSY0J72PO3nsWSLsz_APGiQylbDCx2J_EqodeI9w92lc5REcR7KCN_D5VKgZIyPolyEe-tVa6mY/s1600/Jules+Bastien-Lepage+-+The+Beggar.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_FXsE9c5hlvl8taKPvi3GeGEEk1G2gtXmEtw11aGHyXGSCh-Fl5P925L64DlAWPucJSY0J72PO3nsWSLsz_APGiQylbDCx2J_EqodeI9w92lc5REcR7KCN_D5VKgZIyPolyEe-tVa6mY/s320/Jules+Bastien-Lepage+-+The+Beggar.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The blasphemer  is one who "blesses" (that is, curses) the Divine Name of God. The act of blasphemy is always referred to in the Talmud by the euphemism "blessing." The blasphemer is not liable unless he pronounces the Divine Name, yud, keh, vav, keh. In referring to the Tetragrammaton name of God, it is accepted practice to modify the spelling and to pronounce the letter "heh" as "keh."<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehoshua ben Korchah describes the trial procedure. Whenever the judges examine the witnesses, they use a pseudonym, asking the witnesses, for example, whether the accused said, "May Yose strike Yose." However, when the case is completed, they may not execute the offender based on a pseudonym. Rather, they send everyone out of the courtroom and then ask the most eminent of the witnesses, "State explicitly what you heard the blasphemer say," and he says it. Upon hearing the blasphemy, the judges stand up and rend their garments, and never repair them. The second witness then says, "I, too, have heard as he did." There is no need for him to repeat the exact words.<br />
<br />
Art: The Beggar by Jules Bastien-Lepage</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/57.txt
<a id="src-00090"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/57.txt`

Sanhedrin 57 – The 7 Noahide Laws
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhoVb0vAqAlCHIZz_Fn7H6-fsRJt8DIzvYUcgnX5IaiQFiGx_Xkt179c5jaWUcmnw8vXma2XOptEecoET0rW2Win0CeSw9DhOVq1x6m2g4eloAWt704mOKF05Q34hZbE5-ZPAR3__3hoQU/s1600/Manfredi+de+Battilor+Bartolo+Di+Fredi+Fredi+-+Noah+Building+the+Ark.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhoVb0vAqAlCHIZz_Fn7H6-fsRJt8DIzvYUcgnX5IaiQFiGx_Xkt179c5jaWUcmnw8vXma2XOptEecoET0rW2Win0CeSw9DhOVq1x6m2g4eloAWt704mOKF05Q34hZbE5-ZPAR3__3hoQU/s320/Manfredi+de+Battilor+Bartolo+Di+Fredi+Fredi+-+Noah+Building+the+Ark.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">After Noah went out of the Ark, he was given seven laws for the following generations: civil law to enforce the other six prohibitions, prohibitions of blasphemy, idolatry, sexual transgressions, murder, theft, and eating a limb torn from a live animal. For the violation of three transgressions, a Noahide may be executed: for sexual transgressions, murder, and "blessing” the Divine Name. Some add idolatry to this list, and some say that for violation of any of the seven Noahide laws, a Noahite is executed.<br />
<br />A Noahite is executed by one judge based on the testimony of one witness, even though he violated the prohibition without having received prior warning. A man who judges or testifies can even be a relative of the accused.<br />
<br />
Art: Noah Building the Ark by Manfredi de Battilor Bartolo Di Fredi Fredi</span>

---
