Sanhedrin 58 – Noahide Marital Laws
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUJrob8H3Sxz60oGdukbmCgDb6g9witlDiHBnLmLEFc8TKJsecrcaqU4o9b5AbOUamDEx03ZQjZCmjTs83muxnwONg3H91Gs931_N8rf8zhiyJ1d6HhY7qITyoi6Mt1eKWwncPKQqnvHk/s1600/Edward+John+Gregory-+Mabel,+Daughter+of+Charles+Galloway.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUJrob8H3Sxz60oGdukbmCgDb6g9witlDiHBnLmLEFc8TKJsecrcaqU4o9b5AbOUamDEx03ZQjZCmjTs83muxnwONg3H91Gs931_N8rf8zhiyJ1d6HhY7qITyoi6Mt1eKWwncPKQqnvHk/s320/Edward+John+Gregory-+Mabel,+Daughter+of+Charles+Galloway.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Noahide marital laws are derived from the verse, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=2">Therefore shall a man leave his father and his mother and cling to his wife</a>," but not to the wife of his fellow man, not to an animal, etc.<br />
<br />
A Noahite is permitted to marry his daughter. You may ask why Adam did not marry his daughter? He did it so that Cain could marry his sister, based on "The world will be built through kindness" in Psalms. A Noahite is also permitted to marry his sister. Didn't we just say that "The world will be built through kindness" allowed Cain to marry his sister, but otherwise, it would be prohibited?! True, but once it was permitted to Cain, it remained permitted.<br />
<br />
Art: Mabel, Daughter of Charles Galloway by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Edward John Gregory</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/59.txt
<a id="src-00092"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/59.txt`

Sanhedrin 59 – Eating Meat
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhCPTQN3gvuyIA-03n-w4yh8xDcrx4njjbccW3eG4b-LfCSqERCHOS1ZOb2J6v4LFhHKekPpBqdWlAb57QAEDCExCgCADTWv8Z_FKvv0BMRy7pYSj1R2OOtivLGfaa2i8oYq_PDTlw5RM/s1600/Jean+Simeon+Chardin+-+Girl+Peeling+Vegetables.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhCPTQN3gvuyIA-03n-w4yh8xDcrx4njjbccW3eG4b-LfCSqERCHOS1ZOb2J6v4LFhHKekPpBqdWlAb57QAEDCExCgCADTWv8Z_FKvv0BMRy7pYSj1R2OOtivLGfaa2i8oYq_PDTlw5RM/s320/Jean+Simeon+Chardin+-+Girl+Peeling+Vegetables.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Resh Lakish said that an idolater who ceased work for an entire day is liable to death, as it says, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=8">Day and night they shall not cease</a>."&nbsp;This is true for any day, even Monday. <br />
<br />
Rabbi Yochanan said that an idolater who engrosses himself in Torah study is liable to death, as it says, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=33">Moses commanded us the Torah; it is an inheritance</a>..." But did not Rabbi Meir say that he is rather like a High Priest, because it says about the laws of the Torah "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=18">That a man should keep them and live by them</a>." - any man, even an idolater? - This refers to the seven Noahide laws.<br />
<br />
Adam, the first man, was commanded to subsist on vegetation, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=1">it shall be yours for food</a>." If so, why was he given dominion over animals? Only for work. For fish? Only for work. But can fish do work? - Yes, since it is prohibited to use a combination of fish and goat to pull a wagon. Why was he then expressly prohibited a limb torn from a living animal? - Adam was allowed to eat an animal that died of itself.<br />
<br />
Art: Girl Peeling Vegetables by Jean Simeon Chardin</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/6.txt
<a id="src-00093"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/6.txt`

Sanhedrin 6 – Settle or Go To Court?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgzK6_jAby7wGDfOIT4SS1TViUq8taQxyZ8DgaYu5BojNa-v4mpIAlghliGnmpiiEe56uj4mMbOp2_wA59wyw5go-Jlcspl-9qeQtd9GLPC0nt54T3dnh_FT5nsz44ODZ3EDY1ir9clS4U/s1600-h/Louis+Katzenstein+-+Anthony+van+Dyck+at+the+Court+of+Charles+I.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgzK6_jAby7wGDfOIT4SS1TViUq8taQxyZ8DgaYu5BojNa-v4mpIAlghliGnmpiiEe56uj4mMbOp2_wA59wyw5go-Jlcspl-9qeQtd9GLPC0nt54T3dnh_FT5nsz44ODZ3EDY1ir9clS4U/s320/Louis+Katzenstein+-+Anthony+van+Dyck+at+the+Court+of+Charles+I.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Eliezer ben R. Yossi says, "It is forbidden for a judge to arbitrate a compromise." It is certainly permissible for disputants to settle out of court or to ask an arbitrator to help them. However, once they come to court, the judge who arbitrates a compromise shows that, in his opinion, the compromise settlement is more correct than an appropriate ruling based on Torah law. Furthermore, in settlement, the would-be winner is robbed of some money.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehoshua ben Korcha </span><span style="font-size: medium;">says</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> on the contrary that before the verdict, it is a meritorious deed for a judge to arbitrate a compromise - "...<a href="http://bible.cc/zechariah/8-16.htm">execute truth and judgment of peace</a>...", and "judgment of peace" means compromise - like King David, who "...<a href="http://bible.cc/2_samuel/8-15.htm">rendered judgment and righteousness</a>..." Rabbi Eliezer explains that King David would render a strict judgment first, but then, if the losing party was poor, he would pay his own money.<br />
<br />
Art: Anthony van Dyck at the Court of Charles I by&nbsp;&nbsp;Louis Katzenstein
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/60.txt
<a id="src-00094"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/60.txt`

Sanhedrin 60 – Idol Worship Liability
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhxOHVFv_6-VcyQ77dUFApTKt_p2Ey2R3vDVHQmnhPulrZNjlId4GzRLa-JP2G871RFgP57j6wP5tStjVeW88k6s7YOSSLmXLs4jIx7H8Eoue3coiKFkRfxnk5LGElBSMrmItgXYSLOq14/s1600/Maria+Hadfield+Cosway+-+Persian+Lady+Worshipping+the+Rising+Sun.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhxOHVFv_6-VcyQ77dUFApTKt_p2Ey2R3vDVHQmnhPulrZNjlId4GzRLa-JP2G871RFgP57j6wP5tStjVeW88k6s7YOSSLmXLs4jIx7H8Eoue3coiKFkRfxnk5LGElBSMrmItgXYSLOq14/s320/Maria+Hadfield+Cosway+-+Persian+Lady+Worshipping+the+Rising+Sun.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One is liable for idol worship if he serves an idol in its usual way, that is, performs any action that is the usual manner of worship for a particular idol, including embracing and kissing, etc., and even a disgraceful act.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Additionally, one is liable if he performs one of the four services used in the Temple: slaughters an offering, burns an offering, pours a libation, or bows down to an idol, even if that is not its usual manner of service. One is also liable if he accepts the idol upon himself as a deity or says to it, "You are my god."<br />
<br />
However, if one embraces, kisses, sweeps, sprinkles water, washes, anoints, clothes, or shoes  an idol, he merely transgresses a negative commandment. If one vows in the name of an idol or swears in its name, one transgresses a negative commandment. Defecating to Baal Pe'or and throwing a stone at Markulis (Mercury) is a standard service for these idols.<br />
<br />
Art: Persian Lady Worshipping the Rising Sun by Maria Hadfield Cosway
</span></div>

---

### content/sanhedrin/61.txt
<a id="src-00095"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/61.txt`

Sanhedrin 61 – Intention to Worship Idols
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1vW0MdUqfuXj3do1_A4cSktCIHhwSAo-D2L3sgW-6zAAIaeU4ODW5mwMldt_Qj9Qa_pr6lW2ejvzN1b-3_4rbe6p_cEIlgtDt27z8YR3AlzZQGdS_wCuv5EE5Iuw69XoM9VwKh3TL0FU/s1600/Paul+Gauguin+-+Rave+Te+Htit+Aamy+Aka+The+Idol.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1vW0MdUqfuXj3do1_A4cSktCIHhwSAo-D2L3sgW-6zAAIaeU4ODW5mwMldt_Qj9Qa_pr6lW2ejvzN1b-3_4rbe6p_cEIlgtDt27z8YR3AlzZQGdS_wCuv5EE5Iuw69XoM9VwKh3TL0FU/s320/Paul+Gauguin+-+Rave+Te+Htit+Aamy+Aka+The+Idol.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Hamnuna lost several oxen and went to search for them. Rabbah met him and asked a question: we have learned that <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/04/sanhedrin-60-idol-worship-liability.html">one who serves an idol is subject to stoning</a>. This implies that one has to actually serve the idol to be liable. But in regard to a subverted city, we have learned that if one says, “I will serve,” or “I will go and serve,” or “Let us go and serve” a certain idol, he is already liable. So is action required or is professed intention sufficient?<br />
<br />
Rav Hamnuna replied, “In the first case he does not accept the idol as deity until he serves it. In the second case, however, his statement implies that he accepts the idol as his deity as of now – and he will shortly serve it. Thus, he is liable for something else - for accepting the idol as a deity” - precisely <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/04/sanhedrin-60-idol-worship-liability.html">as we have learned</a>.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
The Talmud does not say what happened to the oxen.<br />
<br />
Art: Paul Gauguin - Rave Te Htit Aamy Aka The Idol</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/62.txt
<a id="src-00096"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/62.txt`

Sanhedrin 62- Multiple Acts of Service in One Period of Unawareness
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgDijPyKR6QQB73M-YohPzm9TKN-YpGkslgImpg8r2-JCIOM7XkmJvbgf2qp09ppr6Iv2D7oGdC2Gqn6OyCtQ3gbwvdHwrTskplveki8hW4giW7zWG6OQ7D_3Q2UBYIm7ZwYO-dO8czjFY/s1600/Winslow+Homer+-+Camp+fire.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgDijPyKR6QQB73M-YohPzm9TKN-YpGkslgImpg8r2-JCIOM7XkmJvbgf2qp09ppr6Iv2D7oGdC2Gqn6OyCtQ3gbwvdHwrTskplveki8hW4giW7zWG6OQ7D_3Q2UBYIm7ZwYO-dO8czjFY/s320/Winslow+Homer+-+Camp+fire.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Zakkai taught the following in the academy of Rabbi Yochanan: "If one slaughtered an offering, burnt an offering, poured a libation and bowed down to an idol, and he did all of these acts unintentionally in one period of unawareness, without realizing between the acts that he had committed a transgression, he is liable to bring only one sin offering." Rabbi Yochanan told him, "Leave my study hall and teach this ruling outside; it is incorrect."<br />
<br />
What was their disagreement? Rabbi Zakkai compared the rules of idol worship to the rules of the Sabbath. About Sabbath, it says, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=35%20">Do not ignite any fire, no matter where you live</a>." Since all manner of work is already prohibited, this extra commandment teaches how to treat multiple violations – according to some, as separate transgressions and, according to others, as one single transgression. Rabbi Zakkai followed the "single transgression" rule. However, Rabbi Yochanan held that the laws of idol worship are not comparable to the laws of the Sabbath in this respect.<br />
<br />
Art: Campfire by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Winslow Homer</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/63.txt
<a id="src-00097"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/63.txt`

Sanhedrin 63 – Joining God with Other Powers
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhprtkKP1z2qiBjChRKZruwYaPOQvTcUgHcldJwqAqsdBqnF4H3mZxacCmXF-lvWaMulidW10cIKBQtbEt0eyiYBRiYEeLW8eIsi36VPngreWCJc9rBDrCDcZcHlNg03c5vCMNKxX09nVE/s1600/Jacopo+Tintoretto+-+Adoration+of+the+Golden+Calf.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhprtkKP1z2qiBjChRKZruwYaPOQvTcUgHcldJwqAqsdBqnF4H3mZxacCmXF-lvWaMulidW10cIKBQtbEt0eyiYBRiYEeLW8eIsi36VPngreWCJc9rBDrCDcZcHlNg03c5vCMNKxX09nVE/s320/Jacopo+Tintoretto+-+Adoration+of+the+Golden+Calf.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When the Jews worshiped the Golden Calf, they said, "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/32-8.htm">These are your gods, O Israel, who brought you up from the Land of Egypt</a>." The word "brought" is in the plural, as indicated by an extra letter vav. This means that the Jews continued to recognize the divinity of God but paired Him with another entity. Had they said "brought" in singular, those who do evil to Israel (euphemism for the Jews themselves) would have been subject to extermination – this is the opinion of Rabbi Meir.<br />
<br />
However, Rabbi Shimon says that whoever worships the One in Heaven by pairing the name with something else is torn from the world, for it is stated "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-20.htm">only to God alone</a>." Rather, those who worshiped the Golden Calf accepted upon themselves many deities in addition to the Calf. They recognized God's omnipotence but contended that He had relegated jurisdiction over the world to many hosts.<br />
<br />
Art: Adoration of the Golden Calf by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jacopo Tintoretto</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/64.txt
<a id="src-00098"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/64.txt`

Sanhedrin 64 – Love for Idol Worship
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0cwkfcAc8HXscwYSOeahtOiIx1Ge0knP7nITdXa9ZmuV4Umtrxzb359Wkvp2X0KpOpu4FtPQ8MbIbeVXqjCTnyUzGE7v8Ri1jnfmaVPOZtWR_aYxHye4Mtz96R4QF0uce9PV7EEGecI4/s1600/Charles+Willson+Peale+-+Mother+Caressing+Her+Convalescant+Daughter.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0cwkfcAc8HXscwYSOeahtOiIx1Ge0knP7nITdXa9ZmuV4Umtrxzb359Wkvp2X0KpOpu4FtPQ8MbIbeVXqjCTnyUzGE7v8Ri1jnfmaVPOZtWR_aYxHye4Mtz96R4QF0uce9PV7EEGecI4/s320/Charles+Willson+Peale+-+Mother+Caressing+Her+Convalescant+Daughter.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Said Rav Yehudah in the name of Rav, "The Jews knew that there is no substance to idolatry, and they engaged in it only to permit for themselves overt immorality." However, after they became attached to it, they longed for it like one longs for his son.<br />
<br />
Elijah the Righteous would seek out those bloated from hunger in Jerusalem during the time of the first destruction. He found a child, bloated, in a heap of trash. The child was the last from a large family. Elijah asked, "If I teach you something by which you will merit to live, will you learn it?" The child replied, "Yes." Elijah told him, "Say, every day, Hear, O Israel, God our Lord, God is One." The child said, "Be silent; do not mention the name of God, which my father and mother had not taught." He then brought out the statue of his deity from his bosom, embraced it, and kissed it until his abdomen burst. He fell on his deity to fulfill, "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/26-30.htm%20">I will cast your carcasses upon the carcasses of your idols</a>."<br />
<br />
During the Second Temple, the Sages prayed and fasted for three days to eliminate the power of the Evil Urge for idol worship. It appeared as a fiery lion cub out of the Holy of Holies. They threw it into a lead cauldron and covered it with lead. They then tied the Evil Urge for immorality for three days but could not even find a fresh egg when they needed it. Since they could not eliminate the urge for only the prohibited, they at least removed the desire for relatives, like one's mother and sister.<br />
<br />
Art: Mother Caressing Her Convalescant Daughter by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Charles Willson Peale</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/65.txt
<a id="src-00099"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/65.txt`

Sanhedrin 65 – Molech, Ov, Yidoni
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpkaigV_ZGpWO0FF0ENml7qLsjVhSeST7JPpvdyzsjx324g_iXVaS2CW6f3sFpCoVY5fz8Uh1_pv5yBJ7BRUg6LG5isO1Pw-bnua-kk9TuqkmtncaVJHKBd_0sLBnbC5ikTcVj0ss-iTA/s1600/Aleksei+Ivanovich+Korzukhin+-+The+Wake+at+the+Cemetery.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpkaigV_ZGpWO0FF0ENml7qLsjVhSeST7JPpvdyzsjx324g_iXVaS2CW6f3sFpCoVY5fz8Uh1_pv5yBJ7BRUg6LG5isO1Pw-bnua-kk9TuqkmtncaVJHKBd_0sLBnbC5ikTcVj0ss-iTA/s320/Aleksei+Ivanovich+Korzukhin+-+The+Wake+at+the+Cemetery.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who gives of his offspring to Molech is not liable to stoning unless he hands the child over to Molech and passes him through the fire. The child would remain alive, being either passed between two walls of fire, or the parent would jump with him over a fiery pit. There were other forms of worship, though, where the child was actually burned.<br />
<br />
A practitioner of Ov is a necromancer  - one who communicates with the dead – by raising the spirit of the deceased from the ground and causing it to take up residence under his armpits, from where its voice emanates. A practitioner of Yidoni takes a bone of the animal known as Yadua and places it in his mouth, from where a voice emanates. These are both liable to stoning, and one who inquires of them violates a negative commandment.<br />
<br />
Art: The Wake at the Cemetery by Aleksei Ivanovich Korzukhin</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/66.txt
<a id="src-00100"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/66.txt`

Sanhedrin 66 – Cursing One's Parents, Having Relations with a Betrothed Maiden
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjomvqSRID3lj19isSzzs7kTtAP4vrU5B3gHS0A5hHnHJn5rzL8W1DPBOjlKz2v7klM7Vd4K33djTSDPgJOAJDKNhjDhIEaRvyuhVgcdSIdwZullAhgYnVjiuyJedgRHCtxiYrkecc58U/s1600/Lord+Frederick+Leighton+-+A+Girl.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjomvqSRID3lj19isSzzs7kTtAP4vrU5B3gHS0A5hHnHJn5rzL8W1DPBOjlKz2v7klM7Vd4K33djTSDPgJOAJDKNhjDhIEaRvyuhVgcdSIdwZullAhgYnVjiuyJedgRHCtxiYrkecc58U/s320/Lord+Frederick+Leighton+-+A+Girl.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who curses his father or his mother is not liable unless he curses them with the Name of God. If he cursed them with a subordinate Name of God – Rabbi Meir holds him liable, but the Sages exempt him.<br />
<br />
One who cohabits with a young maiden is not <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/22-21.htm">liable to be stoned</a>&nbsp;unless she is young (naarah), a virgin, betrothed, and still in her father's house. A naarah is a twelve-year-old girl who has sprouted two pubic hairs; she remains a naarah until she is twelve and a half. Virgin – but if she had intimate relations, their punishment is standard - strangulation. Betrothed – the first stage of marriage (kiddushin) has been performed, but there was no huppah, so she is yet not allowed to live with her husband. If two men cohabited with her anally, the first one is liable to stoning, and the second one – to strangulation.<br />
<br />
Art: A Girl by Lord Frederick Leighton</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/67.txt
<a id="src-00101"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/67.txt`

Sanhedrin 67 – Instigator to Idolatry
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhDOJQfE9C_MF-qOfDXKaMEHv83TBx-wRI1ndtCKZWY_cmZZ83i9JZxrFpvaM0txfnIINN8MQFW5gt2-JTm1mbSfMmcjVNAFAWa_A7zcizj1nzVpAcRGHSuNUu8zQRbnmQTwEpq-Z_FVxw/s1600/Niko+Pirosmanashvili+-+Healer+on+a+Donkey.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhDOJQfE9C_MF-qOfDXKaMEHv83TBx-wRI1ndtCKZWY_cmZZ83i9JZxrFpvaM0txfnIINN8MQFW5gt2-JTm1mbSfMmcjVNAFAWa_A7zcizj1nzVpAcRGHSuNUu8zQRbnmQTwEpq-Z_FVxw/s320/Niko+Pirosmanashvili+-+Healer+on+a+Donkey.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">An instigator might say, "There is a deity in such and such far-away place. Thus it eats. Thus it drinks. Thus it benefits. Thus it harms."<br />
<br />
If he says his words to two persons, they are his witnesses, even without a warning, and they bring him to court and stone him. If he says his remarks to one person, that person can entrap him, saying, "I have more friends who are interested." If the instigator is clever and refuses, they arrange witnesses behind a partition, and he asks the instigator to repeat his words in private. He then says, "How can we forget our God in Heaven and worship wood and stones?" If the instigator retracts, this is good; if not, the witnesses behind the partition take him to court.<br />
<br />
A person named Yannai asked for a drink at a certain inn. He saw that the waitress's lips were moving and understood that she was engaged in sorcery. He poured off some liquid, and it turned into scorpions. He gave the waitress to drink and she became a donkey. He rode upon her and went out to the marketplace. Her friend came and dissolved the magic spell, and Yannai was thus seen riding upon a woman in the marketplace.<br />
<br />
Art: Healer on a Donkey by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Niko Pirosmanashvili</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/68.txt
<a id="src-00102"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/68.txt`

Sanhedrin 68 – Wayward and Rebellious Son
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgX2rSuSfBFb_VImKZjeSG4vshoEjgi-phgT1a2mu-Faj7o_wT7zSCRCvFKry9SCN3B434mZAloth86uadjG1Rti0scxGNsxMzcf44D4zwojPkmVlXjNNfkKc974WDCeeCSlUyOWs1sKpE/s1600/Antonio+Mancini+-+The+Poor+Schoolboy.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgX2rSuSfBFb_VImKZjeSG4vshoEjgi-phgT1a2mu-Faj7o_wT7zSCRCvFKry9SCN3B434mZAloth86uadjG1Rti0scxGNsxMzcf44D4zwojPkmVlXjNNfkKc974WDCeeCSlUyOWs1sKpE/s320/Antonio+Mancini+-+The+Poor+Schoolboy.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Eliezer once taught Rabbi Akiba the act of magic with cucumbers: by saying a few words, he had planted a field full of cucumbers, and by saying a few other words, he made them collect into one place. How was he allowed to practice witchcraft if it says, "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/18-9.htm">You shall not learn to do it</a>?"– Because you can learn to understand and teach.<br />
<br />
However, that was the only piece of knowledge that Rabbi Akiba learned from him after Rabbi Eliezer was excommunicated for not following the law accepted by the majority. When Rabbi Eliezer was dying, he predicted that the Sages who did not realize their full learning potential because of not learning from him would die a martyr's death, and it came true.<br />
<br />
A wayward and rebellious son is a boy who commits certain sins associated with theft and gluttony. If his parents admonish him and he ignores their warnings, he is flogged in court. If he still persists in his behavior, he is put to death through stoning.<br />
<br />
Art: The Poor Schoolboy by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Antonio Mancini</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/69.txt
<a id="src-00103"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/69.txt`

Sanhedrin 69 – The Age of Wayward and Rebellious Son
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgv3BwJ_sY55uHFN8z5TrEwtJKAyAZvAh5wKQPvW1QBFlh0ClEqtrorWC0MWk-LfOZRiUqKwMH0XbI0Tn7UToTe9YTPp4ezUyd5OitV7nbfx3e5A2m4KJHG6kmO6ZutIosULA4EEIKDH7w/s1600/Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot+-+Italian+Youth+Sitting+in+Corot%27s+Room.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgv3BwJ_sY55uHFN8z5TrEwtJKAyAZvAh5wKQPvW1QBFlh0ClEqtrorWC0MWk-LfOZRiUqKwMH0XbI0Tn7UToTe9YTPp4ezUyd5OitV7nbfx3e5A2m4KJHG6kmO6ZutIosULA4EEIKDH7w/s320/Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot+-+Italian+Youth+Sitting+in+Corot%27s+Room.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The age at which a boy can become a wayward and rebellious son starts when he produces two pubic hairs after reaching the age of thirteen and continues until his beard grows around. This refers to the lower beard (pubic hair) and not the upper (facial) beard, but the Sages prefer to use clean language. Additionally, he cannot be older than thirteen and three months, so in most cases, this age starts at thirteen and ends at thirteen and three months.<br />
<br />
A man can be declared a wayward and rebellious son, but not a daughter because men are more given to base desires. <br />
<br />
Art: Italian Youth Sitting in Corot's Room by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jean-Baptiste-Camille Corot</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/7.txt
<a id="src-00104"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/7.txt`

Sanhedrin 7 – Common Wisdom and Torah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUh-raXq9fhgYuScPi5fMo5SzOfRH3zo-NMlI_fGswhuyTXTIgpzLyWKepbZGfmMpY4sC37s_YsVY55veyN4aH4_VorBw3GV1oUEKBWq78Fub7O51EWIvyU4LoYX6l9YrG79L5FXUsvak/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Bridge+at+Arles.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUh-raXq9fhgYuScPi5fMo5SzOfRH3zo-NMlI_fGswhuyTXTIgpzLyWKepbZGfmMpY4sC37s_YsVY55veyN4aH4_VorBw3GV1oUEKBWq78Fub7O51EWIvyU4LoYX6l9YrG79L5FXUsvak/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Bridge+at+Arles.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Huna said, "Discord is comparable to a channel from an overflowing river – once it starts, it will continue to widen" - as in Proverbs, "<a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/17-14.htm">The opening of a channel is a beginning of a discord</a>." Abaye Kashisha said, "Discord is like a plank in a bridge: once people walk on it, it becomes firm and stays firm."<br />
<br />
One man liked to say, "Fortunate is one who hears his denigration without responding. A hundred misfortunes will pass him by." Said Rav Yehudah, "beginning of discord (reshit madon) "can be translated as the beginning of a hundred misfortunes (resh meah dinim).<br />
<br />
One man liked to say, "When our love was strong, we could have lain together on the width of a sword, but now a bed of sixty amot (100 feet) does not suffice for us." Said Rav Huna - and so it is with God, at first it was "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/25-22.htm">and I will meet you (Moses) there and speak to you</a>..." from above the ten hand-breadth </span><span style="font-size: medium;">Ark</span><span style="font-size: medium;">, but later about the Temple built by Solomon "...<a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/66-1.htm">Says God - what house can you build for me</a>?"</span><br /><br /><div><span style="font-size: large;">Art: Bridge at Arles by Vincent Van Gogh</span></div>

---

### content/sanhedrin/70.txt
<a id="src-00105"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/70.txt`

Sanhedrin 70 – What Must a Boy Do to Earn the Designation of Wayward and Rebellious Son
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9z-U1f1vSFWeFEv9QVE8lc1qo4VhQBTqT9V1PMYnry4aImacZvC3kpTuW1V1D3Hd27zT5mNBNmYwMi2-KIgrzOBplWGrdX-ySWpg-CQxbCoQNLnJQu9RpVjScxB9hpVXgUsQVgpMFvmo/s1600/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Still+Life+With+Apples+Meat+And+A+Roll.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9z-U1f1vSFWeFEv9QVE8lc1qo4VhQBTqT9V1PMYnry4aImacZvC3kpTuW1V1D3Hd27zT5mNBNmYwMi2-KIgrzOBplWGrdX-ySWpg-CQxbCoQNLnJQu9RpVjScxB9hpVXgUsQVgpMFvmo/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Still+Life+With+Apples+Meat+And+A+Roll.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A wayward and rebellious son is executed because he engages in the type of gluttony that will lead him to murder. He incurs liability if he eats a large measure of meat, called tarteimar (about 1.5 pounds), and drinks half a log (volume of three eggs) of Italian wine, which is habit-forming. Rabbi Yossi doubles these measures. <br />
<br />He must buy that meat with the money stolen from his father, and he should be a repeat offender with prior warning and flogging.<br />
<br />
If he ate it at a gathering that involved a mitzvah, or at a meal convened to publicize the intercalation of a day into a month, or as second tithe in Jerusalem, if he ate an animal that died of itself, or one that was not properly slaughtered, if he ate non-kosher birds or non-kosher seafood, if he ate something from which tithes have not been separated – for all these he does not earn the designation, as it says, "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/21-20.htm">A glutton and a guzzler</a>."<br />
<br />
Art: Still Life With Apples, Meat, And A Roll by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Vincent Van Gogh</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/71.txt
<a id="src-00106"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/71.txt`

Sanhedrin 71 – Exclusions from the Law of Wayward and Rebellious Son
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhEgPHlw4U9TwYYf17GjB9E4i10b1RGOi8eRW8u-YeWI9A-fEf3MBAE3-_tP0HSjT6ab4osoBpwcUJI0fkPiHxlVDBB_LqhPk9ssUo-3jCnpS4MtHjmUzxBy9_GShUJ1MDhRt1c5XRQeLM/s1600/Arnold+Boonen+-+A+Young+Man+Seated+at+a+Table.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhEgPHlw4U9TwYYf17GjB9E4i10b1RGOi8eRW8u-YeWI9A-fEf3MBAE3-_tP0HSjT6ab4osoBpwcUJI0fkPiHxlVDBB_LqhPk9ssUo-3jCnpS4MtHjmUzxBy9_GShUJ1MDhRt1c5XRQeLM/s320/Arnold+Boonen+-+A+Young+Man+Seated+at+a+Table.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">To become a "wayward and rebellious son," the boy must steal money, spend it on meat and wine, and consume the requisite amounts. If he stole from his father and ate in his father's domain, or if he stole from others and ate in the domain of others – he does not qualify as a wayward and rebellious son, unless he steals from his father and eats in the domain of others. Rabbi Yose says not until he steals from both his father and his mother.<br />
<br />
The boy is not declared a wayward and rebellious son until both his father and mother are willing. If one of the parents is missing a hand or is lame, mute, blind, or deaf – the son does not become a wayward and rebellious son, because the parents need to be able to “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/21-19.htm">seize him...take him...and say</a>.”<br />
<br />
Art: A Young Man Seated at a Table by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Arnold Boonen</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/72.txt
<a id="src-00107"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/72.txt`

Sanhedrin 72- Judgment on the Account of the Ultimate End
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgBLRBt5lS0O0CfbIO7cZXvwXFu5pH56T_V1zDF7yGVtAala6io_BRvpKU_BLXm4RYS7ayvfKwXn5cwC6gdJud2E93_ljYi8opdQM8KiKiCa_TsKAHOSLPradjWjqKgUtKU5_BvW4czoCg/s1600/Joseph+Mallord+William+Turner-+A+Canal+Tunnel+Near+Leeds.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgBLRBt5lS0O0CfbIO7cZXvwXFu5pH56T_V1zDF7yGVtAala6io_BRvpKU_BLXm4RYS7ayvfKwXn5cwC6gdJud2E93_ljYi8opdQM8KiKiCa_TsKAHOSLPradjWjqKgUtKU5_BvW4czoCg/s320/Joseph+Mallord+William+Turner-+A+Canal+Tunnel+Near+Leeds.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A wayward and rebellious son is judged on account of his ultimate end: having accustomed himself to stealing and indulgence, he will eventually rob and kill people. Therefore, let him die while he is still innocent and not guilty of a capital crime. For the wicked, death is beneficial to them and to the world, but for the righteous, death is detrimental to them and to the world.<br />
<br />
A burglar who enters a house by tunneling through its wall is judged on account of his ultimate end. He is aware that the occupant of the house will defend his belongings, and it is therefore assumed that the burglar decides to kill an occupant if that becomes necessary. Therefore, the occupant is permitted to kill the burglar.<br />
<br />
Art: A Canal Tunnel Near Leeds by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Joseph Mallord William Turner</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/73.txt
<a id="src-00108"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/73.txt`

Sanhedrin 73 – Preventing a Criminal at the Cost of his Life
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUnIWzuZ1etRIrN_F827Occ2s3C34w-ithwHZDLlSWg1o-rkiLYh1IDb3QPhMQXCY6adrQTHXTdrcjBsCHTYXD8oO0tIVS9C3rUDbV-nXW7sKaiDZcPl_MvYPurhagtDIEdUDanoZFj5o/s1600/Paul+C%C3%A9zanne+-+Murder.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUnIWzuZ1etRIrN_F827Occ2s3C34w-ithwHZDLlSWg1o-rkiLYh1IDb3QPhMQXCY6adrQTHXTdrcjBsCHTYXD8oO0tIVS9C3rUDbV-nXW7sKaiDZcPl_MvYPurhagtDIEdUDanoZFj5o/s320/Paul+C%C3%A9zanne+-+Murder.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following may be prevented from sinning at the cost of their lives, that is, they may be killed in order to prevent them from committing the transgression: one who pursues a fellow to kill him, and one who runs after a male to sodomize him, or after a betrothed maiden to violate her.<br />
<br />
However, the following may not be killed: one who pursues a beast for the purpose of sodomy, one who is about to desecrate the Sabbath or one who is about to engage in idol worship. <br />
<br />
Art: Murder by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Paul Cezanne</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/74.txt
<a id="src-00109"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/74.txt`

Sanhedrin 74 – Use of Lesser Force
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhrJfE63Z4WL1gHgrKxFCP85Zl_W7ZGqc4mqSe3LZTJpwuxEp4mOgU-ZJZvQT_yFAoKjAt8NdAIiSPQA4_t_tS-Gn-KDm7iwyalRH6hJCm4rnRPu807uQns0SrAaiQ3f-9ArDk9ukUYnwQ/s1600/Emile+Friant+-+The+Fight.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhrJfE63Z4WL1gHgrKxFCP85Zl_W7ZGqc4mqSe3LZTJpwuxEp4mOgU-ZJZvQT_yFAoKjAt8NdAIiSPQA4_t_tS-Gn-KDm7iwyalRH6hJCm4rnRPu807uQns0SrAaiQ3f-9ArDk9ukUYnwQ/s320/Emile+Friant+-+The+Fight.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Yonathan ben Shaul said, "If someone was pursuing a victim with the intent of killing him, and it was possible to save the intended victim by disabling one of the pursuer's limbs, and the rescuer did not save the victim through those means, but instead killed the pursuer, the rescuer is put to the death on account of killing the pursuer." Whether the rescuer is actually executed by the courts for killing the pursuer or whether he is subject to death at the hands of Heaven – is a subject of disagreement between later authorities.<br />
<br />
If someone being pursued broke items of the pursuer, he is exempt from paying, but if he broke items belonging to any other person, he is liable. However, if the rescuer was chasing the pursuer to prevent him from committing murder and broke vessels of any party, he is always exempt, because otherwise nobody would be saving his fellow from the pursuer.<br />
<br />
Art: The Fight by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Emile Friant</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/75.txt
<a id="src-00110"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/75.txt`

Sanhedrin 75 – Who is Burned
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_9AKmkjMTrSfRN_gHvv1AUsArMpKla3xdOhbKuEuZzNBAH_MuSvo_sNXfKSEyZl03qGgIQ1mXEpdEWE39uA3eMdyNdNiVT-0wzppLjeF3HBGNzn9YQ8_XsfAG7EYLJOi0NEsvDqzlIqg/s1600/Mrs.+Louisa+Starr+Canziani+-+Kathleen+and+Mary+Ann.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_9AKmkjMTrSfRN_gHvv1AUsArMpKla3xdOhbKuEuZzNBAH_MuSvo_sNXfKSEyZl03qGgIQ1mXEpdEWE39uA3eMdyNdNiVT-0wzppLjeF3HBGNzn9YQ8_XsfAG7EYLJOi0NEsvDqzlIqg/s320/Mrs.+Louisa+Starr+Canziani+-+Kathleen+and+Mary+Ann.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following transgressions carry the penalty of burning. "Burning" does not mean that the convict is set on fire, but rather that molten lead is poured down his throat.<br />
<br />
One who cohabits with a woman and her daughter, and the married daughter of a Kohen who commits adultery – however, the man who committed adultery with her is strangled, like all other adulterers. Similar to the category of a woman and her daughter, one is burned for cohabiting with his daughter, his daughter's daughter and his son's daughter, his wife's daughter, her daughter's daughter, and her son's daughter; his mother-in-law, his mother-in-law's mother, and his father-in-law's mother.<br />
<br />
Art: Kathleen and Mary Ann by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Mrs. Louisa Starr Canziani</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/76.txt
<a id="src-00111"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/76.txt`

Sanhedrin 76 – Who is Beheaded
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj4H0lEPy_XicHt0RGL9hIpm6wmzXe8q4n5NJnGEWWE-4ANKn3ocbN9M5tXpcd072aSIkKEKFFT9ybIagJTyH84COWKHIWjvCK7LPJU-rG-gsF6RkePBlTHyXJztfdauaA8Ku_bk-x5QWQ/s1600/Arthur+William+Devis+-+The+Snake+Charmer.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj4H0lEPy_XicHt0RGL9hIpm6wmzXe8q4n5NJnGEWWE-4ANKn3ocbN9M5tXpcd072aSIkKEKFFT9ybIagJTyH84COWKHIWjvCK7LPJU-rG-gsF6RkePBlTHyXJztfdauaA8Ku_bk-x5QWQ/s320/Arthur+William+Devis+-+The+Snake+Charmer.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following transgressors face the penalty of beheading: a murderer and people of a subverted city who were led astray and worshipped a false god.<br />
<br />
If a murderer struck his fellow with a stone or with a piece of iron, or if he held him in water or fire and the victim could not escape and died, the murderer is liable to execution. But if the murderer pushed him into water or into fire and he was able to escape, but he died anyway, the murderer is not liable to execution. If he incited a dog or a snake to bite a man, and a dog or a snake bit him, and he died, the murderer is not liable to execution. Since he did not murder the victim directly, he cannot be executed by a human court.<br />
<br />
If someone took the snake in his hand and held its fangs to the victim's flesh, Rabbi Yehudah rules that he is liable to the death penalty, but the Sages exempt him.<br />
<br />
Art: The Snake Charmer by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Arthur William Devis</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/77.txt
<a id="src-00112"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/77.txt`

Sanhedrin 77 – No Liability for Indirect Killing
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiYiceSyQRyKWm_B90UXIveMptiMwk0qwo200TFUQRF3ZwKEDgarMoi6OHU1xDtRT2h0ykhY1LgHlitL4VnZy5xSvwbDpNaWC-ki93OpHAwU3188m9kffMQ7frVCkFwCCMcPd98pjMKyV8/s1600/William+Payne+-+Landscape+with+a+waterfall.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiYiceSyQRyKWm_B90UXIveMptiMwk0qwo200TFUQRF3ZwKEDgarMoi6OHU1xDtRT2h0ykhY1LgHlitL4VnZy5xSvwbDpNaWC-ki93OpHAwU3188m9kffMQ7frVCkFwCCMcPd98pjMKyV8/s320/William+Payne+-+Landscape+with+a+waterfall.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Someone bound his fellow by the seashore, then caused a stream of water to sweep over him and thereby killed him. This was done thus - he made a hole in a dam that stood between the water and the victim so that the water would gush out and drown the victim. In such a case, the water is considered like arrows that he shot at the victim, and he is liable to execution. <br />
<br />
However, this is only so when the water that reached the victim fell on him immediately after the barrier was breached. If some time lapsed before the water reached the victim, it is no longer considered the perpetrator's primary force, and he is not liable.<br />
<br />As a general principle, one is liable for murder only if it was caused by his direct force, not by any removed or consequential action, and, of course, if he has been properly warned a short while before the action.<br />
<br />
Art: Landscape with a waterfall by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">William Payne</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/78.txt
<a id="src-00113"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/78.txt`

Sanhedrin 78 – Group Murder, Partial Recovery
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgQTfEkw3R-xTgrF3VnQHbnb0K8SWakX7HE1hgMzDLrpFXdPxSejawPWGeRsSDRYo6jwjghbQE08FchL5F4pJv6bny5L8m5e2nngITL24cXwqBc_V2WMq3F_nRTkzuAeqyrwiebTbvhJZ8/s1600/Joost+Cornelisz+-+Droochsloot+-+Brawling+Peasants.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgQTfEkw3R-xTgrF3VnQHbnb0K8SWakX7HE1hgMzDLrpFXdPxSejawPWGeRsSDRYo6jwjghbQE08FchL5F4pJv6bny5L8m5e2nngITL24cXwqBc_V2WMq3F_nRTkzuAeqyrwiebTbvhJZ8/s320/Joost+Cornelisz+-+Droochsloot+-+Brawling+Peasants.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If ten people beat someone with ten clubs and he died, whether they hit him all at the same time or one after the other, they are not liable to execution.<br />
<br />
If they hit him one after the other, the last nine are not liable because they struck a man who would have died anyway. The first assailant is not liable because there is a remote possibility that the man would have recovered had the others not continued beating him. If they hit him simultaneously, each one can plead that the victim might have lived if not for the blows of others. Rabbi Yehuda ben Beteira makes the last one liable. Both derive their rulings from "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/24-17.htm">if a man strikes all human life</a>." <br />
<br />
If someone struck his fellow, and the judges assumed that he would die, but he recovered somewhat and then deteriorated and died, the attacker is liable. Rabbi Nechemiah makes him not liable, since there are grounds for asserting that the victim did not die a result of the attacker's blow.<br />
<br />
Art: Brawling Peasants by Joost Cornelisz - Droochsloot</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/79.txt
<a id="src-00114"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/79.txt`

Sanhedrin 79 – Aiming at One, but Killing Another
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgaGrN4REPhNF8jAFvOptGW6DCIpC1MkX0aq0j71A3IVUQDrFsvmOOQt__ggUt5uFhIE14kUE_MgC2TX3r0GlvIs_cEBMbspeyrX-IsxlsgB3QhhVt7g6WHgqCWJbrwgJ5WorOp-oZqIt0/s1600/Frank+Duveneck+-+The+Cobbler%27s+Apprentice.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgaGrN4REPhNF8jAFvOptGW6DCIpC1MkX0aq0j71A3IVUQDrFsvmOOQt__ggUt5uFhIE14kUE_MgC2TX3r0GlvIs_cEBMbspeyrX-IsxlsgB3QhhVt7g6WHgqCWJbrwgJ5WorOp-oZqIt0/s320/Frank+Duveneck+-+The+Cobbler%27s+Apprentice.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one intended to kill an animal but killed a man instead, he is not liable since he lacked the intent to kill a man. If one intended to kill an idolater but killed a Jew instead, he cannot be executed by a Jewish court. While it is certainly forbidden to kill any human being, this matter is outside of the jurisdiction of Sanhedrin. If one intended to kill a premature, nonviable baby but killed a viable one instead, he is not liable to execution because the warning given to him would have been uncertain.<br />
<br />
If he intended to strike an adult with a blow not sufficient to kill an adult, but it landed on a child instead, and it was sufficient to kill a child, and the child died, he is not liable because he did not intend to commit murder, and any warning would be uncertain.<br />
<br />
If he intended to kill an adult, but it landed on a child instead, and the child died, the killer is liable to execution.<br />
<br />
Art: The Cobbler's Apprentice by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Frank Duveneck</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/8.txt
<a id="src-00115"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/8.txt`

Sanhedrin 8 – One Who Defames His Wife
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0-_T42wmxCv9rVsK0sFlxkWQwHn0exVSrw8-ySZv16loJLdHLV5DlDDvb4TsGu7Z5cy6qzeTkJHCsHQdURhXUFjBiwVoShZ_0QAVqyssZTeM3DUvI-UNcJ9rdwTtL7RwQLSAVvB_Tf1c/s1600-h/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Cittern+Player.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0-_T42wmxCv9rVsK0sFlxkWQwHn0exVSrw8-ySZv16loJLdHLV5DlDDvb4TsGu7Z5cy6qzeTkJHCsHQdURhXUFjBiwVoShZ_0QAVqyssZTeM3DUvI-UNcJ9rdwTtL7RwQLSAVvB_Tf1c/s320/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Cittern+Player.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Claims against a rapist, a seducer, and the claim of a defamer are judged by the court of three – this is the opinion of Rabbi Meir. The Sages say that the claim of a defamer is judged by a court of twenty-three (small Sanhedrin), because defamation cases include capital cases.<br />
<br />
A defamer usually refers to a husband who falsely declares in court that his wife was not a virgin when their marriage was consummated. He claims that she had committed adultery after they were legally married and produces false witnesses to her adultery. After the witnesses are found false, he must pay a fine of 100 shekels to her father; he is liable to lashes, and he may never divorce her against her will.<br />
<br />
Art: The Cittern Player by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Gabriel Metsu</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/80.txt
<a id="src-00116"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/80.txt`

Sanhedrin 80 – Murderer Mix-Up
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg89x7XYwrFl4WW8fJnYRjDm4Z-oiEiPnz12VG354pGOJ_cfhT7VTsDDdrPpfErF86DUjXpo1ywIp2BiuHrYf4-j08qvgW4d0bdL2TS8qbnnObQkUqi0_fYVI0c0pqxFYXJSNNHmsJRKFY/s1600/Johann+Sperl+-+A+Wine+Cellar.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg89x7XYwrFl4WW8fJnYRjDm4Z-oiEiPnz12VG354pGOJ_cfhT7VTsDDdrPpfErF86DUjXpo1ywIp2BiuHrYf4-j08qvgW4d0bdL2TS8qbnnObQkUqi0_fYVI0c0pqxFYXJSNNHmsJRKFY/s320/Johann+Sperl+-+A+Wine+Cellar.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a murderer becomes intermingled with others, they are all exempt from capital punishment. Rabbi Yehudah says, "We place them in a cell where they are fed barley until their stomachs burst."<br />
<br />
Who are these others? One explanation is that a murderer whose verdict has not been finalized – even though the judges have voted for a guilty sentence - got mixed with other murderers whose verdicts have been finalized. Since the verdict has to be announced in his presence, and they don't know who he is, and since moreover, they have to say to him, "So-and-so, you are liable," and again, they can't – he is free and with him all the other murderers. Rabbi Yehudah holds that since, after all, they are murderers and cannot be executed only because of a technicality, the court causes their deaths indirectly.<br />
<br />
Art: A Wine Cellar by Johann Sperl
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/81.txt
<a id="src-00117"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/81.txt`

Sanhedrin 81 – Indirect Death Sentence
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiOd-UH49Hy8Tbm4v91uKVUQAEAXrBrcrGzHeGJmPc_G0cOQZJcJxrWBHscODdglDQXp9S1q4fTZ3L6hB7-Lux_k9I2i6ntn2KpmhDxFqzgibHcxY_By9PVfEQNIWz0mPhzrdzo0XEB4p8/s1600/Jean+Michelin+-+The+Bread+Seller+and+Water+Carriers.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiOd-UH49Hy8Tbm4v91uKVUQAEAXrBrcrGzHeGJmPc_G0cOQZJcJxrWBHscODdglDQXp9S1q4fTZ3L6hB7-Lux_k9I2i6ntn2KpmhDxFqzgibHcxY_By9PVfEQNIWz0mPhzrdzo0XEB4p8/s320/Jean+Michelin+-+The+Bread+Seller+and+Water+Carriers.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who became liable to two types of execution by the court is subject to the more severe type. <br />
<br />One who has been flogged twice by the court – the court places him in a cell, and there they feed him barely until his stomach bursts. How could that be? Here, we are dealing with one who repeated the same transgression twice, provided that this transgression carries the penalty of excision from Heaven. Since he demonstrated that he wanted to die, the court just sped up his death. However, if he transgressed multiple prohibitions, but each of them only once, he just tastes various prohibitions.<br />
<br />One who killed another but not in the presence of witnesses – that is, they gave him a warning, but he just nodded his head instead of a verbal reply or a similar technical disqualification – the court places him in a cell and feeds him scant bread and water until he dies.<br />
<br />
Complete cell procedure: They put him in a cell the size of his body, then fed him scant amounts until his stomach shrinks, then fed him abundant barley until his stomach bursts.<br />
<br />
Art: The Bread Seller and Water Carriers by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jean Michelin</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/82.txt
<a id="src-00118"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/82.txt`

Sanhedrin 82 – Extrajudicial Executions
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjC2aqrdKsW0PDm9cz2mo8e7Z7FxpeXDE1dszZOHR9s1Apqp1VFCP2Cb8EyeK91gZ02BPBkxw59C3Zmm1-RWbHzJFk2F4cGYtGSXLAdiq60QTvkoG6uEDkEpT35lWJ9LUz2pUIpYCVY_8Q/s1600/Paul+Cezanne+-+Vessels+Fruit+And+Cloth+In+Front+Of+A+Chest.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjC2aqrdKsW0PDm9cz2mo8e7Z7FxpeXDE1dszZOHR9s1Apqp1VFCP2Cb8EyeK91gZ02BPBkxw59C3Zmm1-RWbHzJFk2F4cGYtGSXLAdiq60QTvkoG6uEDkEpT35lWJ9LUz2pUIpYCVY_8Q/s320/Paul+Cezanne+-+Vessels+Fruit+And+Cloth+In+Front+Of+A+Chest.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There are exceptional cases of transgressions that do not involve court action but are carried out either by the zealots or by Kohanim in the Temple. <br />
<br />
One who steals service vessels in the Temple; one who blasphemes by a supernatural force, saying, "Let the supernatural force (that is, the idol) smite him (the blasphemer's enemy), his Creator, and his Provider"; and one who cohabits with an Aramean woman – zealots may kill him.<br />
<br />If a zealot comes to ask about this ruling, he is not told about it and is not given permission. He has to know it from before and then take the risk into his own hands. Furthermore, he can only do it while the sinner is engaged in his sin. If the sinner stops, and the zealot kills him after that, the zealot is responsible for murder.<br />
<br />
If a Kohen serves in the Temple in a state of ritual impurity, young Kohanim remove him outside the Courtyard and split open his skull with clubs.<br />
<br />
Art: Vessels Fruit And Cloth In Front Of A Chest by Paul Cezanne
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/83.txt
<a id="src-00119"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/83.txt`

Sanhedrin 83 – Transgressions and Punishments of  a Kohen
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9BAS1iklbjhyphenhyphenkZ6wHLuYqqOI4zfHn5A8XngJIFMlg0PcECk7MYWoDzKMEZ0gC8V7UNfwk-JDIyN8gpdf9ZwijDIhRRQZHykjdNf3VEis2kGfSNEuxs-D2muWhwY4i7Gg7Ppk_c3kPtJU/s1600/Le+Nain+Brothers-+The+Peasant+Meal.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9BAS1iklbjhyphenhyphenkZ6wHLuYqqOI4zfHn5A8XngJIFMlg0PcECk7MYWoDzKMEZ0gC8V7UNfwk-JDIyN8gpdf9ZwijDIhRRQZHykjdNf3VEis2kGfSNEuxs-D2muWhwY4i7Gg7Ppk_c3kPtJU/s320/Le+Nain+Brothers-+The+Peasant+Meal.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Acha bur Huna inquired of Rav Sheshet, "If a Kohen served in the Temple in a state of spiritual impurity, is he liable to death at the hands  of Heaven?"<br />
<br /><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">Said Rav Sheshet, "Your answer is in&nbsp;<a href="" target="_blank">the previous ruling</a>: Young Kohanim removed him outside the Courtyard and split open his skull with clubs.</span>&nbsp;If he is liable at the hands of Heaven, simply leave him to die at the hands of Heaven!" Answered Rav Acha, "But could it be that he is not liable at the hands of Heaven, and yet we do kill him?" The final rule is that the Kohen is indeed liable to death at the hands of Heaven, but only if he performed a concluding service.<br />
<br />
The following are liable to death at the hands of Heaven: one who eats produce before tithe separation, a non-Kohen who eats a Kohen's portion, a non-Kohen who serves in the Temple, and a ritually impure Kohen who serves in the Temple.<br />
<br />
Art: The Peasant Meal by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Le Nain Brothers</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/84.txt
<a id="src-00120"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/84.txt`

Sanhedrin 84 – Who is Strangled
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5n53_s4bomlgIEyV4C72HbiZLulMmg_HpwUDctapDs6QjsSjMTlX-bThS1HsC0rcNgIuePrJZ7NKokR9e0Ne05AIQuto-XVyph1lJ2GlDbzw3nugL0i1eTqqEsnkPL7RbKTHPR7ppmaE/s1600/William+Etty+-+The+slave.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5n53_s4bomlgIEyV4C72HbiZLulMmg_HpwUDctapDs6QjsSjMTlX-bThS1HsC0rcNgIuePrJZ7NKokR9e0Ne05AIQuto-XVyph1lJ2GlDbzw3nugL0i1eTqqEsnkPL7RbKTHPR7ppmaE/s320/William+Etty+-+The+slave.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The complete <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/04/sanhedrin-53-who-is-stoned.html">procedure for strangulation was described earlier</a>.<br />
<br />
The following are executed by strangulation: one who strikes his father or his mother and inflicts a wound; one who kidnaps a Jewish person, works him, then sells him as a slave; a sage who rebels against the word of the High Court; a false prophet; one who prophesies in the name of a false god; one who commits adultery; false witnesses against a daughter of a Kohen; and a man who illicitly cohabited with the daughter of a Kohen.<br />
<br />
Even though the witnesses have tried to impose the punishment of burning on the daughter of a Kohen, when they are disqualified as false  witnesses, they receive the punishment appropriate for the adulterer, and not the adulteress, because of "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/19-19.htm">as he conspired to do to his brother</a>."<br />
<br />
Art: The Slave by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">William Etty</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/85.txt
<a id="src-00121"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/85.txt`

Sanhedrin 85 – Striking and Cursing a Parent, Selling a Kidnapped into Slavery
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhI1TKcG9kp2T9qNKCLEiE59K3bUQ_hh8oy6Gz1VkFHThqtJGSguOTKEPzdugWJ5yLRgouh8D90vHoHp1NSKAhBVUeXsi_xJaa4s_3eiazhi5tUAzuMQy6CJNf5aui5pRY0DU3epy_4AC0/s1600/Salvatore+Frangiamore+-+A+Slap+In+The+Face.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhI1TKcG9kp2T9qNKCLEiE59K3bUQ_hh8oy6Gz1VkFHThqtJGSguOTKEPzdugWJ5yLRgouh8D90vHoHp1NSKAhBVUeXsi_xJaa4s_3eiazhi5tUAzuMQy6CJNf5aui5pRY0DU3epy_4AC0/s320/Salvatore+Frangiamore+-+A+Slap+In+The+Face.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who strikes his father or mother is not liable to execution unless he wounds them. Cursing a parent is more stringent than striking him since one who curses his parent after the parent's death is liable to execution, but one who strikes his parent after the parent's death is exempt.<br />
<br />
One is liable for cursing a parent only if the parent is "among your people," that is, doing the deeds of your people – observing the Torah. One is liable for striking even a non-observant parent.<br />
<br />
One who kidnaps a Jew is not liable to strangulation unless he takes him into his possession, works him, and sells him. If one kidnaps his own son, then Rabbi Ishmael makes him liable, but the Sages exempt him. If one kidnapped someone who was half slave and half freeman, Rabbi Yehudah renders him liable, but the Sages exempt him.<br />
<br />
Art: A Slap In The Face by Salvatore Frangiamore</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/86.txt
<a id="src-00122"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/86.txt`

Sanhedrin 86 – A Rebellious Sage
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjXP-MH1Rqqbrb8yOi3Ym1j7dGcmwW-mGD-3oNyqDT2BPrp-YgU_SvcSVeofcWIJZef7EgZAH1A6RYpoD1bBOJzVDJXMOPA5feQU-dzhyphenhyphen_g_8jCM6dvAgXLdELPsUI0dLnnGrGKceLv5vY/s1600/Jean-L%C3%A9on+G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me+-+Dispute+D%27Arabes.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjXP-MH1Rqqbrb8yOi3Ym1j7dGcmwW-mGD-3oNyqDT2BPrp-YgU_SvcSVeofcWIJZef7EgZAH1A6RYpoD1bBOJzVDJXMOPA5feQU-dzhyphenhyphen_g_8jCM6dvAgXLdELPsUI0dLnnGrGKceLv5vY/s320/Jean-L%C3%A9on+G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me+-+Dispute+D%27Arabes.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A sage who rebels against the word of  the High Court is executed by strangulation.<br />
<br />
There were three courts in Jerusalem, one sitting at the entrance to the Temple Mount, one higher up on the Temple Mount, at the entrance of the Temple Courtyard, and one even higher up the Mount sitting in the Chamber of Hewn Stone.<br />
<br />
The dissenting sage and his disputants on the local court would come to the court at the entrance to the Temple Mount, and the dissenting sage would say before the court, "Thus have I expounded, and thus have my colleagues expounded, thus have I taught, and thus have my colleagues taught." If the court judges have heard the answer from their teachers, they tell the disputants the law; if not, they go to a higher court. There, the procedure is repeated. If the highest court has a tradition, they tell it; if not, they decide it, and it becomes binding.<br />
<br />Art: Dispute D'Arabes by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jean-Leon Gerome</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/87.txt
<a id="src-00123"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/87.txt`

Sanhedrin 87 – What Has the Rebellious Sage Done?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhdLtu5lWSdLnOnq9-DKHtsUCXK9diFwuzClkA-RopYFj791fCMQCDdcVLc4ocCjYWy5TahOq8fOlxbON2KfLOMY_3OBhMh_00v8RZgaQ5l-G-BLhFfb8kGWI4CKJ9ChJB4QkujLTlhls/s1600/Arthur+Boyd++Houghton+-+The+sage+and+the+geckos.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhdLtu5lWSdLnOnq9-DKHtsUCXK9diFwuzClkA-RopYFj791fCMQCDdcVLc4ocCjYWy5TahOq8fOlxbON2KfLOMY_3OBhMh_00v8RZgaQ5l-G-BLhFfb8kGWI4CKJ9ChJB4QkujLTlhls/s320/Arthur+Boyd++Houghton+-+The+sage+and+the+geckos.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">After the High Court has decided in opposition to the ruling of the rebellious sage, and the sage has returned to his town and taught and interpreted in the manner he was used to before being instructed otherwise by the High Court, he is not yet liable; but if he instructed people to act in accordance with his overruled opinion, he is liable to the death penalty as a rebellious sage, as it is stated, "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-12.htm">but the man who will act with willfulness</a>."<br />
<br />
A disciple who instructed people to act in accordance with his opinion that was overruled by the High Court is not liable – and it emerges that his stringency (no authority to decide the questions of law) is his leniency (not being liable as a rebellious sage).<br />
<br />
Art: The sage and the geckos by Arthur Boyd Houghton
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/88.txt
<a id="src-00124"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/88.txt`

Sanhedrin 88 – How is a Judge Selected to High Court
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJaTpZmDsHmo8wYirMRPykNKypnS2r1pEZTIwNEQ0d2VomE9w8e4ddHth6UiCkmiGVFrc8vzk6HfyUvmHYXOOjKM8upP3oaOm-V7dKUjhL_wcDYBW7mqFtA9_w3nkIbdpFn5zozRmPuKc/s1600/Marc+Chagall++-+The+Praying+Jew.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJaTpZmDsHmo8wYirMRPykNKypnS2r1pEZTIwNEQ0d2VomE9w8e4ddHth6UiCkmiGVFrc8vzk6HfyUvmHYXOOjKM8upP3oaOm-V7dKUjhL_wcDYBW7mqFtA9_w3nkIbdpFn5zozRmPuKc/s320/Marc+Chagall++-+The+Praying+Jew.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The judges  of the Great Sanhedrin would send the following message to lower courts in all places, "Anyone who is wise and humble and whom the people find agreeable shall be a judge in his city." From there, they elevate the deserving judge to the court that sits at the entrance to the courtyard and, from there – to the Sanhedrin, which sits in the Chamber of Hewn Stone. An additional qualification is that he constantly learns Torah but does not take credit for it for himself.<br />
<br />
With regard to a rebellious sage, greater stringency is attached to the teachings of the Sages, like the ones found in the Talmud, than to the words of the Torah. If, for example, he says that there is no commandment of tefillin, he is exempt since it is such an obvious distortion that it cannot be viewed as a ruling. However, if he says that there are five compartments in the tefillin and not four, he is liable.<br />
<br />
Art: The Praying Jew by Marc Chagall
</span>

---
