Sanhedrin 89 – False Prophet
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj59UDxyZgNTr4xxXKvSSOekIIfpiWgRMcc2eErc4GFZ3d9Jhdfx2-QcLu4aA5vqA94-h2lF5RxuE5vkeWl0mm996ik0fPX8RMYHddY1g-_gy8U_DwGDnTKe-D-SF5Ky50Dt5quV4u3tIY/s1600/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Study+for+Two+Heads+for+Boston+Mural+%27The+Prophets%27.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj59UDxyZgNTr4xxXKvSSOekIIfpiWgRMcc2eErc4GFZ3d9Jhdfx2-QcLu4aA5vqA94-h2lF5RxuE5vkeWl0mm996ik0fPX8RMYHddY1g-_gy8U_DwGDnTKe-D-SF5Ky50Dt5quV4u3tIY/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Study+for+Two+Heads+for+Boston+Mural+%27The+Prophets%27.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">The rebellious sage is executed by the High Court in Jerusalem at the time of the next Festival so that "<a href="" target="_blank">the entire nation shall hear and fear and will not act willfully anymore</a>"&nbsp;- these are the words of Rabbi Akiva.</span>&nbsp;However, Rabbi Yehudah says that they do not delay the judgment but rather execute him immediately and then write out proclamations and send messengers to all places.<br />
<br />
A false prophet is executed at the hands of man, but one who suppresses his prophecy, one who disregards the word of a prophet, or a prophet who transgresses his own words is subject to death at the hands of Heaven. <br />
<br />
Art: Study for Two Heads for Boston Mural 'The Prophets' by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">John Singer Sargent</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/9.txt
<a id="src-00126"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/9.txt`

Sanhedrin 9 – Reasons for Disagreement on Defamer
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjA0sj4hncJ6Sj8f4VDDB9F1ru7haMz09x3tmeTrCssyeMj7z3SebyTeHYPFlRSTWsSt5F4SDHPmbv24jlQ_yFrH2ygYrvSGGIj_oM3Sj2e4QPiE5YDD_sKfargLy959bVvu2gBe7WG9mY/s1600-h/Ivan+Nikolaevich+Kramskoy+-+Reading+%28portrait+of+the+artist%27s+wife%29.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjA0sj4hncJ6Sj8f4VDDB9F1ru7haMz09x3tmeTrCssyeMj7z3SebyTeHYPFlRSTWsSt5F4SDHPmbv24jlQ_yFrH2ygYrvSGGIj_oM3Sj2e4QPiE5YDD_sKfargLy959bVvu2gBe7WG9mY/s320/Ivan+Nikolaevich+Kramskoy+-+Reading+%28portrait+of+the+artist%27s+wife%29.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Meir requires only <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/02/sanhedrin-8-one-who-defames-his-wife.html">three judges to judge a husband who defames his wife, but the Sages require twenty three</a>. Here are four out of eight possible reasons for the disagreement.<br />
<br />
* The husband comes without the support of the witnesses, but the Sages fear that witnesses to adultery might come forward when gossip spreads;<br />
* The husband claimed to have witnesses of adultery, and the court of twenty-three was convened to try this capital case, but then the husband failed to produce witnesses. The Sages rule that the original twenty-three judges should be retained for the sake of their honor;<br />
* The witnesses warned the woman that if she commits adultery, she will be liable to the death penalty, but did not specify the method of execution;<br />
* The woman was learned, and the witnesses did not give her any warning not to commit adultery.<br />
<br />
Art: Reading (portrait of the artist's wife) by Ivan Nikolaevich Kramskoy
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/90.txt
<a id="src-00127"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/90.txt`

Sanhedrin 90 – Share in the World to Come
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwwEFMmln6GyS95duD9oM7rMFSAccnGUyRZIPnJRpsfdOy9tDuzBWrcwdeyMpu_qFiSY6JkL9da9mEvRxx9HqD6mNm7B8QjfE5LB4uCG96XKZxPr8yjKGJvE4IL2YZ3ywYtakH6Es91Bw/s1600/Claudio+Francesco+Beaumont+-+The+Resurrection+of+the+dead.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwwEFMmln6GyS95duD9oM7rMFSAccnGUyRZIPnJRpsfdOy9tDuzBWrcwdeyMpu_qFiSY6JkL9da9mEvRxx9HqD6mNm7B8QjfE5LB4uCG96XKZxPr8yjKGJvE4IL2YZ3ywYtakH6Es91Bw/s320/Claudio+Francesco+Beaumont+-+The+Resurrection+of+the+dead.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/60-21.htm">All of Israel has a share in the world to come</a>. However, the following don't have this share: one who says that there is no reference to the Resurrection of the Dead in the Torah; one who says that the Torah is not from Heaven; and one who disparages Torah scholars, which leads him to deny the existence of God. Other sources also enumerate multiple other transgressions, which, if performed habitually, lead one to lose his share in the World to Come, but they can be derived from the list above.<br />
<br />
Rabban Gamliel gave this source for the Resurrection of the Dead in the Torah: God saying to Moses, "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/31-16.htm">Behold, you will lie with your forefathers and rise</a>." <br />
<br />
Art: The Resurrection of the Dead by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Claudio Francesco Beaumont</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/91.txt
<a id="src-00128"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/91.txt`

Sanhedrin 91 - Defense Against the Canaanites Who Wanted Israel Back
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgrznGQbqON7s5pow-yVAXI9mLlJ5VUYVp4CLBYMFOeH69sA7a_6KIYI8vL4juhxgTOxGpGdeTIZz5UvIiPwn75qicLAAbs_oIMhY8eHlo0pfgvSZKr85SzoIZKbACNtmcniRDMw3kQZKw/s1600/Ilya+Repin+-+Hunchback.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgrznGQbqON7s5pow-yVAXI9mLlJ5VUYVp4CLBYMFOeH69sA7a_6KIYI8vL4juhxgTOxGpGdeTIZz5UvIiPwn75qicLAAbs_oIMhY8eHlo0pfgvSZKr85SzoIZKbACNtmcniRDMw3kQZKw/s320/Ilya+Repin+-+Hunchback.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Geviha ben Pesisa was a hunchbacked Sage. A certain disputant said to him, "Woe to you, O sinners, for you say that the dead will live. Even the living eventually die, so how can the dead come back to life?" Geviha answered, "Woe to <i>you,</i> O sinners! If the non-existent (baby before it is born) come to life, then isn't it all the more possible that one who once lived will live again?" The disputant retorted, "You dare call me (and all of us) sinners? If I arise, I will kick you so hard that I will straighten out your hump!" Geviha said to him, "If you do that, you will be called a skilled doctor and command a large fee."<br />
<br />
The Girgashites were descendants of Canaan who moved to Africa when the Jews conquered Israel. They came back with Alexander the Great to demand the land back. Geviha ben Pesisa said to the Sages, "Let me answer. If I lose, tell them I am just a commoner, so their victory means nothing. If I win, say that the Torah of Moses defeated them." The Girgashites then claimed the Land, based on the fact that the Jews took "<a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/34-2.htm">the Land of Canaan according to its borders</a>." <br />
<br />
Geviha asked them, "From where do you bring the proof?" They said, "From the Torah." He said, I will also bring the proof from the Torah, "<a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/9-25.htm">Accursed is Canaan, a slave of slaves shall he be to his brothers</a>." If a slave acquired property, to whom belongs the slave and the property? Certainly to his master! So the Land of Canaan belongs to us, the descendants of Shem, and not only that, but all your fields too. They thought for three days but found no answer. They then ran away and left their sown fields, which was great because that year was Shmita when work in the field was forbidden.<br />
<br />
Art: Hunchback by Ilya Repin<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/92.txt
<a id="src-00129"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/92.txt`

Sanhedrin 92 - The Resurrection of the Dead
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJNmRqOoE4D1zeSXxbZVSxp9IdjcddOUhXn683M31xFcqgB1uaXkgcfu6mxOho9nLFKR7LznGx6FYs1Ve_c2vjrAuaAKi7N1G3HNAujQNnC_T0rQ_dRcowB-z6thyA1Alj1Pd3mAjEMe0/s1600/Michelangelo+Buonarroti+-+Ezekiel.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJNmRqOoE4D1zeSXxbZVSxp9IdjcddOUhXn683M31xFcqgB1uaXkgcfu6mxOho9nLFKR7LznGx6FYs1Ve_c2vjrAuaAKi7N1G3HNAujQNnC_T0rQ_dRcowB-z6thyA1Alj1Pd3mAjEMe0/s320/Michelangelo+Buonarroti+-+Ezekiel.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Of the many sources in the Scripture, this one does not admit a figurative explanation, "<a href="http://bible.cc/daniel/12-2.htm">And many of those who sleep in the dusty earth shall awaken; these for everlasting life, and these for shame</a>." <br />
<br />
Said Rabbi Elazar, "If a person has understanding, it is as if the Temple were built in his days, for <a href="http://bible.cc/1_samuel/2-3.htm">understanding is mentioned between the two names of God</a>, and <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/15-17.htm">so is the Temple</a>."<br />
<br /><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">Regarding the&nbsp;<a href="" target="_blank">dead whom prophet Ezekiel resurrected</a>, there are many opinions: they stood on their feet, uttered a song, then died; it is a parable; they went to Israel, married wives, and fathered sons and daughters, and Rabbi Yehudah ben Beteira was one of their descendants.</span><br />
<br />
Regarding who they were, there are many opinions: that they were from the tribe of Ephraim, who left Egypt too early and were killed; they were people who denied the Resurrection of the Dead; these were people who covered the entire Temple with pictures of various idols.<br />
<br />
Art: Ezekiel by Michelangelo Buonarroti</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/93.txt
<a id="src-00130"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/93.txt`

Sanhedrin 93 - Daniel, Chananyah, Mishael, and Azariyah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjsSMpOgdSN8GH41yTlU3X4xGwJYlC2lDQg96qhGLDvPOs50UK412Z1qyKetXBQ7DpBTVRfYLAypIBC6HiyzV_U7t4hr3NQYV24nTZuFjn3JX9JYnSXfJnh5g2Gqj-AZSzk-dqZrBt8tTg/s1600/Maximilien+Luce+-+Tall+Furnaces.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjsSMpOgdSN8GH41yTlU3X4xGwJYlC2lDQg96qhGLDvPOs50UK412Z1qyKetXBQ7DpBTVRfYLAypIBC6HiyzV_U7t4hr3NQYV24nTZuFjn3JX9JYnSXfJnh5g2Gqj-AZSzk-dqZrBt8tTg/s320/Maximilien+Luce+-+Tall+Furnaces.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Chananyah, Mishael, and Azaryah refused Nebuchadnezzar's demand to bow down to an idol and were thrown into a fiery furnace. Six miracles occurred for them. The furnace rose to ground level, the walls were breached, and the foundation caved in so everyone could see them unscathed inside the fire. The golden image on top of it was overturned on its face; the elite Nebuchadnezzar guards were burned by the furnace's fire, and Ezekiel resurrected the dead in the plain of Dura.<br />
<br />
When they emerged from the fiery furnace unscathed, all the nations of the world came and struck the enemies of Israel (a euphemism for the Jews themselves) on the faces, saying to them, "You have such a powerful God, and yet you submit to Nebuchadnezzar's threat and bow to the idol?!" Chananyah, Mishael, and Azaryah immediately declared, "<a href="http://bible.cc/daniel/9-7.htm">Yours, O Lord, is the righteousness, and ours is the shamefacedness as of this day</a>."<br />
<br />
Art: Tall Furnaces by Maximilien Luce
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/94.txt
<a id="src-00131"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/94.txt`

Sanhedrin 94 - Chizkiah and Sancheiriv
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgpjBL8-b5-FZaoUVd4tgMQVG4-Km8SLRgpeEgJDALhw0Xj_VNH2qCUOlVe_wTH75pAdwLwJtR9UNJ6mljBruRl9N5NeN2stHkkNOHS6SVrpgmAYHrcjjiXuAkJuszlFv4OqdSLkNYNYvA/s1600/Godfried+Schalcken+-+A+woman+reading+by+candlelight.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgpjBL8-b5-FZaoUVd4tgMQVG4-Km8SLRgpeEgJDALhw0Xj_VNH2qCUOlVe_wTH75pAdwLwJtR9UNJ6mljBruRl9N5NeN2stHkkNOHS6SVrpgmAYHrcjjiXuAkJuszlFv4OqdSLkNYNYvA/s320/Godfried+Schalcken+-+A+woman+reading+by+candlelight.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Why is Chizkiah called by this name? Because he strengthened (Chizek) the heart of Israel toward their Father in Heaven. What did he do? He thrust a sword near the entrance to the study hall and said, "Whoever does not engage in Torah study will be pierced by this sword." He then supplied the oil to light the study halls. They searched all of Israel and could not find one unlearned person who was not well-versed in the Torah. Then, they searched within the territory of Judah and could not find even a young boy or girl, man or woman, who was not well-versed in the most intricate laws of ritual purity. In this generation, people neglected their most valuable land because of the Torah study.<br />
<br />
Sancheiriv understood <a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/8-7.htm">the prophecy of Isaiah</a> as referring to him conquering Jerusalem. His army then made a ten-day journey in one day. When Sancheiriv reached Jerusalem, they built an observation platform for him, and he was amazed at how small the city was compared to the ones he had previously conquered. He told his soldiers to go to sleep, rest, and be ready to take the walls of Jerusalem apart in the morning. During the night, <a href="http://bible.cc/2_kings/19-35.htm">the angel of God came and burned the soldiers</a>.<br />
<br />
Art: A woman reading by candlelight by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Godfried Schalcken</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/95.txt
<a id="src-00132"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/95.txt`

Sanhedrin 95 - David, Yishbi, and Avishai
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhnluHaRB_nSQLbQTtqX_6GmH2v3brlzJJrVx6QFDYnvOZHX4wPQBP0zzbbJ9krXunFHg9WS0alKiJ6oH4hs24WCPeaopLdSBSFIAW90OMENjbM0A5EPaAr1PJtoEcyzDkAZStrQBFYCw4/s1600/Frans+Snyders+-+Hunting+deer.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="201" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhnluHaRB_nSQLbQTtqX_6GmH2v3brlzJJrVx6QFDYnvOZHX4wPQBP0zzbbJ9krXunFHg9WS0alKiJ6oH4hs24WCPeaopLdSBSFIAW90OMENjbM0A5EPaAr1PJtoEcyzDkAZStrQBFYCw4/s400/Frans+Snyders+-+Hunting+deer.jpg" width="400" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">God told David, "Because of you the inhabitants of Nov were killed, Doeg lost his share in the World to Come, and Shaul with his three sons died. Do you choose for your descendants to be obliterated or for yourself to be delivered in the enemy's hand?" David chose the second, and Satan, disguised as a deer, drew the hunting David into the land of the Philistines, where Yishbi, the brother of Goliath, captured him.<br />
<br />
Yishbi put David under an olive press, but&nbsp;<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;"><a href="" target="_blank">the ground under him softened through a miracle</a></span>. Yishbi was still sitting on top.<br />
<br />
Avishai, one of David's officers, was preparing to shampoo his hair for Sabbath when he saw bloodstains in the water and understood that David was in danger. He reasoned, "One can not ride on the king's horse - but what about in the time of danger?" They told him that in times of danger, it is allowed. He then mounted David's mule and rode off. The road miraculously contracted under him.<br />
<br />
On the road, Avishai saw Orpah, the mother of Yishbi. She tried to kill him with a spindle, but he killed her instead. Seeing Avishai approach, Yishbi threw David up and prepared a spear to catch him. <a href="http://bible.cc/2_samuel/21-17.htm">Avishai said the name of God, and David hung in the air</a>. Avishai then asked David what he was doing there, and David explained that he had chosen punishment for himself. Avishai advised him to leave the punishment for his descendants and save himself from the trouble. Avishai then said another name of God, David came down, and the two started running away. Yishbi kept pursuing them until they told him, "Look at your mother in the grave," after which they killed him. <br />
<br />
After this David's soldiers swore to him, "<a href="http://bible.cc/2_samuel/21-17.htm">You must no longer go forth with us in battle, so that the light of Israel not be extinguished</a>."<br />
<br />
Art: Hunting Deer by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Frans Snyders</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/96.txt
<a id="src-00133"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/96.txt`

Sanhedrin 96 – Nebuchadnezzar, Nebuzaradan, and the Temple
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh6add3arCQOPTpdVo-pP5kZGoxGzqk1z_CwVPhiIb3ycsDciEr3v1SpJ-0y66dPkGCyvYUjS46l5sem-ucDXXL32h4XuNNU_4tmTCqKUr40XPkQDiATlZHI-iHAIxIUUplddn4tbOq6nU/s1600/BLAKE+William+-+Nebuchadnezzar.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh6add3arCQOPTpdVo-pP5kZGoxGzqk1z_CwVPhiIb3ycsDciEr3v1SpJ-0y66dPkGCyvYUjS46l5sem-ucDXXL32h4XuNNU_4tmTCqKUr40XPkQDiATlZHI-iHAIxIUUplddn4tbOq6nU/s320/BLAKE+William+-+Nebuchadnezzar.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When King Chizkiah was ill and then recovered, <a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/38-8.htm">the sun reversed its course</a>. The king of Assyria sent him a letter, "Greeting to Chizkiah, greetings to Jerusalem, greetings to the great God!" Nebuchadnezzar, the king's secretary, ran after the messenger to rewrite the letter in the correct order of greetings. He made three steps and was rewarded with the opportunity to destroy Jerusalem. People now make three steps at the end of prayer, asking to restore Jerusalem.<br />
<br />
<a href="http://bible.cc/jeremiah/52-12.htm">The general who came to destroy Jerusalem was Nebuzaradan</a>. He had three hundred mule-loads of iron-cutting axes, but one gate of Jerusalem swallowed them all. Nebuzaradan wanted to retreat, but the Heavenly voice told him, "You always wanted to destroy Jerusalem; now is your chance." With the wooden handle of a hatchet, he destroyed all the gates, conquered Jerusalem, and burned the Temple.<br />
<br />
Nebuzaradan saw the blood of Zechariah seething on the floor of the Temple. He asked, "What is it?" They told him, "Blood of offerings that spilled." He brought offerings, but it did not look the same. He then threatened torture, and they told him the truth: Zechariah prophesied about the destruction of the Temple, and they killed him, a Kohen, and a prophet. Nebuzaradan then brought the Sages and slew them over the blood, but it did not rest. He killed schoolchildren and Kohanim and kept killing until the count came to 940,000. He then called to Zechariah, "Do you want me to kill everyone?" - and the blood rested.<br />
<br />
Nebuzaradan then reasoned, "If for killing one person God punished them so, what will He do to that man (meaning himself)?" He then sent a will to his household and converted to Judaism.<br />
<br />
Art: Nebuchadnezzar by W</span><span style="font-size: large;">illiam Blake</span>

### content/sanhedrin/97.txt
<a id="src-00134"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/97.txt`

Sanhedrin 97 – The Generation at the Time of the Mashiach and The Age of the World
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSHNGgI5QAPioSd5Xo2Mh9c5owpFi4FEVUK_Kzz8aDfxNcost3w8QOUVI37-_mbVWDebaFTuJv7Zc7VXm9fn3c0mgjvXjSSHqDchE0n31NICOCPYl5FFw1eYqFlJzmGvyqLubFjij0ui0/s1600/Johannes+Christoffel+Vaarberg+-+A+Tavern+Interior.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSHNGgI5QAPioSd5Xo2Mh9c5owpFi4FEVUK_Kzz8aDfxNcost3w8QOUVI37-_mbVWDebaFTuJv7Zc7VXm9fn3c0mgjvXjSSHqDchE0n31NICOCPYl5FFw1eYqFlJzmGvyqLubFjij0ui0/s320/Johannes+Christoffel+Vaarberg+-+A+Tavern+Interior.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">In the generation when the son of David (Mashiach) will come, the meeting place of the scholars will be used for licentiousness, the wisdom of the scholars will decay, those who fear sin will be despised, and the face of the generation will be like the face of a dog. The truth will be absent, as in "<a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/59-15.htm">And the truth will be absent, and he that turns away from evil will become foolish</a>.” <br />
<br />Rabbi Meir Abulafia (c. 1170 – 1244, Burgos, Spain), in his book “Yad Ramah,” remarks: “I am in wonderment! According to these signs, why has the son of David not come in this generation of ours?”<br />
<br />But how can we say the truth will be absent when there is a promise that the Jewish people will never be devoid of Torah scholars devoted to truth? - Truth will be divided into many small groups, each with its own truth, so it will be tough to find.<br />
<br />
The world is destined to exist for six thousand years; the first two thousand were of nothingness, without the Torah, the second two thousand were of Torah, and the third two thousand are the days of the Messiah. <a href="http://www.lulu.com/product/file-download/the-age-of-the-universe---a-torah-true-perspective/3097384">This, however, is only talking about the last 7-year cycle, in which we find ourselves, but according to one estimate in Kabbalah, we are at the end of sixth Shmita, at  42,000 years divine years, which translates into 15 billion human years</a>.<br />
<br />
There are many calculations of the world's end, most of which have already passed. <br />
<br />
Art: A Tavern Interior by Johannes Christoffel Vaarberg
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/98.txt
<a id="src-00135"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/98.txt`

Sanhedrin 98 – The Signs of the Coming of the Mashiach
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0OfV_l4vkGkaLNBl12aCzoy4HJk4xxe_2UxMpsypPLKGQYK7_HWfS5JvDDIQXvyLhBn6jvB7K4gwtOfz9QS_Zu2j8NSdGoNHYNuYmorxSJw9jvpW2DGvx2N0dX6SOprOgkS6AIMxchqQ/s1600/Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot+-+The+Donkey.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0OfV_l4vkGkaLNBl12aCzoy4HJk4xxe_2UxMpsypPLKGQYK7_HWfS5JvDDIQXvyLhBn6jvB7K4gwtOfz9QS_Zu2j8NSdGoNHYNuYmorxSJw9jvpW2DGvx2N0dX6SOprOgkS6AIMxchqQ/s320/Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot+-+The+Donkey.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Said Rabbi Abba;- There is no more unambiguous indication of the "End" than this: "<a href="http://bible.cc/ezekiel/36-8.htm">But you, O mountains of Israel, you shall shoot forth your branches and bear your fruit for My people Israel</a>," that is, the Land of Israel will yield fruit in abundance shortly before the redemption.<br />
<br />
In the generation of the Messiah, there will be denunciation among the Torah scholars.<br />
<br />
The Messiah will come to the wholly virtuous or sinful generation. If a person is somewhat virtuous, he is unlikely to repent because he focuses on his good attributes.  On the other hand, one who completely lacks virtue has no grounds for self-deception and thus is open to the realization that he must repent and merit God's redemption.<br />
<br />
The coming of the Messiah will be preceded by multiple troubles and tribulations. Ulla said, "May he come, but may I not see him," but Rav Yosef said, "May he come, and may I merit to sit in the shadow of his donkey's dung!"<br />
<br />
Art: The Donkey by Jean-Baptiste-Camille Corot
</span>

---

### content/sanhedrin/99.txt
<a id="src-00136"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sanhedrin/99.txt`

Sanhedrin 99 – Torah Study as the Meaning of Life
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjQeY4oMtc7sw3aIM0iN9eYohgBhhkPKLI62aC5IDipcYe6ZZM3iA1WqPWudCGMbZO1b-Qrly7muz7eH4MoFK1QrIFoPFn8STrga56ATOuosR2EvJ73F66NACWoWvU4RY4uYSsa1y8TIyQ/s1600/Mikolajus+Ciurlionis+-+Paradise.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjQeY4oMtc7sw3aIM0iN9eYohgBhhkPKLI62aC5IDipcYe6ZZM3iA1WqPWudCGMbZO1b-Qrly7muz7eH4MoFK1QrIFoPFn8STrga56ATOuosR2EvJ73F66NACWoWvU4RY4uYSsa1y8TIyQ/s320/Mikolajus+Ciurlionis+-+Paradise.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Messianic Era may last for <a href="http://bible.cc/psalms/95-10.htm">40 years</a>, <a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/23-15.htm">70 years</a>, <a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/15-13.htm">400 years</a>, or <a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/63-4.htm">365,000 years</a> – God's year.<br />
<br />
The books of Prophets contain many descriptions of life's utopian, idyllic state. All these refer only to the Messianic Era, but the reward of the World to Come is beyond human comprehension, and "<a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/64-4.htm">No eye except Yours, O God, has seen that which He will do for one who awaits Him</a>" – this is the opinion of Rabbi Yochanan. However, Shmuel says there will be no difference between this world and the Messianic Era, except that the Jews will be completely free from foreign dominion.<br />
<br />
What is the reward for constant Torah study? "<a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/16-26.htm">If a person toils in the study of Torah, the Torah will toil for him after death</a>" - asking God to keep giving him knowledge. <br />
<br />
Every <a href="http://bible.cc/job/5-7.htm">man is created for toil</a>, and it is <a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/16-26.htm">not physical labor but verbal toil</a>, specifically the study of Torah, because "<a href="http://bible.cc/joshua/1-8.htm">This Book of the Torah is not to leave your mouth</a>." Therefore, happy is one who merits to toil in Torah.<br />
<br />
Art: Paradise by Mikolajus Ciurlionis
</span>

---

### content/shabbat/10.txt
<a id="src-00137"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/10.txt`

Shabbat 10 – Giving a gift
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgH6cef4axtUxprwYzsjY2DZ6OlzP67EtiC_a-klOjmLs3s3ouUXva9jca0I7diO-Y8lh7wAdFrfB9v53KAPWd2NzWkbkzoHJLfbkhzAGQ-s37hnj2ykE6cj9hyphenhyphenCLCGmG8VejlWApS6RFZi/s1600/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Hunter's+Gift.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgH6cef4axtUxprwYzsjY2DZ6OlzP67EtiC_a-klOjmLs3s3ouUXva9jca0I7diO-Y8lh7wAdFrfB9v53KAPWd2NzWkbkzoHJLfbkhzAGQ-s37hnj2ykE6cj9hyphenhyphenCLCGmG8VejlWApS6RFZi/s320/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Hunter's+Gift.jpg" width="301" /></a>Rava bar Mechasya said in the name of Rav, “One who gives a gift to his friend has to inform him.” What is his source? When God gave Jews the Shabbat, He said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=31#P2431">To know that I am God who sanctifies them</a>.” The words “to know” mean this: God told Moses, “I have a wonderful present in My treasure house, and its name is Shabbat, go and tell them.” 
<br />
<br />
In the same vein, Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel taught that if one gives bread or other food to a child, he has to inform the child's parents. How does he do it? He rubs a little oil or rubs cosmetic paint on the child's eye – the parents will ask the child about it, and he will tell them about the present. Today, though, this may arouse suspicion, so it's better to rub some of the food that he gave.
<br />
<br />
However, Rav Chama taught that one should NOT tell about a gift, based on the phrase in the Torah, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=34#P2523">And Moses did NOT know that the skin of his face became radiant.</a>” How is this to be reconciled? – It's no problem really, Rav Chama meant a situation where the gift will become revealed in any case, and that is why one does not have to inform about it. Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel was talking about a situation where the gift would otherwise not be revealed, and one has to tell about it, to increased the amount of good feelings and friendship among people.
<br />
<br />
However, Shabbat is known – it is a good day of rest, so why did God ask Moses to inform about it? – While it is true that the day itself is known for its rest, the reward for it in the future world is not known, and that is why God had to tell about it.
<br />
<br />
Art: Gabriel Metsu - The Hunter's Gift

---

### content/shabbat/101.txt
<a id="src-00139"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/101.txt`

Shabbat 101 – Ships in a sea
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgr_6kVcDtgnKQm6xXtgAKTUro1lVT5at_UsiLJ3r6njxJPw04raqidEbh00uOGq2AvNu9Z_sjRD8Stfi3gbVs1S4iauq1ENiKZUcE_owMa-Sz2WXEzqLX5DUyWCHd5BozHpA-E6aDjkiVz/s1600/Andries+Van+Eertvelt+-+Two+Ships+at+Anchor.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="207" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgr_6kVcDtgnKQm6xXtgAKTUro1lVT5at_UsiLJ3r6njxJPw04raqidEbh00uOGq2AvNu9Z_sjRD8Stfi3gbVs1S4iauq1ENiKZUcE_owMa-Sz2WXEzqLX5DUyWCHd5BozHpA-E6aDjkiVz/s320/Andries+Van+Eertvelt+-+Two+Ships+at+Anchor.jpg" width="320" /></a>If on Shabbat on throws an object from the sea to the dry land or from the dry land to the sea, he is exempt from bringing a sacrifice. As usual, “exempt” means that the Sages prohibited it, to put him farther away from a transgression, but this is not a real violation. But why would this be prohibited? The sea is not a public area where many people walk!? – Nevertheless, it is similar to a public area in the vastness of its expanse. Such areas are called “karmelit,” as <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/10/shabbat-7-special-area-called-karmelit.html">we discussed before</a>, and carrying there is prohibited.
<br />
<br />
Likewise, he is prohibited from carrying from a ship to the land, and even from a ship to a ship. However, if two ships are tied together, then carrying between them on Shabbat is permitted, because both represent private areas. If they become untied, then carrying between them is again prohibited, even if they are still together – because it is very likely that in the near future that will separate.
<br />
<br />
Art: Andries Van Eertvelt - Two Ships at Anchor

---

### content/shabbat/102.txt
<a id="src-00140"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/102.txt`

Shabbat 102 – Building
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhRPXTw_kvmb7nFJyj1f42d2Yq7nKY7rHhU5B1p82PnONAIEEkqtd-Vbo8i_rHD5KeBGLUL7y5kzb31DTPFuN3iiqlQcS6mgBu_gvgQP44yU0quXUkVkrmCTmc1fd-wi1_zSUJNOR9qucWH/s1600/Winslow+Homer+-+Dog+on+a+Log.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="220" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhRPXTw_kvmb7nFJyj1f42d2Yq7nKY7rHhU5B1p82PnONAIEEkqtd-Vbo8i_rHD5KeBGLUL7y5kzb31DTPFuN3iiqlQcS6mgBu_gvgQP44yU0quXUkVkrmCTmc1fd-wi1_zSUJNOR9qucWH/s320/Winslow+Homer+-+Dog+on+a+Log.jpg" width="320" /></a>If one threw an object on Shabbat but, while the object was still in the air, remembered that it was in fact Shabbat, and the dog ate it in mid-flight, he does not bring a sacrifice – because the sacrifice is only brought when the violation is done while forgetting about Shabbat, from the beginning to the end.
<br />
<br />
This rule seems to have two cases mixed up! – Rav Ashi explained that indeed, there is a missing part in this ruling, and in the corrected version there are three cases: throwing the object that a dog ate (no sacrifice), remembering about Shabbat in midair (no sacrifice), and immediately forgetting about Shabbat (there is a sacrifice and it helps).
<br />
<br />
If so, why still teach the old ruling and not the corrected one? That is because each such ruling has a spiritual secret in it, and it also has a practical application. The spiritual secret is the more important one, so when they come into conflict, the ruling is taught according to it, at the expense of the practical application, which has then to be amended.
<br />
<br />
How much does one have to build on Shabbat to be liable? – Any amount. How can any amount of building be useful? – A poor may build a small hole to keep is money in it. Corresponding to this, they would store needles in the Temple's curtain. – No, that's a bad example, because we have a Temple rule: “There is no show of poverty in the place of opulence." Rather, a poor may want to fix a very small hole. And what would be a similar labor in the Temple? – They would fix a small hole in a beam that a worm has eaten – because all prohibited Shabbat work has its source in the building of the Temple.
<br />
<br />
Art: Winslow Homer - Dog on a Log

---

### content/shabbat/103.txt
<a id="src-00141"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/103.txt`

Shabbat 103 – One writes two letters
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgU9G4j638RTr_SsuF7wadGFHebDNR8WljZ4jbbpUaixjbG5SR1fZnvVfzrRYld0VCu7kFCBc5oVfLejZY629CBMDp2YTwF-GPMvF6Ep9Ig192zeBOzURCZagQ2ebJcxwZm58_a5GcEzQs4/s1600/Gerard+Ter+Borch+-+Lady+Reading+a+Letter.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgU9G4j638RTr_SsuF7wadGFHebDNR8WljZ4jbbpUaixjbG5SR1fZnvVfzrRYld0VCu7kFCBc5oVfLejZY629CBMDp2YTwF-GPMvF6Ep9Ig192zeBOzURCZagQ2ebJcxwZm58_a5GcEzQs4/s320/Gerard+Ter+Borch+-+Lady+Reading+a+Letter.jpg" width="243" /></a>When one plows on Shabbat, he is liable for any amount of plowing. Although with sowing there are amounts required for violation, such as two seeds – this is because people usually won't trouble themselves to sow one seed. However, with plowing, any amount of preparing the earth is significant.
<br />
<br />
If one is cutting branches from a live tree, then if he is doing it to improve the tree – any amount of cutting is significant. However, if his purpose is to collect firewood, he is liable once he collects enough to cook a “light egg” – that is, an egg of a chicken, which is the easiest to cook.
<br />
<br />
If one writes two letters, whether with his right hand or left hand, in any language, he is liable. Rabbi Yose say that the prohibition extends even further, and that any two useful marks, not letters, already make one liable. Others say that on the contrary, the two letters must be part of a word. Another question arises when one intended to write a long word, like Daniel, and stopped after writing the first two letters, dalet and nun, thus forming the word “Dan.” Even though he did not complete his intent (the usual condition in Shabbat violations) , Rabbi Yehudah holds him liable.
<br />
<br />
Art: Gerard Ter Borch - Lady Reading a Letter

---

### content/shabbat/104.txt
<a id="src-00142"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/104.txt`

Shabbat 104 – Nonpunishable Shabbat writing 
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIvIOowzqGwjwzoECLSSiixD56fUv6Wnv-w7rNFsPeboSPN-XJPgRIo3Q5g8ZuTLpk3rwGN05gZ40_vce9iuNJ-Jx8IO6UXskaBZvNjOkDxFEiKTFmtPvhz1lrjJj457XLsSds7JQOelyW/s1600/Alexei+Kondratyevich+Savrasov+-+Sea+of+Mud.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="249" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIvIOowzqGwjwzoECLSSiixD56fUv6Wnv-w7rNFsPeboSPN-XJPgRIo3Q5g8ZuTLpk3rwGN05gZ40_vce9iuNJ-Jx8IO6UXskaBZvNjOkDxFEiKTFmtPvhz1lrjJj457XLsSds7JQOelyW/s320/Alexei+Kondratyevich+Savrasov+-+Sea+of+Mud.jpg" width="320" /></a>The Sages told to Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi that young students came to the study hall and are expounding the secrets of the alphabet. And what was their wisdom? They said that “aleph”, “beth” means “alaph binah” - learn insight. “Gimel,” “dalet” stands for “Gemol dalim” – aid the  needy. They continued to expound the shape of every letter, and of every letter pair, going forward, and backward, and even combing the letter by using the “first letter – last letter method.” Why do letters of “falsehood,” “sheker” are close together in the alphabet? – Because falsehoods are common. And why the letters of “truth” - “emet” are far apart? – Because truth is rare. Why the letters of “emet – truth” stand on a solid foundation? Because in end truth will stand. Correspondingly, the letters of “falsehood – sheker” all stand on one leg (one point touching the foundation) to indicate that in the end falsehood will not endure.
<br />
<br />
When is one not liable for writing on Shabbat? – When his writing will not endure. For example, if he wrote with fruit juice, which will dry out, or he wrote in the mud or on dust. He is also not liable if he wrote in an unusual way: by turning his hand backward, by holding the pen with his mouth or with his elbow – because people don't normally write this way.
<br />
<br />
Art: Alexei Kondratyevich Savrasov - Sea of Mud

---

### content/shabbat/105.txt
<a id="src-00143"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/105.txt`

Shabbat 105 – Abbreviations
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgjDWphg-O3-pcO7Pew3gLej9CIBEMcLQGk_c0_GeAcffXGLgIDEd7ABCvtLin3xbagl5QA7bxOzuZ07Umh_LYc465NLChnV0Jou9_UG_lFUGmTQ_-Qf28-kpmZjsoupQlW8lPVhOmKlDSI/s1600/Francisco+De+Zurbaran+-+Hercules+Tearing+the+Burning+Robe.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="259" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgjDWphg-O3-pcO7Pew3gLej9CIBEMcLQGk_c0_GeAcffXGLgIDEd7ABCvtLin3xbagl5QA7bxOzuZ07Umh_LYc465NLChnV0Jou9_UG_lFUGmTQ_-Qf28-kpmZjsoupQlW8lPVhOmKlDSI/s320/Francisco+De+Zurbaran+-+Hercules+Tearing+the+Burning+Robe.jpg" width="320" /></a>Abbreviations are used in many places in the text of the Torah. For example, in the First Commandment, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=20#P2054">I am God your Lord</a>” the word “I” has a somewhat unusual long form, “Anochi”. This stands for “Ana nafshi ketivat yahavit” and means “I Myself wrote and gave the Torah.”
<br />
<br />
If one tears his clothing in anger or for a dead, he is acting destructively, and for destructive acts one is not liable for Shabbat violation. But if he destroys in order to repair, then he is indeed liable. What is the minimal measure of destruction in this case? – The same as would be for repair.
<br />
<br />
However, we learned in another place that one is liable for tearing on Shabbat!? – This is talking about his own dead, for whom he is obligated to rend his clothes. This is also true if a Sage dies, for them everybody is obligated to mourn.
<br />
<br />
Rav Avin said that if he tears to cool his anger, then he has achieved a constructive purpose and should be liable for it on Shabbat. But is such behavior even allowed? One should never get angry, and freely venting one's anger is tantamount to subjugating oneself to its power, where one's soul burns out!? – True! What Rav Avin meant is that one only pretends to be angry, to show his displeasure with specific people.
<br />
<br />
Art: Francisco De Zurbaran - Hercules Tearing the Burning Robe

---

### content/shabbat/106.txt
<a id="src-00144"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/106.txt`

Shabbat 106 – Traps
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0Rv0AQ7iXhQGLE8sla3NO39Kv1Zp3_7oT7jb54Rda8PZMoz8fl-hC16TciI2kFBy7ydIrwAxgwh8UMTZEdvrPiQF4xOfnfXQITpdqmRSax-kbV3U_c_r6QKksyw_zgwiBMXVps4NMZRTs/s1600/Christian+Krohg+-+Young+Woman+on+a+Bench.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0Rv0AQ7iXhQGLE8sla3NO39Kv1Zp3_7oT7jb54Rda8PZMoz8fl-hC16TciI2kFBy7ydIrwAxgwh8UMTZEdvrPiQF4xOfnfXQITpdqmRSax-kbV3U_c_r6QKksyw_zgwiBMXVps4NMZRTs/s320/Christian+Krohg+-+Young+Woman+on+a+Bench.jpg" width="297" /></a></div>
<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/01/shabbat-105-abbreviations.html">Earlier we learned</a> that for doing destructive acts on Shabbat one is not liable. However, Rabbi Shimon finds two exceptions to this: wounding a person or burning something. Here one is liable for Shabbat violation. Why? After all, Rabbi Shimon is the one who permits unintended violations, such as dragging a bench on the ground, even though he may dig a ditch! Rabbi Shimon will tell you that since the Torah had to allow circumcision on Shabbat, this shows us that normally making a wound is prohibited. Then what about our previous learning that ALL destructive acts are not a Torah violation? – That is the opinion of Rabbi Yehudah. And what is the basis for it? He said that circumcision is a constructive act of rectifying the child.
<br />
<br />
Trapping an animal constitutes hunting, and that is prohibited on Shabbat. But what is trapping?&nbsp;–&nbsp;If one drives a bird into a cage or a deer into courtyard – in other words, if he makes the animal sufficiently trapped so that he can catch it in one attempt. A swallow bird is an exception: it loves freedom so much that even after being trapped in a small enclosure it will not becomes submissive, but will try to fly away instead. Therefore, a smaller than usual enclosure would make it trapped.
<br />
<br />
Art: Christian Krohg - Young Woman on a Bench

---

### content/shabbat/107.txt
<a id="src-00145"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/107.txt`

Shabbat 107 – Two people catch a deer
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjYWkrEMZ21dYgLhdDCBC62KgGbBNNM3leua4vdLSJo5Jc7iCgez6-NeuoXayV5V8laJsiiNOGjFhOh9hV2RrO6tfehyphenhyphen-BeQSMJz2YgToMiM3hIl14ha8-gpRQ1ZMrrrmiSbm09LNvEeAlS/s1600/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Two+Deer+In+A+Forest+Glade.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="264" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjYWkrEMZ21dYgLhdDCBC62KgGbBNNM3leua4vdLSJo5Jc7iCgez6-NeuoXayV5V8laJsiiNOGjFhOh9hV2RrO6tfehyphenhyphen-BeQSMJz2YgToMiM3hIl14ha8-gpRQ1ZMrrrmiSbm09LNvEeAlS/s320/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Two+Deer+In+A+Forest+Glade.jpg" width="320" /></a>If a deer was inside the house, and a person sat in the doorway without completely blocking it, so that the deer can get out, that person is not liable for trapping the deer on Shabbat. However, if a second person sat in that door and made the exit completely blocked, the second one is liable. The first one is not, because he did nothing.
<br />
<br />
On the other hand, if a person sat in the door and completely blocked it, and then the second one came and sat there also, then, even if the first person leaves and the second one is the one who is blocking the door now – only the first one is liable, because he effected trapping, while the second one again is doing nothing at all.
<br />
<br />
<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/01/eight-reptiles.html">The eight reptiles mentioned by the Torah</a> are different from other crawling creatures: if one bruises one of them (such as a mouse) on Shabbat, he is liable, but for others (like a snake), he is not. The difference is that a mouse has thicker hide, and a bruise leads to blood accumulation, which is taking away a life, albeit in a small measure. The hide of other reptiles is soft, akin to skin, and the reddening caused by a minor bruise soon dissipates. 
<br />
<br />
One is also liable to trapping one of the eight reptiles, because people do normally catch them, for various reasons.
<br />
<br />
Art: Rosa Bonheur - Two Deer In A Forest Glade

---

### content/shabbat/108.txt
<a id="src-00146"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/108.txt`

Shabbat 108 – Writing on fish skin
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhXGTYDIfssX3Rz8s_tOv97jqRAKEAXhCXsjznk6VFvoSPNrOKYbezdb9uifFftphk3WTWLSqU_sheyVzKwnPRHfFWv3s1SM3wqc1F6ote-Qut6IxTpKax6LfT4LGhtnB69z3hhhyphenhyphenmRbCSh/s1600/Jacob+Toorenvliet+-+A+Fish+Seller.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="252" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhXGTYDIfssX3Rz8s_tOv97jqRAKEAXhCXsjznk6VFvoSPNrOKYbezdb9uifFftphk3WTWLSqU_sheyVzKwnPRHfFWv3s1SM3wqc1F6ote-Qut6IxTpKax6LfT4LGhtnB69z3hhhyphenhyphenmRbCSh/s320/Jacob+Toorenvliet+-+A+Fish+Seller.jpg" width="320" /></a>Rav Huna said, “One can write tefillin on the skin of a kosher bird.” Rav asked asked, “What is Rav Huna teaching us? That bird skins qualify as hides? – <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/01/shabbat-107-two-people-catch-deer.html">We know that</a>! One who bruises a bird on Shabbat is liable, and that can only be because birds have hides, under which the blood collects.” His student Abaye told him, “Actually, Rav Huna is teaching us a lot. Since birds skins are perforated with weathers, we might have thought that this makes them invalid for writing a tefillin, and he teaches us otherwise.”
<br />
<br />
Mar bar Ravina asked of Rav Nachman, “Can one write tefillin on the skin of a kosher fish?” Rav Nachman answered, “When Elijah the prophet comes, he will tell us.” What kind of answer is this? We see ourselves that fish do have skin. Furthermore, we know the teaching that the skin and the bones of a fish accept ritual impurity of a corpse in the house, so of course they have skin! – He meant, is that skin valid. Does the stench completely depart from it, or perhaps it never does? This is one of the unclear facts that Elijah has the authority to reveal, and that's why we must wait for him.
<br />
<br />
Art: Jacob Toorenvliet - A Fish Seller

---

### content/shabbat/109.txt
<a id="src-00147"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/109.txt`

Shabbat 109 – Healing on Shabbat
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiCjG9g6VlqLA9ddNhTeHumoek8_2Tg6TpC0RqfKlLPB6lUbiIzOqywOv8BaXsnrk9ct0ufBRLVrTKD5W6IbkJ-euxs3I3P28Te1PTwJ9a7md3sloBsYcs19dVJfDRAamgggfc69SlRuqOa/s1600/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Sick+Child.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiCjG9g6VlqLA9ddNhTeHumoek8_2Tg6TpC0RqfKlLPB6lUbiIzOqywOv8BaXsnrk9ct0ufBRLVrTKD5W6IbkJ-euxs3I3P28Te1PTwJ9a7md3sloBsYcs19dVJfDRAamgggfc69SlRuqOa/s320/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Sick+Child.jpg" width="260" /></a>One may not prepare brine (salt water for pickling) in large quantities on Shabbat, because he is in fact preparing for the weekdays after Shabbat. However, one may prepare a small quantity that will be consumed that day. Rabbi Yose challenged this: “Is brine not the same, whether in large or in small quantities? If you have a law like this one, then people will say that a small amount of work on Shabbat is permitted, and only a large amount is forbidden. Rather, all brine is forbidden to be made on Shabbat, unless one first adds oil either to water or to salt – and in this way he makes a distinction and a reminder that it is Shabbat.”
<br />
<br />
Generally it is prohibited to effect cure of minor diseases on Shabbat. The Sages accepted this decree due to the possibility that one may come to grind medicine on Shabbat, which would definitely be prohibited. However, if he eats foods that have therapeutic effect, but that are generally eaten also by healthy people, then it is not obvious that he does it for healing, and it is allowed.
<br />
<br />
Art: Gabriel Metsu - The Sick Child

---

### content/shabbat/11.txt
<a id="src-00148"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/11.txt`

Shabbat 11 – Friday afternoon
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjlQDhgZW6ZTpL-y1gp5gXDfwBwWkgaQVli_BfS0FUx68SlrbO9-SKryyxiMkLi_lqV4c3DCclx8jR4B6eUTl4JZMvlnEZ0jsWF6d1bvGStt8KyI3gW_-OqdMCO42knJzXCPYOjBHJxi7m/s1600/Quiringh+Gerritsz.+van+Brekelenkam+-+The+Tailor's+Workshop.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjlQDhgZW6ZTpL-y1gp5gXDfwBwWkgaQVli_BfS0FUx68SlrbO9-SKryyxiMkLi_lqV4c3DCclx8jR4B6eUTl4JZMvlnEZ0jsWF6d1bvGStt8KyI3gW_-OqdMCO42knJzXCPYOjBHJxi7m/s320/Quiringh+Gerritsz.+van+Brekelenkam+-+The+Tailor's+Workshop.jpg" width="259" /></a></div>
On Friday afternoon close to sundown, a tailor should not go out into the street with his needle, lest he forget that has it, and come to carry it four steps in the street, when it is already dark, which would be a Shabbat violation. Similarly, a scribe should not go out with his pen. Even though a pen is much larger than a needle, he still might forget that he is carrying it, and this applies even to objects larger than a needle.
<br />
<br />
Why are the above rules true? A tailor usually carries his needle pinned to his clothing; this is an uncommon manner of carrying, and as such it is not prohibited by the Torah, but only by the decree of the Sages. A further precaution of not carrying it while it is still Friday would constitute a decree to protect another decree, and that is usually not done!? We have to admit that he is carrying it in his hand. 
<br />
<br />
But we learned a clear rule, that a tailor should not go out of Friday afternoon with a needle pinned to his garment! – That is talking on Shabbat itself. But we learned yet another rule, that he should not go out with a needle pinned to his garment on Friday afternoon!? – We have to admit that this rule is not universal, but that it is only the opinion of Rabbi Yehudah, who says that for a craftsman the way of carrying common in his profession is in fact prohibited by the Torah on Shabbat. 
<br />
<br />
Indeed, we learned the following rule in the name of Rabbi Yehudah: “A carpenter may not go out with his ruler behind his ear, nor a money-changer with a dinar behind his ear” – which proves our point.
<br />
<br />
Art: Quiringh Gerritsz. van Brekelenkam - The Tailor's Workshop

---

### content/shabbat/110.txt
<a id="src-00149"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/110.txt`

Shabbat 110 – Water left uncovered
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjV0tXTiRCU4hvY2jCIMhEEgrHqccCSxtbAzMDFne3pSX0jGDMaUetasdZedBQaq3wl5DqzfFClfzcS6QKAiOjoaj3TCgsFNwqmUqj7wRlKTBOjJDeHVgpPraneduh1aMVACch4-5Di93bP/s1600/William+Oliver+-+A+snake+in+the+grass.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjV0tXTiRCU4hvY2jCIMhEEgrHqccCSxtbAzMDFne3pSX0jGDMaUetasdZedBQaq3wl5DqzfFClfzcS6QKAiOjoaj3TCgsFNwqmUqj7wRlKTBOjJDeHVgpPraneduh1aMVACch4-5Di93bP/s320/William+Oliver+-+A+snake+in+the+grass.jpg" width="144" /></a>In Babylon, where snakes were abundant, there was a danger that water left uncovered might have been drunk by a snake, who could leave there its poison. For this reason, the Sages prohibited drinking any water that was left uncovered for enough time that the snake hiding behind the vessel might have appeared and drunk from. In other times and at other places this law should not apply, but it has mystical connotations, and is discussed often in the Talmud.
<br />
<br />
What is a cure for a one who drank water left uncovered? – It is made of a tree used for shepherd's staff. If one does not have it, he should take five roses and five cups of beer, and boil them together. A certain man drank uncovered water. The mother of Rav Achadvoi cooked roses in beer and made him drink it in a hot oven, and poison came out of him like a green leaf of a palm branch.<br />
<br />
Alternatively, they should bring a sweet <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etrog">etrog</a>, carve out a hole in it, fill it with honey, then cook it in burning coals, and he should eat it. The Talmud then discusses what to do when one swallows a snake, or when a snake enters a woman.
<br />
<br />
Art: William Oliver - A snake in the grass

---

### content/shabbat/111.txt
<a id="src-00150"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/111.txt`

Shabbat 111 – Aches and pains
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj5DD-SiONv_Lkk6XPl1nre5durLp8eKbwkGQmEJBHNK8MttjtRNnvN5w37GbyedHbZpVEA6xAVzYYD1qAYytwXBMMYLqvpzIUZLDhziQmIUKVjIBmBPADVdA_M7OjPI6G3q7AaDb0oLWmh/s1600/Jan+Matejko+-+Stanczyk+Faking+a+Toothache.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj5DD-SiONv_Lkk6XPl1nre5durLp8eKbwkGQmEJBHNK8MttjtRNnvN5w37GbyedHbZpVEA6xAVzYYD1qAYytwXBMMYLqvpzIUZLDhziQmIUKVjIBmBPADVdA_M7OjPI6G3q7AaDb0oLWmh/s320/Jan+Matejko+-+Stanczyk+Faking+a+Toothache.jpg" width="256" /></a>Even if one has toothache, he should not sip vinegar (slightly spoiled wine). Vinegar strengthens the gums, and therefore sipping it, obviously done for health reasons, is forbidden. However, one can dip bread in vinegar while eating – since it was normal for people to dip their bread in vinegar – and if he is thereby cured, then he is cured.
<br />
<br />
If one feels pain in his loins, he should not smear them with wine or vinegar. These liquids are not commonly used for anointment, and thus his intention is obvious. However, he can apply oil to his skin, since normal, and not only sick people, do so. He should not use rose oil though unless he is a prince, that is, a son of a prominent or a rich person, because princes use rose oil even on weekdays, and it is not apparent that he is doing this only for therapeutic reason. Rabbi Shimon says that all Israel are considered princes, and thus they all can anoint themselves with rose oil on Shabbat.
<br />
<br />
Rava said: “The law is like Rabbi Shimon, but not for his reason.” What does he mean? Rava does not agree that all Israel are princes, but he permits using rose all in those locales where it is common – and in Rava's locale it was indeed common, so he allowed everyone to use rose oil on Shabbat.
<br />
<br />
Art: Jan Matejko - Stanczyk Faking a Toothache

---

### content/shabbat/112.txt
<a id="src-00151"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/112.txt`

Shabbat 112 – And these are the knots...
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZq3TBvq8TmboiOiPH3fEEOLF19_wL9ZP5q63Heb6mDwEY_C7Eq90C17Qx3Ks9N44EGcdo9AQ9DSSLhL44R1lI_JB4vRf_ahEAaJUYECrctRwr5iHsZTgOfomup-TJjaebYc1_uSZ_49pf/s1600/Camille+Pissarro+-+Young+Woman+Knotting+Her+Hair.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZq3TBvq8TmboiOiPH3fEEOLF19_wL9ZP5q63Heb6mDwEY_C7Eq90C17Qx3Ks9N44EGcdo9AQ9DSSLhL44R1lI_JB4vRf_ahEAaJUYECrctRwr5iHsZTgOfomup-TJjaebYc1_uSZ_49pf/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Young+Woman+Knotting+Her+Hair.jpg" width="227" /></a>In the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/12/shabbat-73-thirty-nine-complete-list.html">list of the thirty-nine types of work</a> that are prohibited on Shabbat we mentioned <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/12/shabbat-73-thirty-nine-complete-list.html">tying and untying a knot</a>. Now the Talmud comes to give examples of which knots are prohibited: the camel driver's knot and the sailor's knot. Both are meant to be remain tied forever, and they are thus considered permanent knots. However, if one ties a knot to these permanent knots, such as a leash to the camel, then this is meant for a week or two, but not for all time, and therefore it is not prohibited by the Torah. However, the Sages prohibited even such knots, because if they were allowed, people might come to tie even permanent knots.
<br />
<br />
On the other hand, knots that are tied and untied every day are not prohibited at all. For example, a woman may tie the opening of her chemise, string of a hat, or a girdle (a wide belt tied by laces), straps of a shoe or a sandal; additionally, one may tie leather bags of wine and oil, or a pot of meat, where a piece of cloth was sometimes tied to its top.
<br />
<br />
Since the rule is that any knot that is tied and untied daily is permitted, then why did the Talmud have to give us all of the last examples? – They are all necessary. For example, in the case of a woman's chemise we are talking about a chemise with two straps, where we might have thought that she will tie one of them permanently, and only tie and untie the other ones – the Talmud thus informs us that we are not concerned about this possibility but rather assume that she will tie and untie both daily.
<br />
<br />
Art: Camille Pissarro - Young Woman Knotting Her Hair

---

### content/shabbat/113.txt
<a id="src-00152"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/113.txt`

Shabbat 113 – Clothing
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiLgbM9tQg47R3cCmwcrYquiSXE1c0bF0Mxg5_d9Gc2m9-25erUi_B9onDvcou2MFxUIa6OYYzZcPSQPtCsK6aXJN0yDAmViuDcYjrJLOvT4Sv-urW8cWjUx53Ns5W0XxPffzRWVFpkPtCn/s1600/Nicolas+Poussin+-+Ruth+and+Boaz.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="229" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiLgbM9tQg47R3cCmwcrYquiSXE1c0bF0Mxg5_d9Gc2m9-25erUi_B9onDvcou2MFxUIa6OYYzZcPSQPtCsK6aXJN0yDAmViuDcYjrJLOvT4Sv-urW8cWjUx53Ns5W0XxPffzRWVFpkPtCn/s320/Nicolas+Poussin+-+Ruth+and+Boaz.jpg" width="320" /></a>If one needs to lift some water from a well, using a pail, he should not tie this pail with a regular rope, but should rather use a weaver's rope, or some other rope that he values so much that he will not leave it tied to the pail. 
<br />
<br />
Folding garments improves them in some measure, therefore, one may fold his garments multiple times if he plans to use them on the same day, but not if he plans to use them after Shabbat, because then he is preparing on Shabbat for weekdays. Likewise, one may make the beds any number of times during Shabbat, but not when Shabbat will end soon.
<br />
<br />
In general, on should honor Shabbat by wearing special clothing and by walking and talking in special ways, just as Isaiah said, “<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt1058.htm">If you restrain your feet and business, proclaim Shabbat a delight – then you will delight with God</a>.”<br />
<br />
When Naomi instructed Ruth for a night encounter with Boaz, she told her to <a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt2903.htm">bathe and anoint herself and don special garments</a>. Which garments were these? – Those of Shabbat. Ruth, however was wise, and the rule is “<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt2809.htm">Give to a wise, and she will become wiser</a>”, so she first went to the place of the meeting, and then prepared herself – so that the people meeting her would not suspect her of being a prostitute. Incidentally, why did Boaz ask the harvesters, “To whom does this young woman belong?” Boaz was the member of the Sanhedrin, the leading Sage of the generation, and a righteous person, and he did not inquire about every woman who came to glean his field!? – He noticed her wisdom in fulfilling precisely the laws of gleaning (two stalks belong to the poor, three should remain to the field owner) and her modestly in sitting down, not bending to pick up the stalks.
<br />
<br />
Art: Nicolas Poussin - Ruth and Boaz

---

### content/shabbat/114.txt
<a id="src-00153"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/114.txt`

Shabbat 114 – Clean garments
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgjpx1yb4p6erVZeBCBFFgq3v532q-VFwGB5ti9YUTHZG5AJHSxTDN86wT8SxgxvHkLqvM_8LdYWOTvGorUWdK0Uvq8jPmnfzTnHLKQY-ds60rSbl75VDnDEHCDQErjW9K-OQshtyB5dUMh/s1600/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+A+Pair+Of+Leather+Clogs.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="244" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgjpx1yb4p6erVZeBCBFFgq3v532q-VFwGB5ti9YUTHZG5AJHSxTDN86wT8SxgxvHkLqvM_8LdYWOTvGorUWdK0Uvq8jPmnfzTnHLKQY-ds60rSbl75VDnDEHCDQErjW9K-OQshtyB5dUMh/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+A+Pair+Of+Leather+Clogs.jpg" width="320" /></a>The Kohen performing the first service in the Temple, one of removing a handful of ashes from the Altar, <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=6#P2858">would change his garments to inferior ones, when taking them outside</a>. We learn from his example that one should dress up for Shabbat, prayer, and Torah study.
<br />
<br />
Torah scholar who wears soiled garments makes people dislike the Torah and is liable to a punishment. So too, it is a disgrace for a Torah scholar to go out in patched shoes. But Rab Acha bar Chanina did go out wearing patched shows!? – We mean, patches on patches, but one level of patches is allowed.
<br />
<br />
Which Torah scholar can be appointed a leader over a community? – One whom you can ask any question in learning, even in the areas rarely studied. For such a scholar the community has the obligation to provide  – but how much? – only for bread but not for luxuries.
<br />
<br />
Before the calendar was fixed, Yom Kippur could fall on Friday. In this case Rabbi Ishmael permits to fold garments on Yom Kippur in preparation for Shabbat. If Yom Kippur falls on Sunday, one can burn Shabbat offerings in the Temple on the Yom Kippur day, because Yom Kippur has lesser sanctity than Shabbat. However, Rabbi Akiva considers the two days to be of equal strenght, and fordibs preparing on one for the other. Both base their proof on the phrase from the Torah, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=28#P4585">Bring Shabbat offering on its own Shabbat</a>,” but understand it differently.
<br />
<br />
Art: Vincent Van Gogh - A Pair Of Leather Clogs

---

### content/shabbat/115.txt
<a id="src-00154"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/115.txt`

Shabbat 115 – What can be saved from fire on Shabbat
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1uTkAb3nbYddQNUl2L2c0v7VXIiEEfM-3PI650EJBjAObRnkMDuUjDuR8Fs4oYcXzotepluh-eOKPFNUd9rTr2e-wLesC1UHFhrh9HX5rP1k7dNy3QDTx4mQYBfAk4fIvOJd_HNPjZs3b/s1600/Egbert+van+der+Poel+-+A+house+on+fire+at+night+with+peasants+coming+to+rescue.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1uTkAb3nbYddQNUl2L2c0v7VXIiEEfM-3PI650EJBjAObRnkMDuUjDuR8Fs4oYcXzotepluh-eOKPFNUd9rTr2e-wLesC1UHFhrh9HX5rP1k7dNy3QDTx4mQYBfAk4fIvOJd_HNPjZs3b/s320/Egbert+van+der+Poel+-+A+house+on+fire+at+night+with+peasants+coming+to+rescue.jpg" width="304" /></a>In general, one is not allowed to extinguish fire on Shabbat, and this extends even to cases where that fire is destroying his possessions. Since one can't extinguish the fire, all he can do is save his possessions from it. Even here, there are limitations: one can only save specific items and in specific amounts. What is the rationale for this view?
<br />
<br />
A man is naturally nervous when he sees his possessions being destroyed by fire, and he may come to extinguish it, thus violating Shabbat. In order to prevent this, the Sages established a set of rules on how to behave in the face fire on Shabbat. Being mindful of these rules, one will not come to extinguish the fire. According to this, one is permitted less than not in the presence of fire, and we are talking about carrying from his house into a courtyard. On another theory, one is permitted slightly more, and we are talking about carrying into the semi-public street, or a “<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/10/shabbat-7-special-area-called-karmelit.html">karmelit</a>”. The rationale though remains the same – to stop a man from violation.
<br />
<br />
It should be mentioned that if there is any danger to human life, one should by all means extinguish the fire. Also, since in many time periods the neighbors, on seeing a Jewish property burn, might start plundeing it, then any fire became a matter of saving one's life, and any fire is to be extinguished, with the possible exception of a barn far away from people. Still, in the next few  pages we will learn the laws as they were formulated in the times of the Talmud.
<br />
<br />
First, can one save holy scriptures? The answer here is yes, whether it refers to the Torah of the writings of the prophets, and whether one can read them or no. Back then, people did not read the writings of the prophets on Shabbat. That was prohibited because the writing were considered entertaining, and being absorbed in reading them one might have missed a public lecture which was filled with practical laws. Such lecture was very important to the populace, and one was supposed to attend it rather than read the prophets. Nevertheless, even such writings, unusable on Shabbat, could be saved.
<br />
<br />
Art: Egbert van der Poel - A house on fire at night with peasants coming to rescue

---

### content/shabbat/116.txt
<a id="src-00155"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/116.txt`

Shabbat 116 – Eighty-five letters
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiFX6wz7F9eKj5rMzxuSVAlS-jnNuR6EEp4nJw7PeZOnms7kaUjnpAU6r3Z09SlikbWQ2faDPUqhsEuCHBmxxjG9QQ-oI2y5dZywkfgP3cAhh9PGUaV8PfUcVrWBoJEikYKvyJzidAnCz-p/s1600/John+Dawson+Watson+-+Fireside+Thoughts.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiFX6wz7F9eKj5rMzxuSVAlS-jnNuR6EEp4nJw7PeZOnms7kaUjnpAU6r3Z09SlikbWQ2faDPUqhsEuCHBmxxjG9QQ-oI2y5dZywkfgP3cAhh9PGUaV8PfUcVrWBoJEikYKvyJzidAnCz-p/s320/John+Dawson+Watson+-+Fireside+Thoughts.jpg" width="232" /></a>What is the smallest book in the Torah? – Rabbi Yehudah the Prince says that it is the phrase “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=10#P4021">When the Ark went forth, Moses said, 'Arise, O God, and scatter your enemies! Let your foes flee before You!'...</a>'” which contains eighty-five letters. If this phrase is indeed a separate book, then the Book of Numbers contains not one but three books - before this phrase, after it, and the phrase itself, and the total number of the books in the Torah is seven.<br />
<br />
Accordingly, Rav Huna asked a question, “A Torah scroll where many letters were erased and only eighty-five letters are intact, can it be saved from fire on Shabbat?” There is no doubt that a worn-out scrolls with even less letters deserves respect and cannot be destroyed directly but has to be “buried” in a clean place, and if it decays, it decays. The question is, can it be saved from fire? Rav Chisda answered that it was not permitted, and they started arguments back and forth.
<br />
<br />
A related question: the side margins of the Torah scroll, may they be saved from fire? Do we say that the scroll that had  letters – once the letters have been erased – looses its sanctity and may not be saved, but the margins, which never had letters, are more sanctified and may be saved? Or the other way around, if the letters once were there, then the sanctity persists, but not if they were never there? Here too the views are divided.
<br />
<br />
Art: John Dawson Watson - Fireside Thoughts

---

### content/shabbat/117.txt
<a id="src-00156"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/117.txt`

Shabbat 117 – Saving food
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiqO2pnpzmUmOTXMUytRYajqPUe5f1adhjFIWsjobdSjWCnrHoxSE54Nbbs_JFd6Oj0rCgzOx4AZw5H-HhLdq-zDfnRhAsuzjS9S36JpH3xIK5pH7VKSt43NSepmhraMc0N_s699Qa8pVaT/s1600/Carlo+Magini+-+Still+life+with+food+and+vegetables.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="245" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiqO2pnpzmUmOTXMUytRYajqPUe5f1adhjFIWsjobdSjWCnrHoxSE54Nbbs_JFd6Oj0rCgzOx4AZw5H-HhLdq-zDfnRhAsuzjS9S36JpH3xIK5pH7VKSt43NSepmhraMc0N_s699Qa8pVaT/s320/Carlo+Magini+-+Still+life+with+food+and+vegetables.jpg" width="320" /></a><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/01/shabbat-115-what-can-be-saved-from-fire.html">As we learned before</a>, one is allowed to save Torah scrolls from fire on Shabbat by carrying them outside the house, and this includes the tefillin. Moreover, if the tefillin bag has money in it, then – even though normally money cannot be handled on Shabbat – here he is not required to throw it away, but can save the bag with the tefillin and the money inside.
<br />
<br />
One is also allowed to save food, both for humans and for animals. However, one can only save enough for Shabbat: for example, if the fire broke out of Friday evening, he can save the amount necessary for three meals, but if it started on Shabbat morning, he can only save two meals. Rabbi Yose allows to save three meals under all circumstances, because in his opinion the law is already strict enough, and there is not need to count meals.
<br />
<br />
The rationale for both opinions is the same: in truth, we are talking about carrying the food into a courtyard, properly fenced from the public area, so carrying any amount of it should be allowed. However, since a person is naturally agitated when his possessions are burning and may start extinguishing the fire, the Sages added prohibitions, so that while observing them he will recall that if he is not allowed to save all the food he wants, then certainly he is not allowed to extinguish the fire.
<br />
<br />
Art: Carlo Magini - Still life with food and vegetables

---

### content/shabbat/118.txt
<a id="src-00157"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/118.txt`

Shabbat 118 – Three or four meals?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjm-rmmjrd2rjUYszkoHui80RNr823zEJllVgxEYSoF8omciThxRCtCedC2u5Z2pdV6K9gb00ZUENxkSQBiio8tYg9T8qdzt-zHHH3CjB1n5eaKcZ6oucp9mYv0V9DX8esYyspm0SX-xEcH/s1600/Gillis+Van+Tilborch+-+A+couple+sitting+and+having+a+meal.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="220" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjm-rmmjrd2rjUYszkoHui80RNr823zEJllVgxEYSoF8omciThxRCtCedC2u5Z2pdV6K9gb00ZUENxkSQBiio8tYg9T8qdzt-zHHH3CjB1n5eaKcZ6oucp9mYv0V9DX8esYyspm0SX-xEcH/s320/Gillis+Van+Tilborch+-+A+couple+sitting+and+having+a+meal.jpg" width="320" /></a>On Shabbat one is obligated to eat three meals, one of Friday evening and two others on the Saturday day. However, Rabbi Chidka says that one needs to eat four. Both opinions are based on the same phrase, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=16#P1973">Moses announced, 'Eat it today, for today is God's Sabbath. You will not find [anything] in the field today</a>.” The word “today” is mentioned three times, and this means three meals. And Rabbi Chidka? – He says that these three meals are during the day, and there is also  a fourth meal, on Friday night. But <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/01/shabbat-117-saving-food.html">we just learned</a> that if there fire breaks out on Friday night, he can only save three meals!? – Rabbi Chidka will answer that he already ate the Friday night meal, and then the fire broke out, so he saves the three meals for the next day, to the total of four. But we learned that Rabbi Yose allows to save three meals under all circumstances!? – True, Rabbi Chidka has nothing to say, and we are forced to conclude that this ruling does not agree with Rabbi Chidka, but he is entitled to his opinion.
<br />
<br />
One who observes eating three meals on Shabbat is saved from three calamities at the end of days. One who delights in Shabbat is forgiven all the idol worship he did during the week; some say that he is given a boundless heritage. Finally, one who delights in Shabbat is given his heart's wishes.
<br />
<br />
Art: Gillis Van Tilborch - A couple sitting and having a meal

---

### content/shabbat/119.txt
<a id="src-00158"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/119.txt`

Shabbat 119 – Each one has his own mitzvah
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhM7KyZLFIo8wADVU93ctY1frC-548Lz7kiRomuCXoUEDd7egj-kkWz5ZfKnV438-YcGfHtaqvrXLrzEvNnhdsSPh5imV2nnepxPi5oHqnCkVyZ1Z8bgq9w-LS9dbM4QKz4v4shg-YoUG8k/s1600/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-+The+Railway+Bridge+At+Argenteuil.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="235" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhM7KyZLFIo8wADVU93ctY1frC-548Lz7kiRomuCXoUEDd7egj-kkWz5ZfKnV438-YcGfHtaqvrXLrzEvNnhdsSPh5imV2nnepxPi5oHqnCkVyZ1Z8bgq9w-LS9dbM4QKz4v4shg-YoUG8k/s320/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-+The+Railway+Bridge+At+Argenteuil.jpg" width="320" /></a>Although one must perform all the mitzvot in the Torah in order to complete his spiritual ascent, it is recommended for one to choose a specific mitzvah, especially dear to him, and fulfill it in every detail,  since it is likely that his current reincarnation was for this purpose. For example, Rav Nachman said, “May my reward come from my carefully observing the three meals of Shabbat." Rabbi Yose was extremely modest and pliable to the demands of his scholarly colleagues. Abbaye, when he saw a young scholar complete a tractate of the Talmud, would make a feast for everyone.
<br />
<br />
Following are some ways in which the Sages used to honor the Shabbat. Rav Abahu would sit on an ivory stool and fan the fire for cooking; Rav Safra would singe the head of an animal; Rabbah and Rav Yosef would split wood; Rav Zeira would kindle the fire.
<br />
<br />
Yosef Mokir Shabi (Yosef Who Honors Shabbat) would spare no expense for Shabbat. There was a rich man in his&nbsp;neighborhood&nbsp; to whom astrologers predicted that all his wealth will go to this Yosef. He sold it all, bought an extremely valuable pearl with the money, and had it sown into his hat, to alwayscarry it with him. However, as he was passing a bridge, the wind blew the hat off his head and a fish swallowed it, fishermen caught the fish and Yosef bought it - since there was no one else who would buy such a fish this late, close to the beginning of the Shabbat. He then found the pearl and sold it for thirteen attics full of golden dinars. A certain elder then met him and told him the rule, “He who borrows for the sake of Shabbat, Shabbat repays him.”
<br />
<br />
Art: Claude Oscar Monet - The Railway Bridge At Argenteuil

---

### content/shabbat/12.txt
<a id="src-00159"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/12.txt`

Shabbat 12 – Work that is not needed
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtx_UKcrCIsrcm8990eutXBBplt1M0S-lzb0eyZNpJ_qUMU7s8q5gyyGlXcVxxba3S2aDVF2OUyek7kkkEKGu2VOWNV5kZcPTgElQjmLV36VXfF2jV7etMPMxwXKtRz6P7a70bl-gNkMxk/s1600/Carl+Vilhelm+Holsoe+-+Woman+Reading+by+Lamplight.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="290" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtx_UKcrCIsrcm8990eutXBBplt1M0S-lzb0eyZNpJ_qUMU7s8q5gyyGlXcVxxba3S2aDVF2OUyek7kkkEKGu2VOWNV5kZcPTgElQjmLV36VXfF2jV7etMPMxwXKtRz6P7a70bl-gNkMxk/s320/Carl+Vilhelm+Holsoe+-+Woman+Reading+by+Lamplight.jpg" width="320" /></a><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/10/shabbat-11-friday-afternoon.html">Earlier we saw</a> that on Friday afternoon a tailor should not go into the street with his needle, because he may forget and continue carrying it after sundown, when Shabbat already started. However, in discussing the case of a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/06/definition-of-term-zav.html">zav (a man who had a gonorrheal discharge)</a>, we find one ruling that allows him to carry a pouch to collect his discharge, while the other one forbids it. How are we to understand the opinion that it is allowed? The answer is that only that labor that is needed is prohibited on Shabbat. However, this man needs not his pouch but what collects in it (so that he can know when he becomes ritually pure), and that carrying is permitted – this is the opinion of Rabbi Shimon.
<br />
<br />
Another Friday night precaution: one should not delouse his garment or read a book, using a oil lamp, lest he strain to see something and adjust the light. On Shabbat during the day, how is one to delouse his garment? One should roll the flee between his fingers and throw it away, but not kill it. Nor should one do this in the street, out of respect for the passer-byes. Rabbi Ishmael ben Elisha&nbsp;thought&nbsp;that he could read by lamp light, and almost came to tilt the lamp. Some say, he did tilt it, and later wrote a note, “When the Temple is rebuilt, I will bring a fine sacrifice for my violation.”<br />
<br />
Can one visit sick people on Shabbat? Beit Shammai prohibit it, but Beit Hillel reluctantly allow it. One should pray for the sick when he visits, and say that “It is Shabbat, when we are forbidden to pray for daily needs, but the recovery is near.”
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Carl Vilhelm Holsoe - Woman Reading by Lamplight

---

### content/shabbat/120.txt
<a id="src-00160"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shabbat/120.txt`

Shabbat 120 – Helping others to save food from fire
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
