<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPlX1TO9Bb03FNamDANq5zwMWr4BLRoRhEpSj1Mlj3gcYPqRTZvpbtF2iS3eAX5Qdv7RvLSYxMsoiLDCm-HzXDIzUNreE-hfz_uvaG0l7teNE6ss-2UC1T0eox8Unuxbms-lqN4dcIiWZs/s1600/The+Treasurer+by+James+Gillray.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPlX1TO9Bb03FNamDANq5zwMWr4BLRoRhEpSj1Mlj3gcYPqRTZvpbtF2iS3eAX5Qdv7RvLSYxMsoiLDCm-HzXDIzUNreE-hfz_uvaG0l7teNE6ss-2UC1T0eox8Unuxbms-lqN4dcIiWZs/s320/The+Treasurer+by+James+Gillray.jpg" width="241" /></a>If the half-shekels were too heavy to carry, one could exchange them for smaller golden coins of larger value, called “darkon.” The collection chests, called “shofar” due to their shape, were set up in every city. They were regularly emptied and transported to Jerusalem.
<br />
<br />
If, while being transported, the coins were lost or stolen, the agents who transported them would have to take an oath that they have not been negligent – and then they would be free of the obligation to pay. But, to whom do they swear? If money to buy sacrifices in the Temple has already been separated, then the condition was that the money on the way would also be included. Thus, in this case, the money was considered in possession of the Temple, and the agents would swear to the Temple's treasurer. However, if the accident happened before the money was separated, the agents would swear to the townspeople – and the townspeople&nbsp;would have to undertake another collection.
<br />
<br />
If, after being thought missing, the coins were found, then both the first and the second collection have acquired the designation of “half-shekel” and cannot be taken back; moreover, the extra coins cannot be used for the next year either, because they were designated for this year. What do they do? They put them in another collection box, called "Old shekalim." These monies were used not for sacrifices but for the betterment of the city of Jerusalem. 
<br />
<br />
Art: The Treasurer by James Gillray

---

### content/shekalim/6.txt
<a id="src-00310"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shekalim/6.txt`

Shekalim 6 – Counting pennies
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgdcBW-euEJqnFJuVwgUnVA6JLPfqEXS9cb6PTUaTz2fke4t6BY9sorzwatiJLHvT80oN5COLuvea-ZTvz4YqP70cQgGheDpaBiS9NGk_MfPosxA3L43HMZ1YFeBBWeU9ujdmdYL72kEdT6/s1600/Merchants+counting+money+by+(after)+Salomon+Koninck.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="220" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgdcBW-euEJqnFJuVwgUnVA6JLPfqEXS9cb6PTUaTz2fke4t6BY9sorzwatiJLHvT80oN5COLuvea-ZTvz4YqP70cQgGheDpaBiS9NGk_MfPosxA3L43HMZ1YFeBBWeU9ujdmdYL72kEdT6/s320/Merchants+counting+money+by+(after)+Salomon+Koninck.jpg" width="320" /></a>If one was collecting small coins to accumulate his half-shekel – having declared “this is for my half-shekel” – but eventually he collected more than needed, &nbsp;what would he do with the surplus? Even though his designation of the surplus coins was invalid since he did not need them in the end, the coins still became consecrated, and the money should be put into the collection box in the Temple, to be used when the Altar is idle – this is the opinion of Beit Shammai. Beit Hillel disagrees: Temple consecration in error is invalid, and the money remains his. If his declaration was, “I will bring my shekel from this money,” all agree that the extra money remains his. 
<br />
<br />
What if he was collecting money for his sin-offering and collected more than he needed? Here the surplus definitely goes to the Temple. Why? Because the cost of a sin-offering does not have a fixed limit, whereas the half-shekel does – so explains Rabbi Shimon. However, Rabbi Yehudah argues with his explanation and says that the half-shekel also is not a fixed amount: when the Jews just got back from Babylon, they donated the “darkon” coin, which is 4 times more valuable, then they switched to two times more, then to half-shekels, although never less than that. So it depends on the basic currency unit. Still, Rabbi Shimon answers that the half-shekel is fixed in the sense that all give the same amount. The Talmud describes other surpluses; for example, the Passover sacrifice's surplus money must be used for another Passover sacrifice.
<br />
<br />
Art: Merchants counting money by (after) Salomon Koninck

---

### content/shekalim/7.txt
<a id="src-00311"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shekalim/7.txt`

Shekalim 7 – Monument
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhRgOdNmgLIw5RHTUmalGndVW6vzZ446sBB6QWWAePCyvu0-inujAEXbkl3qxJD6svM464GXSFQxKEMx_3fX3RHpU0qZP0xVr8_K1Hpgk8p2ATwButhgZZK5weAeIVXRwrUOvIPKPxVK7Cy/s1600/View+of+the+Monument+to+Peter+the+Great+in+Senate+Square+by+Vasilij+Ivanovic+Surikov.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="233" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhRgOdNmgLIw5RHTUmalGndVW6vzZ446sBB6QWWAePCyvu0-inujAEXbkl3qxJD6svM464GXSFQxKEMx_3fX3RHpU0qZP0xVr8_K1Hpgk8p2ATwButhgZZK5weAeIVXRwrUOvIPKPxVK7Cy/s320/View+of+the+Monument+to+Peter+the+Great+in+Senate+Square+by+Vasilij+Ivanovic+Surikov.jpg" width="320" /></a>Continuing with <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/10/shekalim-6-counting-pennies.html">surpluses</a>, money collected for prisoners' redemption and then left over should be used to redeem other prisoners, but nothing else. Similarly, surplus money intended to redeem one captive should be given to that captive since he already acquired it through the hands of collectors acting as his appointed agents.
<br />
<br />A surplus of money collected for the poor should be given to other poor people, but a surplus of money collected for one person should be given to him. A surplus of money collected to bury the dead should be used for other burials. Still, if it was collected for a specific dead, then there are three opinions: give it to his heirs, make a monument for him, or keep it intact until Elijah the prophet comes and decides.
<br />
<br />
Incidentally, only common people need monuments, but the righteous's teachings serve as their memorials and outlive the stone. Nevertheless, today is customary to build monuments for the righteous, not for their benefit, but for the living who will be reminded of them.
<br />
<br />
In the final analysis, &nbsp;charity and just deeds are better than the sacrifices and the money (shekalim) used for the sacrifices. People used to taunt King David, going next to his windows and asking, “When will the Temple be built?” – because it was known that it can be built only after King David's death. However, David would say, “Even though they want to anger me, I am happy with their words. I, too, would give up my life to build the Temple.” And nevertheless, God would say, “I will make your life complete, because one day of your life, David, with your charity and just deeds, are more precious to Me than the future sacrifices.”
<br />
<br />Art: View of the Monument to Peter the Great in Senate Square by Vasilij Ivanovic Surikov

---

### content/shekalim/8.txt
<a id="src-00312"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shekalim/8.txt`

Shekalim 8 - Scooping the shekalim
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIH7y31Y6DxWrFGlTB7LgiEvtV6_qFei8qE6JRmtmFZ0sKJvkxERd9ZCyFqcbScSSAAgKS-3ykKcNnkb48qXyKrGtWv47zsA_DIWo1gyqbKAAX0kLDG68FwR1z7qU_-77gtNcPQRZLay8u/s1600/The+Parable+Of+The+Rich+And+Poor+Man+by+(after)+Frans+II+Francken.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="207" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIH7y31Y6DxWrFGlTB7LgiEvtV6_qFei8qE6JRmtmFZ0sKJvkxERd9ZCyFqcbScSSAAgKS-3ykKcNnkb48qXyKrGtWv47zsA_DIWo1gyqbKAAX0kLDG68FwR1z7qU_-77gtNcPQRZLay8u/s320/The+Parable+Of+The+Rich+And+Poor+Man+by+(after)+Frans+II+Francken.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
All of the collected shekalim coins were deposited in a certain chamber in the Temple, and three times a year, they would scoop the money from there, before each of the three holidays: Passover, Shavuot, and Sukkot. These were also the times designated for separating the tithe of the animals. These times (about two weeks before each holiday) were established by the Sages for a few reasons: these are normal times when the animals bear their young; so that the people had the meat to eat at pilgrimages, and so that they would not delay their offerings.
<br />
<br />
Scooping was performed with three boxes, numbered aleph-bet-gimel, and some say with Greek letters, alpha-beta-gamma. The priest who performed the scooping did not enter with a hemmed garment, a shoe, a sandal, or any other box - to avoid the situation that if he would later become poor, people would say, “This happened to him because he stole!” and if he would become rich, they would say, “He became rich from the proceeds of his stealing!” This illustrates that one must strive to be clear of all suspicions, and even if he is clear in the  eyes of God, he must still strive to avoid suspicions in the eyes of men.
<br />
<br />
Art: The Parable Of The Rich And Poor Man by (after) Frans II Francken

---

### content/shekalim/9.txt
<a id="src-00313"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shekalim/9.txt`

Shekalim 9 - Scooping three times
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhO-wknDF5svkrKdjvPGCW0tWPpTtKtQRm7aDj5KWeZy1JYL7nTTYX25j_mhESSoyrsMbEd2ti5jAlvCJ8LitH7UQhtHBOzPioGkRNVWJfeFwqmwqWiq7xnRq20OMtCEhN9kBByBoJrABhe/s1600/Divine+inspiration+by+Petrus+Van+Schendel.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhO-wknDF5svkrKdjvPGCW0tWPpTtKtQRm7aDj5KWeZy1JYL7nTTYX25j_mhESSoyrsMbEd2ti5jAlvCJ8LitH7UQhtHBOzPioGkRNVWJfeFwqmwqWiq7xnRq20OMtCEhN9kBByBoJrABhe/s320/Divine+inspiration+by+Petrus+Van+Schendel.jpg" width="260" /></a></div>
There was a procedure to the scooping: the priest would go into the chamber and call from there, “Should I scoop?” and the administrators would command him three times: “Scoop! Scoop! Scoop!” He would fill the first box and cover the money remaining in this part of the room with a hide; he would then fill the second box and again cover the remainder with a hide, and the third portion he would not cover. Why all this? The first portion was of the people of Israel, the second - for the surrounding cities, and the third - for the people of Babylon, Media, and far away lands.
<br />
<br />
The family of Rabban Gamliel was especially zealous: they would enter the chamber and throw the coins right before the priest doing the scooping, and he would try to make sure to scoop their coins into his box.
<br />
<br />
On this subject of extra effort, Rabbi Pinchas ben Yair outlines ten steps of spiritual growth: extra effort brings to being free from wrongdoing; that brings one to re-think his previous wrongful acts; this leads to holiness, that is, refraining even from permitted pleasures; this leads to humility; humility brings one to realize one’s shortcomings and to honest desire not to do wrong again; this brings to doing good beyond the letter of the law - which brings Divine inspiration in its wake; then he can resurrect the dead, and this, in turn, brings Elijah the Prophet, may he be remembered for good.
<br />
<br />
Art: Divine inspiration by Petrus Van Schendel

---

### content/shevuot/10.txt
<a id="src-00314"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/10.txt`

Shevuot 10 – For What Each Specific Goat Atones
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjMchTOGFfImDFUH-P7xN4moncR6AqBbUHFhMIzCSeEsrjbssMp3HVyCXVWoDbsn8XsLhDI66MV7eCJoSH2CXeMrGwTb4dF_gPb0UlCZoJsGvb9pBSbEA1gApEp8dEt88N3OQUBGk03C1A/s1600/Paul+Gauguin+-+Landscape+with+Two+Goats.JPG" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjMchTOGFfImDFUH-P7xN4moncR6AqBbUHFhMIzCSeEsrjbssMp3HVyCXVWoDbsn8XsLhDI66MV7eCJoSH2CXeMrGwTb4dF_gPb0UlCZoJsGvb9pBSbEA1gApEp8dEt88N3OQUBGk03C1A/s320/Paul+Gauguin+-+Landscape+with+Two+Goats.JPG" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">According to Rabbi Yehudah, the goats brought on Festivals and the goats brought on the New Moon atone for violations of ritual purity laws, of which one never becomes aware.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon disagrees about the goats of the New Moon and says that they atone specifically for cases when one, while being pure, inadvertently eats impure sacrifices.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Meir says that the atonement of all he-goats is the same: they atone for inadvertent purity violations of the Temple and its offerings.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon Ben Yehuda has a different version of what Rabbi Shimon said: that the goats atone for a progressively wider range of infringements, from New Moon to Festivals to Yom Kippur. Said the Sages to him, "If they are so similar, can a goat designated for the New Moon be brought on Yom Kippur ?" He said, "Yes. Even though they are not the same, they have that in common: they deal with the purity of the Temple and its offerings.”<br />
<br />Art: Landscape with Two Goats by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Paul Gauguin</span>

---

### content/shevuot/11.txt
<a id="src-00315"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/11.txt`

Shevuot 11 – Removing Holiness from Sacrifices
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihXwiLMuERfkPo5Tagu7Ob0pibye5mHTR_V3n9k6KIw6nnb6yOte1NZ1Rjp9-_-xLSan0TNj25UwoeBt7MiZPc-ZecBAPKBr5UnWz7XsG7Ms6Zfod3_3h74SM09hqFwzZvaFGnFrUizr0/s1600/Pieter+Claesz+-+Still+Life+with+Wine+Glass+and+Silver+Bowl.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihXwiLMuERfkPo5Tagu7Ob0pibye5mHTR_V3n9k6KIw6nnb6yOte1NZ1Rjp9-_-xLSan0TNj25UwoeBt7MiZPc-ZecBAPKBr5UnWz7XsG7Ms6Zfod3_3h74SM09hqFwzZvaFGnFrUizr0/s320/Pieter+Claesz+-+Still+Life+with+Wine+Glass+and+Silver+Bowl.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When an object is donated or consecrated to the Temple, it attains sanctity and should not be used for one's own needs. Consecrated objects can be redeemed with money, and the sanctity transfers to money. Higher than this is physical sanctity: if the consecrated object can be used in the Temple service – for example, if it is an animal fit for the Altar, wine, flour, or incense – then it cannot, as a rule, be redeemed.<br />
<br />
Nevertheless, Ulla said in Rabbi Yochanan's name that daily offerings that are not needed by the community can be redeemed. Such lambs were present at the end of each Temple's fiscal year, when new half-shekels began to be used. <br />
<br />
Here is the procedure. The Temple treasurer borrows some funds, which are thus completely unconsecrated. He redeems the lambs, transferring their holiness to the money. This money is added to the old half-shekels and used for plating the Holy of Holies. The treasurer then repurchases the lambs with new half-shekels. Where does their holiness go? The court makes it a condition when consecrating the lambs in the first place that if they are not needed, they can be redeemed.<br />
<br />
Art: Still Life with Wine Glass and Silver Bowl by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Pieter Claesz</span>

---

### content/shevuot/12.txt
<a id="src-00316"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/12.txt`

Shevuot 12 – Not Removing Holiness from Sacrifices
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgZR5kULSn_QxiEcknAbfxzGrzaUfLIUrKmp-hVdFmTPda5oVPwSg5C3LtoRChQT_9mkB06KgaPhXy-8Jvgn2rhhUqMw3CH3LpHAoHmZJOY54vBVXL8_IrRaM00bWOPbFRDnPoJEIRdFvc/s1600/James+Ward+-+Heath+Ewe+and+Lamb.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgZR5kULSn_QxiEcknAbfxzGrzaUfLIUrKmp-hVdFmTPda5oVPwSg5C3LtoRChQT_9mkB06KgaPhXy-8Jvgn2rhhUqMw3CH3LpHAoHmZJOY54vBVXL8_IrRaM00bWOPbFRDnPoJEIRdFvc/s320/James+Ward+-+Heath+Ewe+and+Lamb.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/07/shevuot-oaths-11-removing-holiness-from.html">Earlier, Rabbi Yochanan stated</a> that daily offerings that are not needed by the community can be redeemed. However, Rabbi Shimon disagrees with this. In looking for the opponents of Rabbi Shimon, whose view Rabbi Yochanan follows, we fail to find an explicit recorded ruling. We are forced to conclude that Rabbi Yochanan had a tradition from his teachers to this effect.<br />
<br />
But according to Rabbi Shimon, what do we do with the leftover lambs? We offer them as treats on the Altar. This agrees with Rabbi Shimon's view that offerings of a similar nature (in this case, they are burnt-offerings, totally consumed on the Altar) are interchangeable.<br />
<br />
Art: Heath Ewe and Lamb by James Ward
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/13.txt
<a id="src-00317"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/13.txt`

Shevuot 13 – Eating and Working on Yom Kippur
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJepIXbgnsqHO59Fn7ELfJRfd-UmS4OJoF0wg70RnRnJzf7b8EwWKQpuIA6gZl4RmGoSyY31Qq3R_0Cag-gRFVbVDefN4hiBT4iNaZnES9jswYkXAM36BsMWjGmM7Mg4E7TZElfNo9DbQ/s1600/George+Goodwin+Kilburne+-+To+Crown+the+Feast.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJepIXbgnsqHO59Fn7ELfJRfd-UmS4OJoF0wg70RnRnJzf7b8EwWKQpuIA6gZl4RmGoSyY31Qq3R_0Cag-gRFVbVDefN4hiBT4iNaZnES9jswYkXAM36BsMWjGmM7Mg4E7TZElfNo9DbQ/s320/George+Goodwin+Kilburne+-+To+Crown+the+Feast.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The goat sacrifice, whose blood is brought inside the Holy of Holies, atones for all transgressions related to ritual purity, whether performed by mistake or deliberately. The goat sent away atones for all sins, whether done by mistake or intentionally, provided that the person repents. The day of Yom Kippur itself is greater than this, since it atones for all transgressions between man and God, again, provided that the man repents.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehudah the Prince has an exceptional opinion that Yom Kippur atones even for the person who does <b>not</b> repent (with three exceptions: denying the existence of the Creator, speaking insolently of the Torah, and refusing to be circumcised).&nbsp;<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">But according to Rabbi Yehudah, how is it possible to deserve being cut off, which&nbsp;<a href="" target="_blank">the Torah promises for eating and working on Yom Kippur,</a>&nbsp;if the last moment of it affects atonement?</span>&nbsp;- It would apply to one who eats, chokes, and immediately dies in the middle of Yom Kippur, or alternatively to one who keeps eating at the end of Yom Kippur.<br />
<br />
Art: To Crown the Feast by George Goodwin Kilburne</span>

---

### content/shevuot/14.txt
<a id="src-00318"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/14.txt`

Shevuot 14 – Awareness of Impurity – Two That Are Really Four
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjV_APdDAAzXfAxGI3AZ1nXTAfBV8W6VRKRwSZ_MA_owemlPWdGeDzJQm2_PycaeyqPS7h_jGav7Gq-0ofvd62OXAXosfsE377VpXllwDQT1GH-WGL_zydkZDtfhc91uKbFTnLkfTCKv94/s1600/Luisa+Vitelli+-+Parrot,+Blue+Tit,+Two+Lizards,+and+Vases.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjV_APdDAAzXfAxGI3AZ1nXTAfBV8W6VRKRwSZ_MA_owemlPWdGeDzJQm2_PycaeyqPS7h_jGav7Gq-0ofvd62OXAXosfsE377VpXllwDQT1GH-WGL_zydkZDtfhc91uKbFTnLkfTCKv94/s320/Luisa+Vitelli+-+Parrot,+Blue+Tit,+Two+Lizards,+and+Vases.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a person touched an object that made him impure, forgot about it, and then knowingly ate sacrifices, he has to bring a “variable” offering that depends on his means. This case is explicitly mentioned in the Torah. However, if he remembered about his impurity but forgot that the food he ate was holy, he is equally liable; this case is not mentioned in the Torah but rather derived.<br />
<br />
Similarly, if he forgot about his impurity and visited the Temple, this is the second of the "two" cases mentioned in the Torah. If he remembered about the impurity but forgot about the Temple, this is the additional derived case.<br />
<br />
Asked Rav Pappa, what if he forgot about the laws of impurity?  - But what exactly did he forget? If he forgot whether it is a lizard or a frog that makes him impure, let him go and learn it with the children in school! Rather, what if he forgot the amount of lizard's meat that makes him impure on contact, is it like a lentil or more? What is the law? - This question remains unresolved.<br />
<br />
Art: Parrot, Blue Tit, Two Lizards, and Vases by Luisa Vitelli<br />
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/15.txt
<a id="src-00319"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/15.txt`

Shevuot 15 – Adding to the City of Jerusalem
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhKLsCeCfHBIclevLWi6_dBzerN_ELIeUWoDtXvongqJOK7Ej4LUJ2PKpcF0g91PaZMrz-n8AQaxnhmqgKl6Rlc2tgGrw9xj2OftBHKKvcjyjEMqVuZtBrpWEyzMMZ5rdQjZ88BEQD2l04/s1600/Jan+De+Bray+-+David+Playing+the+Harp.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhKLsCeCfHBIclevLWi6_dBzerN_ELIeUWoDtXvongqJOK7Ej4LUJ2PKpcF0g91PaZMrz-n8AQaxnhmqgKl6Rlc2tgGrw9xj2OftBHKKvcjyjEMqVuZtBrpWEyzMMZ5rdQjZ88BEQD2l04/s320/Jan+De+Bray+-+David+Playing+the+Harp.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One is liable for entering the Temple while impure, whether he enters the original Courtyard or the area that was added later – and here is the procedure for adding to the Courtyard and to the City of Jerusalem.<br />
<br />
With the consent of the king, a prophet, Urim VeTumim, and the Sanhedrin of seventy-one, they would prepare a Thanksgiving offering and a song. The High Court marches around the perimeter of the area being added, and the two loaves of the Thanksgiving offering in front of them, carried by the kohanim, and all Israel behind them. The Thanksgiving  loaves were used because they could only be eaten inside of Jerusalem, and they were huge, made with a few hundred cups of flour. They sang "<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt26a0.htm">The Song of Thanksgiving, call out to God, everyone on earth.</a>", accompanied by harps, lyres, and cymbals.<br />
<br />
Art: David Playing the Harp by Jan De Bray
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/16.txt
<a id="src-00320"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/16.txt`

Shevuot 16 – Did the Holiness of Jerusalem Lapse with the Exile?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJ4VBJqfSHyp9NG717PYuh1RjagEXddRTTHtMsn4W7AxP7H_5AAUkee4jqWoMZ3ha0-TzJazf2zgNixCwvkolnETjnQyki3YltIjlD1OXWFlr0rH4Sl3nZHHARszLcmB02CkwdaM5EMPk/s1600/Gustave+Bauernfeind+-+David+Street+in+Jerusalem.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJ4VBJqfSHyp9NG717PYuh1RjagEXddRTTHtMsn4W7AxP7H_5AAUkee4jqWoMZ3ha0-TzJazf2zgNixCwvkolnETjnQyki3YltIjlD1OXWFlr0rH4Sl3nZHHARszLcmB02CkwdaM5EMPk/s320/Gustave+Bauernfeind+-+David+Street+in+Jerusalem.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Do we need <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/07/shevuot-oaths-15-adding-to-city-of.html">all attributes (king, prophet, etc.)</a> to sanctify additional areas of Jerusalem, or are some enough? <br />
<br />
Those who say that a few attributes are sufficient say so because, in their view, Jerusalem's initial holiness lapsed with the Babylonian exile. Since Ezra did not have all the attributes but was still able to sanctify Jerusalem and the Temple, we see that not all attributes are needed.<br />
<br />
Those who say that all are required say so because, in their view, the initial holiness of Jerusalem continued through the Babylonian exile. If so, then why did Ezra need any sanctification at all? - Just for remembrance of the ritual.<br />
<br />
If one became impure while in the Temple and forgot about it, he is obligated to bring a "variable" offering. This is not mentioned directly in the Torah. However, since there are two separate prohibitions to enter the Tabernacle and the Temple while being impure, and the words Tabernacle and Temple are used interchangeably, the extra prohibition is applied to one who becomes impure while in the Courtyard.<br />
<br />
Art: David Street in Jerusalem by Gustave Bauernfeind
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/17.txt
<a id="src-00321"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/17.txt`

Shevuot 17 – Different Kinds of Bowing Down
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjsfLc_qvOyKLEIKu8bsjKppW3B8aaYMkeUiryEpDZHuB69o4BECjvfl_ktiQxDvpkxUEpm0l06XyRdQo_faOaxe99bSlARrWSd4sgNL733OQXoEsa4_ODfWPnRful-oLenFHKQdn4jBmA/s1600/Sir+David+Wilkie+-+Woman+with+a+Baby+Kneeling.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjsfLc_qvOyKLEIKu8bsjKppW3B8aaYMkeUiryEpDZHuB69o4BECjvfl_ktiQxDvpkxUEpm0l06XyRdQo_faOaxe99bSlARrWSd4sgNL733OQXoEsa4_ODfWPnRful-oLenFHKQdn4jBmA/s320/Sir+David+Wilkie+-+Woman+with+a+Baby+Kneeling.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one became ritually impure while in the Temple and </span><span style="font-size: medium;">before leaving</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> bowed down, or tarried long enough to bow down, he is liable to the "variable" offering. <br />
<br />
There are three kinds of bowing down are mentioned in the Scripture. "Kidah" means bringing one's face down to the ground from a standing position, with no more than his thumbs to support him in front. <a href="http://bible.cc/1_kings/1-31.htm">Batsheva was able to do it</a>, and the High Priest would attempt it on Yom Kippur in order to keep awake. "Keriah" is kneeling down, and "Hishtachavaah" means complete prostration on the ground, with arms and legs extended.<br />
<br />
Rava asked, "If one, upon being contaminated, suspended himself in the air of the Courtyard, not touching the floor, is he liable for an offering?" Does "tarrying long enough to bow down" imply being able to actually bow down, or does it not? - No answer is given to that question.<br />
<br />
Art: Woman with a Baby Kneeling by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Sir David Wilkie</span>

---

### content/shevuot/18.txt
<a id="src-00322"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/18.txt`

Shevuot 18 – The Proper Way To Withdraw
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEieNmN7_kzUNkvbiSPbw7ouWLQbZcmVl51ySBxVoGo-VV_vUeaKqJfsqbJfOI-6DOpnuglwt0NkgLaYYizTyUrXrb6XF_xCLuZKgCkyBSy0ky4Nh_WsyaP6VcS-8iA5z287wl_As17U5a8/s1600/Jean-Honore+Fragonard+-+Le+Verrou+%28The+Bolt%29.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEieNmN7_kzUNkvbiSPbw7ouWLQbZcmVl51ySBxVoGo-VV_vUeaKqJfsqbJfOI-6DOpnuglwt0NkgLaYYizTyUrXrb6XF_xCLuZKgCkyBSy0ky4Nh_WsyaP6VcS-8iA5z287wl_As17U5a8/s320/Jean-Honore+Fragonard+-+Le+Verrou+%28The+Bolt%29.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one was cohabiting with a woman, and she told him "I have become a niddah" (that is, she sensed during the cohabitation that she has begun to menstruate), and he withdrew immediately (with a “live” organ [erection]) – he is liable to a sacrifice, since his exit is as pleasurable to him as his entry.<br />
<br />
Therefore, as Abaye said, he is liable to two offerings. But, as Rava asked, how could it be two offerings? If he is a Sage, and he knows the rules, then he may liable to bring an offering for the entry, but as far as exit – he is doing it deliberately, and offerings are brought only for mistakes! And if he is an ignoramus, this is all one big mistake, and he brings one offering! Rava himself answered his question, explaining that we are dealing with an incomplete Sage, who does not know the prohibition to withdraw immediately, which makes it for him an unintentional mistake.<br />
<br />
What should he do? He should "thrust his ten fingernails in the ground, like Joseph" (remain still until his organ becomes limp), and he is fortunate for having conquered his evil inclination.<br />
<br />
Art: Le Verrou (The Bolt) by Jean-Honore Fragonard
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/19.txt
<a id="src-00323"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/19.txt`

Shevuot 19 – Two Types of Oaths That Are Four
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgy4eLXDkp_jTiH_NQBFMUEAkpV8leUZQCZNE7SSp9ZNnBPf2_Hdb6u-_P7k9uHrSEk68pgwbzRyI-4SzcIG1efTIMS5EzhyphenhyphenRRkMhpGkqDJaaS0-DpOE__7UuqNmimamZc6TLj9otgqTeI/s1600/Bartolome+Esteban+Murillo+-+Boys+Eating+Fruit.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgy4eLXDkp_jTiH_NQBFMUEAkpV8leUZQCZNE7SSp9ZNnBPf2_Hdb6u-_P7k9uHrSEk68pgwbzRyI-4SzcIG1efTIMS5EzhyphenhyphenRRkMhpGkqDJaaS0-DpOE__7UuqNmimamZc6TLj9otgqTeI/s320/Bartolome+Esteban+Murillo+-+Boys+Eating+Fruit.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one says, "An oath that I will eat" (a particular food object), or "An oath that I will not eat" - these are <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/5-4.htm">the two oaths explicit in the Torah</a>. "An oath that I ate," or "An oath that I did not eat" - these are the two types of oath derived by exegesis.<br />
<br />
If one swore, "An oath that I will not eat," and then, forgetting his oath, ate even a minute amount, he is liable – these are the words of Rabbi Akiva. The Sages told Rabbi Akiva, "Where do we find regarding one who eats a minute amount of forbidden food that he is liable?" There has to be a minimum amount! Rabbi Akiva replied to them, "And where do we find that one speaks and brings an offering because of mere words?"<br />
<br />
Art: Boys Eating Fruit by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Bartolome Esteban Murillo</span>

---

### content/shevuot/2.txt
<a id="src-00324"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/2.txt`

Shevuot 2 – Two Types of Oaths that are in Reality Four
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAo6Ao2QC0zvl164YRwZUO69vieet0b5HOV5pjI02TmfLVnXiVDUxiiqBU68loac0ercA0YusAdQt8TRszPbMUQoUk0xqzPbMaqXd8xSEHjPp9sPasDzLqB57psEq5QwZIpGZXkZjLqB0/s1600/Isaac+Luttichuys+-+Still+Life+with+Bread+and+Wine+Glass.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAo6Ao2QC0zvl164YRwZUO69vieet0b5HOV5pjI02TmfLVnXiVDUxiiqBU68loac0ercA0YusAdQt8TRszPbMUQoUk0xqzPbMaqXd8xSEHjPp9sPasDzLqB57psEq5QwZIpGZXkZjLqB0/s320/Isaac+Luttichuys+-+Still+Life+with+Bread+and+Wine+Glass.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Oaths can be of two types: to do something, or not to do it. For example, "I will eat this bread" or "I will not eat this bread." These are <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/5-4.htm">the oaths explicitly mentioned in the Torah</a>. However, one can derive the same two types of oaths related to the past, where the person swears that he did something, or didn't do it. If made inadvertently, all four types require the offender to bring a variable-type offering, which depends on his means.<br />
<br />
(Here the Talmud digresses from oaths to discuss other cases of "two that are in reality four." It will not come back to oaths until after eighteen pages.)<br />
<br />
But why study oaths right after Makkot (lashes)? Because one of the last subjects in Makkot was multiple penalties for one transgression, and "two that are four" is formulated similarly.<br />
<br />
Art: Still Life with Bread and Wine Glass by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Isaac Luttichuys</span>

---

### content/shevuot/20.txt
<a id="src-00325"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/20.txt`

Shevuot 20 – One Who Attaches His Oath To Another Oath
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhb9zc2Fyfg-9KJhk_5EfTIgIyHKvOoIjRJEbO2EVDbAoNpJeiyiPccpNAOSjJMGANWCLMEPdFhJkyfRw8f9ukbeYcwKO0HfOcXlLB-dQCLEhGB4Ssn5pe2LSedh84H8Nl-t_gDRHdoZQ/s1600/Luis+Mel%C3%A9ndez+-+Still+Life+with+Figs+and+Bread.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhb9zc2Fyfg-9KJhk_5EfTIgIyHKvOoIjRJEbO2EVDbAoNpJeiyiPccpNAOSjJMGANWCLMEPdFhJkyfRw8f9ukbeYcwKO0HfOcXlLB-dQCLEhGB4Ssn5pe2LSedh84H8Nl-t_gDRHdoZQ/s320/Luis+Mel%C3%A9ndez+-+Still+Life+with+Figs+and+Bread.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one made an oath not to eat a particular loaf and then said regarding another loaf, "This one should be to me like that one," does this create another oath? Abaye say, "Yes," but Rava say, "No."<br />
<br />
They challenged both based on the following ruling. If one says, "It is hereby incumbent on me that I not eat meat nor drink wine, as on the day on which my father died (source for fasting on a yahrtzeit), or as on the day when Gedaliyah ben Achikam was killed (fast of the 3rd of Tishrei), or as on the day on which I viewed Jerusalem in its destruct "on" - he is indeed prohibited. Shmuel commented, "This is only true if he already vowed from that day on."<br />
<br />
This seems perfect according to Abaye: one attaches a vow to a vow, and in the same way an oath to an oath. However, it does not agree with Rava, who said that one cannot attach one oath to another oath! Rava will tell you that this ruling discusses a vow attached to a prohibited object (meat and wine), not an attachment to a vow, which, although mentioned, would be ineffective.<br />
<br />
Art: Still Life with Figs and Bread by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Luis Melendez</span>

---

### content/shevuot/21.txt
<a id="src-00326"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/21.txt`

Shevuot 21 – How Strict Is The Opinion of Rabbi Akiva?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2JikgNGgTyQXOKklX4yCnrCOc6nyfvF75lcA6WGae4VwXDFIdwWEYs2_eeNgcR5F-27p499IQQfzPKKULhjwmU9-G-LNNg_E2D51TVkW5lDTLqFvBgsyBEU3OdSvIG6q8Qz-xdEV4xas/s1600/Georges+de+La+Tour+-+Peasant+Couple+Eating.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2JikgNGgTyQXOKklX4yCnrCOc6nyfvF75lcA6WGae4VwXDFIdwWEYs2_eeNgcR5F-27p499IQQfzPKKULhjwmU9-G-LNNg_E2D51TVkW5lDTLqFvBgsyBEU3OdSvIG6q8Qz-xdEV4xas/s320/Georges+de+La+Tour+-+Peasant+Couple+Eating.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">For the violation of the "I will not eat" oath, Rabbi Akiva obligates one for even a minute amount. Why is this? <br />
<br />
Is it because he follows the opinion of Rabbi Shimon, who obligates one for any prohibited food for even a minute amount? If so, Rabbi Akiva should disagree in general and say to the Sages, "I obligate for any food violation, regardless of amount!" No, this idea is incorrect. Rabbi Akiva could simply be answering the Sages according to their words: "I say, one is liable for any amount of forbidden food. You, the Sages, who don't hold so, should at least agree with me in the instance of an oath, where he violates his oath, not just the food prohibition."<br />
<br />
It could also be that, in general, Rabbi Akiva does not follow Rabbi Shimon's opinion and obligates for eating forbidden foods only if a specific amount is consumed. Here, however, Rabbi Akiva says that the one who takes an oath, "I will not eat," means it in the ordinary sense of eating, and small amounts are included.<br />
<br />
The second explanation is the preferred one.<br />
<br />
Art: Peasant Couple Eating by Georges de La Tour
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/22.txt
<a id="src-00327"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/22.txt`

Shevuot 22 – Oath Not To Eat
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyCzSDgDN_fB42hCFv3BZdLeJDs3nf1Zd0zIZ9HiLDiOFFf-OdAcNY181y1Y7YzWRlEtNDwbHLisRT7268Hu-01tsP7asSf3XQMGVKuRCnfmxjmROQXKqwrtHSsM3kf7T4kV2_zhZpXYA/s1600/Giacomo+Ceruti+-+Sea+Food+.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyCzSDgDN_fB42hCFv3BZdLeJDs3nf1Zd0zIZ9HiLDiOFFf-OdAcNY181y1Y7YzWRlEtNDwbHLisRT7268Hu-01tsP7asSf3XQMGVKuRCnfmxjmROQXKqwrtHSsM3kf7T4kV2_zhZpXYA/s320/Giacomo+Ceruti+-+Sea+Food+.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Asked Rava, "If one took an oath not to eat earth, how much must he eat to be liable?" Is it like all eating, a volume of an olive, or, since the earth is inedible, he means even a minute amount? - Remains unresolved.<br />
<br />
If one swore, "An oath that I will not eat," and then he ate and drank, he is liable for only one offering. But if one swore, "An oath that I will not eat and that I will not drink," and then he ate and drank, he is liable to two offerings.<br />
<br />
If one swore, "An oath that I will not eat," and then he ate prohibited foods, such as animals or foul that were not slaughtered correctly, unkosher fish, seals, frogs, flies, bees, mosquitoes – he is liable. Rabbi Shimon exempts him because he swore to do something he is already obligated to do, and his new oath did not take effect.<br />
<br />
Art: Sea Food by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Giacomo Ceruti</span>

---

### content/shevuot/23.txt
<a id="src-00328"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/23.txt`

Shevuot 23 – Not To Eat Bread!
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi0QpjtYZ6szmW-QZ4RNMkT79vc5-2-FjYGeU9p2FCP9ECl4gBMZlm3brKhAs3LxohnkgAGRv2pqU-K6EHT5VqEeDFAdF6M5V4BTGTIDc-D7WfadfO4TN9QcRVOlMX9eCWoVjLqdobs_T0/s1600/Johannes+Vermeer+-+The+Milkmaid.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi0QpjtYZ6szmW-QZ4RNMkT79vc5-2-FjYGeU9p2FCP9ECl4gBMZlm3brKhAs3LxohnkgAGRv2pqU-K6EHT5VqEeDFAdF6M5V4BTGTIDc-D7WfadfO4TN9QcRVOlMX9eCWoVjLqdobs_T0/s320/Johannes+Vermeer+-+The+Milkmaid.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one swore, "An oath that I will not eat!" - and then he ate wheat bread, barley bread, and spelt bread – he is liable for only one offering. But if he swore, "An oath that I will not eat wheat bread, barley bread, and spelt bread!" - and then he ate all three – he is liable for each one.<br />
<br />
But why? Maybe all he meant was "no breads," and this is all one oath? - If so, he should have said, "I will not eat wheat, barley, and spelt." <br />
<br />
But maybe he meant to prohibit himself from chewing those grains? - If so, he should have said, "I will not eat <i>bread</i> of wheat, barley, and spelt." Instead, he included the word "bread" every time, thus separating his oath into three separate oaths.<br />
<br />
Art: The Milkmaid by Johannes Vermeer
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/24.txt
<a id="src-00329"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/24.txt`

Shevuot 24 – Eating Non-kosher Meat on Yom Kippur
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFoHDtbWJ82xLt2KlqYSewn-_n3eFg_RNFBCiAUVWEVHr2tqBKG3X5Km6foQm1V-DAi8Ok5seU9zl-U9NTZ9AcVOGSigqqLNa5jx4lmkrrmvMt3r7hIOTp7kLwXF8mY4ILOGP-osCOAVI/s1600/Jean-Baptiste-Simeon+Chardin+-+Still+Life+with+a+Rib+of+Beef.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFoHDtbWJ82xLt2KlqYSewn-_n3eFg_RNFBCiAUVWEVHr2tqBKG3X5Km6foQm1V-DAi8Ok5seU9zl-U9NTZ9AcVOGSigqqLNa5jx4lmkrrmvMt3r7hIOTp7kLwXF8mY4ILOGP-osCOAVI/s320/Jean-Baptiste-Simeon+Chardin+-+Still+Life+with+a+Rib+of+Beef.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When one eats meat of an animal that was not properly slaughtered (neveilah) on Yom Kippur, this is an example of an inclusive prohibition. This meat was already prohibited to him before Yom Kippur. Now that Yom Kippur has come, it has brought with it an all-inclusive prohibition to eat this and other foods. The Sages make him liable for two prohibitions: eating unkosher meat and eating on Yom Kippur. Rabbi Shimon, however, does not agree to the principle of inclusive prohibition and makes him liable only for eating unkosher meat.<br />
<br />However, what about the following ruling: for one act of eating, one can be liable to five offerings: an impure person who ate forbidden fat usually brought on the altar, beyond the time allowed for the sacrifice, from a consecrated animal, and on Yom Kippur. According to the principle of inclusive prohibition, why not add another one – an oath against eating fat? - We list only those prohibitions that existed by themselves, not the ones he creates.<br />
<br />
Art: Still Life with a Rib of Beef by Jean-Baptiste-Simeon Chardin
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/25.txt
<a id="src-00330"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/25.txt`

Shevuot 25 – The Scope of Oaths is All-Inclusive
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjf7tWz95fnouCqs1voQgeVoX24QytJXN96I8An55tK0AEHouMxm1eRR92i5rhZ4AYh-pd4_OJr49Pt-KG8N-2_A68WtqDXoA-N9xzLT_FCvocfqJSOh8FIZwvuf_BLR7EkybKQOaqaG5I/s1600/Jan+Vermeer+Van+Delft+-+A+Woman+Asleep+at+Table.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjf7tWz95fnouCqs1voQgeVoX24QytJXN96I8An55tK0AEHouMxm1eRR92i5rhZ4AYh-pd4_OJr49Pt-KG8N-2_A68WtqDXoA-N9xzLT_FCvocfqJSOh8FIZwvuf_BLR7EkybKQOaqaG5I/s320/Jan+Vermeer+Van+Delft+-+A+Woman+Asleep+at+Table.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">An oath takes effect regarding both matters relevant to oneself and relevant to another, regarding both matters of substance and those lacking substance.<br />
<br />
For example, if one swears, "I will give something to so-and-so," or "I will not give it to him," or "I swear that I gave it to him," or "I swear that I did not give it to him," this is an oath about others.<br />
<br />
If he said, "I swear that I will sleep" or "that I will not sleep," "I slept" or "I did not sleep" - these are oaths concerning intangible matters.<br />
<br />If one said, "I swear that I will throw a pebble into the sea," or "I will not throw the pebble," "I threw the pebble," or "I did not throw," - these are oaths concerning non-beneficial acts.<br />
<br />
Art: A Woman Asleep at Table - Jan Vermeer Van Delft
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/26.txt
<a id="src-00331"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/26.txt`

Shevuot 26 – No Oaths Regarding the Past
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgaT5NpW6g235pKaTyopmyy1YOPYQAswX3dfLHeOmkRq8OlojSooLHGCCjctDgrY9D1k7DIzOyxIct_l_IbgbHJoRAVwF4Yc4TUOZWv4Nol6NaviOgj4mgNguvKXc8Riqh-SETjldyZO4I/s1600/Frederick+Childe+Hassam+-+Sea+and+Rocks,+Appledore,+Isles+of+Shoals.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgaT5NpW6g235pKaTyopmyy1YOPYQAswX3dfLHeOmkRq8OlojSooLHGCCjctDgrY9D1k7DIzOyxIct_l_IbgbHJoRAVwF4Yc4TUOZWv4Nol6NaviOgj4mgNguvKXc8Riqh-SETjldyZO4I/s320/Frederick+Childe+Hassam+-+Sea+and+Rocks,+Appledore,+Isles+of+Shoals.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">According to Rabbi Ishmael, one is not liable to bring a sacrifice for oaths concerning past events, because of the following: "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/5-4.htm">If a person swears by uttering with his lips to do bad or to do good</a>," and these oaths are expressed in future terms.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiva said to him, "If so, if you want to interpret the verse literally, then you only have oaths dealing with good and bad. What about neutral oaths, such as to throw a rock into the sea?" Rabbi Ishmael answered, "I get it from the extra inclusion of 'for anything that a person utters in an oath'". Said Rabbi Akiva, "This inclusion also includes oaths concerning the past!"<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiva answered well! What does Rabbi Ishmael have to say? The teacher of Rabbi Ishmael was Rabbi Nechunia ben Hakaneh, the time's chief kabbalist, and Rabbi Akiva's teacher was Nachum Ish Gamzu, known for saying, "This also is for the good." They differed on which of the 13 rules of Torah interpretation is prevalent – the generalization/specification or the amplification/limitation.<br />
<br />
Art: Sea and Rocks, Appledore, Isles of Shoals by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Frederick Childe Hassam</span>

---

### content/shevuot/27.txt
<a id="src-00332"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/27.txt`

Shevuot 27 – An Oath to Violate a Mitzvah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhxBtkq7FyQiMrP5-Ps6r-NPyqpp3Vx2TTzTqd5FbrHpZuW_iz250aNGTi-0Or6RPDUkBkow_sSn2jBCb5ukiyaGCOrXGDnfpqy-uVq42Uv8midKtyIy-bfg_oYhZCG0HH9WIgSjtaH4rM/s1600/Jacques+Louis+David+-+Deputies+swearing+oaths.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhxBtkq7FyQiMrP5-Ps6r-NPyqpp3Vx2TTzTqd5FbrHpZuW_iz250aNGTi-0Or6RPDUkBkow_sSn2jBCb5ukiyaGCOrXGDnfpqy-uVq42Uv8midKtyIy-bfg_oYhZCG0HH9WIgSjtaH4rM/s320/Jacques+Louis+David+-+Deputies+swearing+oaths.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one swears to violate a mitzvah but does not violate it, he is not liable for an oath of utterance and a sacrifice. In the same way, if he swears to fulfill a mitzvah and does not do it, he is exempt. Oaths only apply to something that he has the freedom to do or not to do, and not to mitzvot, which one is obligated to do from the time of Mount Sinai. However, in the first case, he is liable to lashes for making a vain oath.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehudah ben Beteira wants to prove that one who swears to do a mitzvah and does not do it is liable, as follows. If in the case of an oath to do an optional act, one is liable for not doing it, then in the case of a mitzvah, which he is already obligated to do, how much more is he liable if he does not do it!<br />
<br />
But the Sages say oaths are only created if one has the freedom to promise to do or not to do something, and in the case of mitzvot, one does not have this freedom.<br />
<br />
Art: Deputies swearing oaths by Jacques-Louis David</span>

---

### content/shevuot/28.txt
<a id="src-00333"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/28.txt`

Shevuot 28 – Repeated Oaths and Quizzes
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgWUK2lO2bY1ZXi718eLnF5qxhO1nRkiEtGd9KMdGB2xUDp2S0c-m9BHJU46i2gdV3veV0_R32JgEIjiXPHptRKZI_jK4juE5PkJcnJKiUzTG7R9NGJ-pe5m5dz519MuVqFMVERLSBwLWY/s1600/Edmond+Lebel+-+Sellers+of+figs+and+nuts.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgWUK2lO2bY1ZXi718eLnF5qxhO1nRkiEtGd9KMdGB2xUDp2S0c-m9BHJU46i2gdV3veV0_R32JgEIjiXPHptRKZI_jK4juE5PkJcnJKiUzTG7R9NGJ-pe5m5dz519MuVqFMVERLSBwLWY/s320/Edmond+Lebel+-+Sellers+of+figs+and+nuts.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one swore, "I take an oath not to eat this loaf of bread,” then again, “I will not eat it,” “I will not eat it,” and ate, he is liable only for transgressing the first oath. Additional ones do not take effect, since the first one already prohibited the loaf to him. If, however, the first oath is annulled, the second one takes effect.<br />
<br />
Aifa studied oaths in the academy of Rabbah. His brother Avimi met him and asked a question, “If one takes an oath that he has not eaten today, and then repeats it, what is the law?” Aifa said, “He transgressed once.” “Wrong!” - said Avimi - “These are two false oaths.”<br />
<br />
Avimi asked another question, “An oath that I will not eat nine figs, an oath that I will not eat ten!” Aifa answered, “Liable for each oath.” “Wrong!” - said Avimi - “If he cannot eat nine figs, then he cannot eat ten.” <br />
<br />
Avimi asked a third question, “'An oath that I will not eat ten figs, an oath that I will not eat nine,' - and then he ate ten, what is the law?” Aifa answered, “He transgressed once, since the second oath is included in the first.” “Wrong!” - said Avimi - “The first oath prohibits ten figs, but allows nine, so the second oath is stricter than the first!” - and if he eats ten figs, he transgresses two oaths.<br />
<br />
Art: Sellers of figs and nuts by Edmond Lebel
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/29.txt
<a id="src-00334"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/29.txt`

Shevuot 29 – Vain Oaths
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5fsjjqWXfD7OK_3HZAaaEWRJob2Sb9XrTKXS7iBpMj3ZIjX1k3f8x3mHYqnqI0vEQ6dWJaOavmRdbcSnfp7hgzNmIbJbvMU-1NKNjKSlTEjVWOIv0-AsPd9lAXKSMobffoir-cbND-Ic/s1600/Edward+Pritchett+-+A+View+Of+St+Mark%27s+Column,+And+The+Doge%27s+Palace,+Venice.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5fsjjqWXfD7OK_3HZAaaEWRJob2Sb9XrTKXS7iBpMj3ZIjX1k3f8x3mHYqnqI0vEQ6dWJaOavmRdbcSnfp7hgzNmIbJbvMU-1NKNjKSlTEjVWOIv0-AsPd9lAXKSMobffoir-cbND-Ic/s320/Edward+Pritchett+-+A+View+Of+St+Mark%27s+Column,+And+The+Doge%27s+Palace,+Venice.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">What is called an oath given in vain? If one swore to contradict something that is well known to people. For example, if he said that a stone column is made of gold, a man is a woman, or a woman is a man.<br />
<br />
Another  example of a vain oath is when he swore about something that is impossible for him to do, or which is prohibited by the Torah, and in this sense, impossible. Thus, if he knew a testimony and swore not to say it, it is a vain oath, since he is obligated by the Torah to testify if he knows a favorable testimony about someone. Similarly, it is a vain oath not to put on tefillin.<br />
<br />
For vain oaths, one is liable to lashes if the violation is willful, but he is completely exempt if he did it by mistake.<br />
<br />
Art: A View Of St Mark's Column, And The Doge's Palace, Venice by Edward Pritchett<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/3.txt
<a id="src-00335"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/3.txt`

Shevuot 3 – Who Authored the “Two that are Four” Ruling?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2lQ4iycQUPdDsNjrtfAVVZbDeS2JCG_cMEwW6tO3TDBe7VE8sZb0S9ZKPuytyIPHLQcfQV_zasZGKWFN-3WtwxR8ohhevSlL_Zb570k0n3ZVrb3CVH5yalRfG4EGo-9PhAVqiXXuv4ao/s1600/Isidor+Kaufmann+-+Discussing+The+Talmud.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2lQ4iycQUPdDsNjrtfAVVZbDeS2JCG_cMEwW6tO3TDBe7VE8sZb0S9ZKPuytyIPHLQcfQV_zasZGKWFN-3WtwxR8ohhevSlL_Zb570k0n3ZVrb3CVH5yalRfG4EGo-9PhAVqiXXuv4ao/s320/Isidor+Kaufmann+-+Discussing+The+Talmud.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><i><b>Argument:</b></i><br />
<br />
<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/06/shevuot-oaths-2-two-types-of-oaths-that.html" target="_blank">That ruling</a>&nbsp;teaching increased liability could not be the opinion of Rabbi Ishmael or Rabbi Akiva. It could not belong to Rabbi Ishmael because he says that one can be liable only for oaths concerning the future, not ones about the past. <br />
<br />
Why could it not be the opinion of Rabbi Akiva? The other part of the "two that are four" ruling says, "There are two types of awareness of impurity that are really four. One can forget that he is impure and eat sacrifices or enter the Temple – these are two. The other two are when one remembers that he is impure, but forgets that these are sacrifices that he is eating, or that it is the Temple area that he is entering." We know, however, that Rabbi Akiva does not make one liable for the second type of unawareness.<br />
<br />
<i><b> Counter-argument:</b></i><br />
<br />
We could still say that the ruling is in agreement with both Rabbi Ismael and Rabbi Akiva, but for the other two transgressions, one is not liable to bring a sacrifice but only to receive lashes.<br />
<br />
Art: Discussing The Talmud by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Isidor Kaufmann</span>

---

### content/shevuot/30.txt
<a id="src-00336"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/30.txt`

Shevuot 30 – The Oath of Testimony
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwbHPInM_CeXf_vcEbKn6aGxyjNgMPJG7qr10dVtzyxXy4FPVpkPTeCV__F_egWLmm9LKA0VC9LLFSo9hB7Q_dSm-4gC1490mPduJHJ60B9Mapu3L_ipJ0ltPRleHzUlMT9-ru8tQrSFc/s1600/Louis+Charles+Auguste+Couder+-+The++Court+Oath.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwbHPInM_CeXf_vcEbKn6aGxyjNgMPJG7qr10dVtzyxXy4FPVpkPTeCV__F_egWLmm9LKA0VC9LLFSo9hB7Q_dSm-4gC1490mPduJHJ60B9Mapu3L_ipJ0ltPRleHzUlMT9-ru8tQrSFc/s320/Louis+Charles+Auguste+Couder+-+The++Court+Oath.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The oath of testimony concerns witnesses who know the testimony that a litigant needs to win a monetary case. If the litigant asks them to testify and they falsely swear that they do not know the testimony, they are liable to bring a "variable" offering when they admit that they lied. If the litigant has other means to win the case or has other witnesses, the liability for false oath does not apply.<br />
<br />
In addition to making a personal oath, one can answer “Amen” to someone saying, “I adjure you. " This also becomes an oath, as if he said it himself. In the case of the oath of testimony, if one repeats in court that he does not know the testimony after being adjured, this also becomes an oath.<br />
<br />
Art: The  Court Oath by Louis Charles Auguste Couder
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/31.txt
<a id="src-00337"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/31.txt`

Shevuot 31 – Mnemonic: Defense, Ignoramus, Theft, Deceit
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjz05Q7RrcgFc2TzPjHoI-akyVzX6i2xevKgoiryKr7yi76O0beTxex7K17p2CXuJhGjZSVqow16sU12fKLxNrixV7nXYxu7iI09JYtPNSDZ5mafPk_oDHGCopLdOmHQsTzunXlUFnE_PY/s1600/Andre+Collin+-+Poor+People.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjz05Q7RrcgFc2TzPjHoI-akyVzX6i2xevKgoiryKr7yi76O0beTxex7K17p2CXuJhGjZSVqow16sU12fKLxNrixV7nXYxu7iI09JYtPNSDZ5mafPk_oDHGCopLdOmHQsTzunXlUFnE_PY/s320/Andre+Collin+-+Poor+People.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Occasionally the Talmud puts in mnemonics for those who are committing it to memory. They are also keys to a deeper meaning. This mnemonic is for the four of the thirteen teachings that can be derived from the phrase “<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/23-7.htm">Distance yourself from falsehood</a>,” and here they are<br />
<br />
* A judge should not defend his opinion about which he has doubts, merely to avoid embarrassment; <br />
* He should not have an ignorant student assist him in judgment;<br />
* He should not join another judge whom he knows to be a thief; <br />
* If he has discerned that the witnesses are lying, he should not continue to judge, internally putting the blame on the witnesses; <br />
* A student assisting a judge who sees an argument in favor of a poor man should not be silent about it; <br />
* If a student sees his teacher making a mistake, he should not wait till the teacher concludes the judgment, for the student to demolish it and get honor; <br />
* If a teacher tells his student “You know me, I won't lie. Someone owes me a maneh ($5,000), but I have only one witness – please be the second one” - the student should not be a witness;<br />
* Six more...<br />
<br />
Art: Andre Collin - Poor People</span>

---

### content/shevuot/32.txt
<a id="src-00338"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/32.txt`

Shevuot 32 – Multiple Oaths
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgKPeSWKyPTTEfv5cYDnagVQUdvGACtDScXsnBtk94Hk9Fgp1nIgsYIiCUTLCmS5rtjZSMqyoXuNzobcBh-JMr3dzNhTotenoQRRKkrmx8sdZE6o5V1VLN6-nCD5AyTOjPTEnD-Wc-wfxs/s1600/William+Morris+Hunt+-+Justice+Lemuel+Shaw.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgKPeSWKyPTTEfv5cYDnagVQUdvGACtDScXsnBtk94Hk9Fgp1nIgsYIiCUTLCmS5rtjZSMqyoXuNzobcBh-JMr3dzNhTotenoQRRKkrmx8sdZE6o5V1VLN6-nCD5AyTOjPTEnD-Wc-wfxs/s320/William+Morris+Hunt+-+Justice+Lemuel+Shaw.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one adjured the witnesses five times outside the court, and they denied knowing the testimony, and then they came to court and admitted that they did know the testimony, they are not liable at all. A denial issued outside a court is not legally significant. However, if they denied knowing testimony in court, they are liable for each and every time they were adjured. Their single denial applies to each adjuration separately; thus, they are liable to bring five offerings.<br />
<br />
If he adjured them five times, this time in court, and they denied knowing testimony in court, they are liable for only one oath. Rabbi Shimon explained, "Why? Because, after denying knowledge of the testimony in court, they cannot retract and confess that they do know the testimony." Their denial in court of knowing testimony is itself treated as testimony, and the rule is that once witnesses give testimony in court, they can never retract or alter that testimony. Therefore, for the last four oaths, they are no longer eligible to give testimony.<br />
<br />
Art: Justice Lemuel Shaw by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">William Morris Hunt</span>

---

### content/shevuot/33.txt
<a id="src-00339"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/33.txt`

Shevuot 33 – Oath of Testimony Must Be About Money
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhf6O5LBbvfhlziAcT7U3ITgu_xASmHomqwS8FYt0cJsS9zXG6U5JAwZBFdZIhGEjuM94CUw6LaXSQS2cPoOmNvQVrKPvcjb_2iAMPmCe5PBayanLCCuomNZnw9J1lcagjGDHIfY6oBy0A/s1600/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Wheat+Stacks+With+Reaper.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhf6O5LBbvfhlziAcT7U3ITgu_xASmHomqwS8FYt0cJsS9zXG6U5JAwZBFdZIhGEjuM94CUw6LaXSQS2cPoOmNvQVrKPvcjb_2iAMPmCe5PBayanLCCuomNZnw9J1lcagjGDHIfY6oBy0A/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Wheat+Stacks+With+Reaper.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In all the following cases, one is not liable for a false oath of testimony.<br />
<br />
A claimant told two witnesses, "I adjure you to come and testify that I am a Kohen" - because this is not a monetary claim. Or he said "that I am a Levi," "that so-and-so is a Kohen," or "that so-and-so is a Levi."<br />
<br />
If he said, "That so-and-so raped another man's daughter" or "seduced another man's daughter." Although the rapist must pay damages and the fifty-shekel fine, and the claim is monetary, but in order to be liable, the witnesses need to be adjured by the claimant himself, to whom the rapist is to pay, not by another person.<br />
<br />
"That he ignited my stack of grain on the Sabbath," - since desecration of the Sabbath is punishable by death, this frees one from monetary liability even when he is not executed.<br />
<br />
Art: Wheat Stacks With Reaper by Vincent Van Gogh</span>

---

### content/shevuot/34.txt
<a id="src-00340"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/34.txt`

Shevuot 34 – Why Can Oath of Testimony Be Only About Money?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTYnB5pu7POCrIxGvH4hy33csy4zLKlAb8kHw6Uq5MBGjOIJLnbfdFVothBSpT6j0-ugd7siNQK2-fvhUArrkFRgVNplRQd0Wd8pAhNB-TMxl1rRbTkjSNT0HDwVcwsBDI37Qq0JzNwOA/s1600/Thomas+Hickey+-+John+Mowbray+with+his+money+agent.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTYnB5pu7POCrIxGvH4hy33csy4zLKlAb8kHw6Uq5MBGjOIJLnbfdFVothBSpT6j0-ugd7siNQK2-fvhUArrkFRgVNplRQd0Wd8pAhNB-TMxl1rRbTkjSNT0HDwVcwsBDI37Qq0JzNwOA/s320/Thomas+Hickey+-+John+Mowbray+with+his+money+agent.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Here are three (of five) explanations why this is so.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Eliezer:<br />
<br />
In <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/5-1.htm">the verse about the oath of testimony</a>, the word "or" is stated two times, and in <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/6-2.htm">the verse about the oath of deposit</a>, the word "or" is also stated two times. This establishes the connection between the two, and just as the oath of deposits speaks only of monetary claims, so too does the oath of testimony speak only of monetary claims.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiva:<br />
<br />
In the phrase, "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/5-5.htm">When one shall become guilty regarding one of these matters</a>," the word "of" is a limitation, meaning that there are cases when one is liable and cases when one is not, and when is one liable? - in money matters!<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yose HaGlili:<br />
<br />
"...<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/5-1.htm">and he is a witness who either saw or knew</a>." Which testimony can be established by either seeing or knowing alone? - in money matters!<br />
<br />
Art: John Mowbray with his money agent by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Thomas Hickey</span>

---

### content/shevuot/35.txt
<a id="src-00341"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/35.txt`

Shevuot 35 – Various Verbiages of Oath
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi9ZS3kc746vcUyTBOPIuJ86mQ5w8xg13pdjH1XI1EoL1c7dfuQYuIWPqZRiMGc8lz9YrLgzkU2SyiSAY9TwfUWdIKF34TNLgsyEQX2IPCQ3VpylKSilQqVvaI1p09q1_PWsRcKWU8WkDo/s1600/Jules+Alexandre+Grun+-+A+Group+O+-Artists.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi9ZS3kc746vcUyTBOPIuJ86mQ5w8xg13pdjH1XI1EoL1c7dfuQYuIWPqZRiMGc8lz9YrLgzkU2SyiSAY9TwfUWdIKF34TNLgsyEQX2IPCQ3VpylKSilQqVvaI1p09q1_PWsRcKWU8WkDo/s320/Jules+Alexandre+Grun+-+A+Group+O+-Artists.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There are five cases when there is no liability for the false oath of testimony: where one testifies to a promise, not actual giving of money; where he adjures them to testify when they will know the testimony in the future; where he addressed himself to a whole group of people, without specifying the witnesses; where their testimony would be hearsay or otherwise invalid; where he sent his slave to adjure the witnesses, or if it was the defendant, not the claimant, who adjured them.<br />
<br />
If one said, "I adjure you," "I command you," I bind you" (to testify) – the witnesses are liable.<br />
<br />
If they swore by heaven and earth, then they are not liable. However, if they swore by "Lord," by the Tetragrammaton, by the "Lord of Hosts," "Compassionate," "Merciful," "Slow to Anger," "Abundantly Kind," or by any of the subordinate Names of God, they are liable.<br />
<br />
Art: A Group Of Artists by Jules Alexandre Grun
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/36.txt
<a id="src-00342"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/36.txt`

Shevuot 36 – Oath of Deposit
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgtELpPJdNdAIBc1K3sz0RTPvF970AgFOmaIYTSMtma5j780u0PRXge9ytx982_RfbbAfT0nutd80TDu1c1_V2Rgz4k-Pq1Bq0smwQAW5lHOPSJCVOtSNETsz72oYMwaEGDu0aN6vUnxTQ/s1600/George+Baxter+-+Stolen+Pleasures.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgtELpPJdNdAIBc1K3sz0RTPvF970AgFOmaIYTSMtma5j780u0PRXge9ytx982_RfbbAfT0nutd80TDu1c1_V2Rgz4k-Pq1Bq0smwQAW5lHOPSJCVOtSNETsz72oYMwaEGDu0aN6vUnxTQ/s320/George+Baxter+-+Stolen+Pleasures.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a person in possession of someone else's money – either a deposit, a loan, a stolen article, or the like – swears that he does not have it, he has taken what is known as an oath of deposit. If he swore falsely and subsequently confesses his sin, he must repay the principal plus an additional fifth and bring a "guilt offering" sacrifice in the Temple.<br />
<br />Although this oath applies to all types of debts, not just deposits, it is nevertheless called the "oath of the deposit" because a deposit is the first example mentioned in the Torah.<br />
<br />
The oath of deposit applies to both men and women, to non-relatives and relatives, to those who are qualified to serve as witnesses, and to those who are disqualified, in court and out of court.<br />
<br />
In truth, there is no reason to think these rules would not apply, but they are only stated to contrast with the oath of witnesses discussed previously.<br />
<br />
Art: Stolen Pleasures by George Baxter
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/37.txt
<a id="src-00343"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/37.txt`

Shevuot 37 – Lashes and/or Sacrifice for the Oath of Deposit?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGH8-SusXmeDSqK7oirSvox46UYB4UoxR8hpWE6nqM-LDYo0KvXDOxiaUcwv99FaTWjEeEEtnIeOQDoSTa7ACMQYvGO1V6sEgNi0L5wufWCnKj-20dupOawoWT5EtfTHrHzz5GDqUpB7M/s1600/Paul+Charles+Chocarne-Moreau+-+The+Spanking.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGH8-SusXmeDSqK7oirSvox46UYB4UoxR8hpWE6nqM-LDYo0KvXDOxiaUcwv99FaTWjEeEEtnIeOQDoSTa7ACMQYvGO1V6sEgNi0L5wufWCnKj-20dupOawoWT5EtfTHrHzz5GDqUpB7M/s320/Paul+Charles+Chocarne-Moreau+-+The+Spanking.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Kahana met three students from the Academy of Rabbah while they were studying oaths and asked them a question: "If one deliberately lied when taking an oath of deposit and he was warned by witnesses, what is the law?"<br />
<br />
Usually, one gets lashes for willful transgressions and brings a sacrifice for mistakes. The oath of deposit is special, however, since one brings a sacrifice even for knowing violation of it. So then he is not lashed. Or maybe he is not lashed when there is no warning, but if there is a warning, he is lashed? It could also be both.<br />
<br />
They answered him based on a well-known ruling that the oath of deposit is more stringent than the oath of testimony, for one gets lashes for it. Therefore, they said, he gets lashes but does not bring a sacrifice.<br />
<br />
When they related this to Rabbah, he said, "Incorrect question!" If the witnesses saw him accept the deposit, the claimant can have the deposit back based on their testimony, and his denial carries no weight; therefore, it is not a true oath of deposit anyway! But Rabbah was later proven incorrect.<br />
<br />
Art: The Spanking by Paul Charles Chocarne-Moreau
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/38.txt
<a id="src-00344"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/38.txt`

Shevuot 38 – Court-Imposed Oaths: Partial Admission
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgf7XHsLPrW-JwLAWkAyZ1Qr6H5U_nllBp1pxE0ZC-GAeGY3yoeOLzz1smYujWSjB7lJnS5qnNPFdMVqhA2lWKn-rT8i0IonZu91sRekx8HGx8Y9EgxfxOrZqYohr2g7ZMRPN9np5k8pv8/s1600/Thomas+Waterman+Wood+-+The+Doubtful+Coin.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgf7XHsLPrW-JwLAWkAyZ1Qr6H5U_nllBp1pxE0ZC-GAeGY3yoeOLzz1smYujWSjB7lJnS5qnNPFdMVqhA2lWKn-rT8i0IonZu91sRekx8HGx8Y9EgxfxOrZqYohr2g7ZMRPN9np5k8pv8/s320/Thomas+Waterman+Wood+-+The+Doubtful+Coin.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Courts have limited authority to impose oaths and can do so in only three specific cases: partial admission, the oath of custodians, and the single-witness oath.<br />
<br />
The first case, partial admission, has its own additional limitations. This oath can be imposed only if the claim is for at least two silver maot (a volume of 32 grains of barley, about $10) and the admission is at least a prutah coin (half a silver barleycorn, under 25 cents). <br />
<br />
In addition, partial admission must be for the same kind. For example, if the plaintiff says, "You have two silver coins in my possession," and the defendant responds, "You have only one prutah coin in my possession," the defendant is free from an oath because the claim was for silver, and the admission was for copper.<br />
<br />
Art: The Doubtful Coin by Thomas Waterman Wood
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/39.txt
<a id="src-00345"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/39.txt`

Shevuot 39 – Oaths Are Too Serious a Matter to be Administered
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiKk32hIrY5LRu8uko5ybyHk66-il7McbmZHbV4Ddy8pyEliGJbbK6DWN9EOnzX9e2YA3s8WNn1lJ1r_wnDzmw0hUVTiTBmej5cD9VrkMbO0Pph0hmfmQbYjokXSq7-I29dCeZbevls0z0/s1600/H.+de+la+Charlerie+-+King+Louis+XVI+Swearing+on+the+Book+of+the+Constitution.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiKk32hIrY5LRu8uko5ybyHk66-il7McbmZHbV4Ddy8pyEliGJbbK6DWN9EOnzX9e2YA3s8WNn1lJ1r_wnDzmw0hUVTiTBmej5cD9VrkMbO0Pph0hmfmQbYjokXSq7-I29dCeZbevls0z0/s320/H.+de+la+Charlerie+-+King+Louis+XVI+Swearing+on+the+Book+of+the+Constitution.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Since the punishment for violating a Biblical oath is very severe, Rashi writes that Jewish courts in his time refrained from asking the defendant to swear and instead placed a curse on any defendant who would lie.<br />
<br />
If the defendant says, “I will not swear,” he is immediately excused from court, owes money, and does not come back to change his opinion. However, if he says, “I shall swear,” those standing there recite the phrase “Turn away from the tents of these wicked men.” Even the plaintiff is considered guilty for causing an oath, since he should not have dealt with an untrustworthy person.<br />
<br />
The judges tell him, “You should know that the whole world trembled at the words 'Do not take the name of Hashem your God in vain'” And why is this? Because about a false oath it says, “God will not absolve.”<br />
<br />
Art: H. de la Charlerie - King Louis XVI Swearing on the Book of the Constitution<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/4.txt
<a id="src-00346"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/4.txt`

Shevuot 4 – Rabbi Yehudah the Prince Combines Conflicting Opinions
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLSUd2wv0lG2u4baI8VC68Gs8Dk30MHP7oOIUcHhbSxF_y5tzbPAcj2aQAy2dBZNATEOfuhcbHgQqY9nu-h1cEDb7djLkqQBYJrH6zK-uC5GVS22BVeTMyI4R8ouLqDFrDuQdbbxIx47w/s1600/Thomas+Hovenden+-+The+Discussion.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLSUd2wv0lG2u4baI8VC68Gs8Dk30MHP7oOIUcHhbSxF_y5tzbPAcj2aQAy2dBZNATEOfuhcbHgQqY9nu-h1cEDb7djLkqQBYJrH6zK-uC5GVS22BVeTMyI4R8ouLqDFrDuQdbbxIx47w/s320/Thomas+Hovenden+-+The+Discussion.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The ruling of “Two that are four” <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/06/shevuot-oaths-3-who-authored-two-that.html">has been established as referring to the liability of lashes, not sacrifices</a>. This change allowed us to say that it could be the opinion of both Rabbi Ishmael and Rabbi Akiva.<br />
<br />
Why is this needed? When Rabbi Yehudah, the compiler of all Mishnaic rulings, formulates an anonymous ruling, he implies that this is the majority opinion and thus the final law. Without our (somewhat forced) explanation, we would have two major authorities disagreeing with the final law.<br />
<br />
However, there is still a problem with our answer. To receive lashes, the person must be warned. If he is warned, how can we talk about him being unaware that he eats sacrifices or that he enters the Temple?<br />
<br />
We are forced to retract our explanation about lashes. Rather, we now answer that Rabbi Yehudah the Prince compiles conflicting opinions of different Sages in one ruling. He does so because he wants to assemble together all cases of “Two that are four.”<br />
<br />
Art: The Discussion by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Thomas Hovenden</span>

---

### content/shevuot/40.txt
<a id="src-00347"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/40.txt`

Shevuot 40 – Claim Amounts for Oaths
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiWYEqpkzIbhz3laYfUxU7ETrhZ92LjiktOgtNBuAOBFt_akPEExe1-pNrue_7t23fZcKsFTe94Xzjmo4s1gyZxy8HQCdiizXEQT3cHfp5bHjlRRGvILjixfTrzhdc0oTENeC4V0CBrGEE/s1600/G.+Alluisetti+-+The+Public+Ministry+of+Finance.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiWYEqpkzIbhz3laYfUxU7ETrhZ92LjiktOgtNBuAOBFt_akPEExe1-pNrue_7t23fZcKsFTe94Xzjmo4s1gyZxy8HQCdiizXEQT3cHfp5bHjlRRGvILjixfTrzhdc0oTENeC4V0CBrGEE/s320/G.+Alluisetti+-+The+Public+Ministry+of+Finance.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/08/shevuot-oaths-38-court-imposed-oaths.html">We have learned previously</a> that to warrant an oath, the amount in question must be at least two silver maot. However, is it the total amount of the claim or the denied amount?<br />
<br />
Rav says that it is the denied amount. For example, the total amount of the loan in dispute may be 10, and the defendant may agree that he owes 8, but deny the remaining 2. In contrast, Shmuel says that the claim itself must be for 2 maot. Then, if the defendant denies 1 perutah or admits one perutah, he is liable for an oath.<br />
<br />
Rava said: "The precise reading of the ruling indicates Rav's opinion, but the words of the Torah sound like the opinion of Shmuel." The precise reading of the ruling seems to agree with Rav, because it says that the minimum amount of "the claim" must be 2 maot, but never mentions how much the denied amount should be, which means that by "claim" the ruling means "the denial". The Torah, however, sounds closer to the opinion of Shmuel, when it says "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-9.htm">this is it!</a>" indicating that the amount of claim itself is essential when it is 2 coins.<br />
<br />
Art: The Public Ministry of Finance by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">G. Alluisetti</span>

---

### content/shevuot/41.txt
<a id="src-00348"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/41.txt`

Shevuot 41 – A Borrower Would Not Outright Deny a Loan
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgnsv8A45yEulPnK3evsbWX7wSbrWdg7iP88Q9l4jMp8PIxbmYZ7EVjRjmL0QMsnpekhSw3rpGqBOkgn8rDuGDo7cyGliwQgPvHEVn56ZLxPQAMA9hlov-h1PtNt5MbA2xIEtaKloT-whI/s1600/Leopold+Loeffler+-+Forgotten+Speech.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgnsv8A45yEulPnK3evsbWX7wSbrWdg7iP88Q9l4jMp8PIxbmYZ7EVjRjmL0QMsnpekhSw3rpGqBOkgn8rDuGDo7cyGliwQgPvHEVn56ZLxPQAMA9hlov-h1PtNt5MbA2xIEtaKloT-whI/s320/Leopold+Loeffler+-+Forgotten+Speech.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the plaintiff says, "You have a maneh ($5,000) of mine in your possession," and the defendant responds, "You do not have anything of yours in my possession," - the defendant is free from an oath, since there is no admission of partial liability.<br />
<br />
The Torah assumes that no person would be so impudent as to deny a loan outright. After all, the lender did him a favor by loaning money interest-free (and other types of loans are anyway forbidden). When the borrower partially admits a loan, but partially denies it, this is just because he does not have all the money and plans to pay the balance later on. This is not right, however, and the Torah imposes an oath on him. But we cannot assume this in the case of complete denial.<br />
<br />
Later, however, this situation changed, and the Sages established an “Oath of Forgetfulness” even for cases of complete denial. However, this Rabbinical oath is different in that it can be switched: if the defendant does not want to take an oath, the plaintiff can take one and collect the money.<br />
<br />
Art: Forgotten Speech by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Leopold Loeffler</span>

---

### content/shevuot/42.txt
<a id="src-00349"></a>
