**Source file:** `content/shevuot/42.txt`

Shevuot 42 – When an Oath is Not Required
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiX0CFs551Hze2OqrmGkvuC0KyjAHselyCPgjTFyEWqYdOr2iv17wdpji1_hzcfOwPFY-B-kC9RsOcPhl11bYtSwrNtuW3QcRHK5AceR-bHBeeZRKJLGyv-k5A_s7ttCA8xWefPN_-sxn0/s1600/John+George+Brown+-+Woman+Seated+At+Window.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiX0CFs551Hze2OqrmGkvuC0KyjAHselyCPgjTFyEWqYdOr2iv17wdpji1_hzcfOwPFY-B-kC9RsOcPhl11bYtSwrNtuW3QcRHK5AceR-bHBeeZRKJLGyv-k5A_s7ttCA8xWefPN_-sxn0/s320/John+George+Brown+-+Woman+Seated+At+Window.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">These are things regarding which one need not swear: slaves, notes of indebtedness, land, and consecrated property. Incidentally, for these things, one is not liable to a twofold penalty for theft, nor to  the fourfold and fivefold penalty for stealing, killing, and selling an animal.<br />
<br />
An unpaid custodian, who ordinarily must swear that he was not negligent in guarding an object entrusted in his care, does not have to swear regarding these things. A paid custodian, who is ordinarily liable for theft, does not have to swear and does not pay for those things.<br />
<br />
An oath requires a definite measure. For example, if one says, "I delivered a house full of produce to you for safekeeping," or "a purse full of money," and the guardian says, "I do not know how much you gave, but I am giving you back everything," - he does not have to swear. However, if he says that the produce reached the ceiling beam, and the guardian says it only reached the window, the guardian has to swear due to his partial admission.<br />
<br />
Art: Woman Seated At Window by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">John George Brown</span>

---

### content/shevuot/43.txt
<a id="src-00350"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/43.txt`

Shevuot 43 – Lender is Responsible for Collateral
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjsY8Zo51JaOD1unGH3KbOnDQQ-Q0GOylgpACwS5yjlrSjqSE2w8dGK6ErFafTSntccq6zZzxyffWl7K2Ttcb1hYqSkcrAxzLYMulQHwCmg2BatOebkYzULddIZJTyQUw1bK4zIqIm3xr4/s1600/Hans+Thoma+-+Earth.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjsY8Zo51JaOD1unGH3KbOnDQQ-Q0GOylgpACwS5yjlrSjqSE2w8dGK6ErFafTSntccq6zZzxyffWl7K2Ttcb1hYqSkcrAxzLYMulQHwCmg2BatOebkYzULddIZJTyQUw1bK4zIqIm3xr4/s320/Hans+Thoma+-+Earth.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one lends his fellow money on collateral, he is considered a paid guardian of this collateral. Therefore, should the collateral be lost or stolen, the lender is liable for it. If the collateral was worth more than the loan, the lender must pay the balance to the borrower, and if it was worth less than the loan, the borrower pays the balance to the lender. <br />
<br />
If the borrower claims that the collateral was worth the loan amount, and the lender says that it was less, the borrower is free from an oath, since there was no admission of partial liability. However, if the borrower says that he owes a balance, and the lender says that he owes a larger balance, the borrower has to swear. <br />
<br />
Who swears as to the value of the collateral? The one in whose possession it was lost, or the lender. If the borrower were to swear and not be careful in assessing the value, and the lender would later produce the deposit, the borrower would be disqualified from taking oaths and from testifying in court. This would be unfair, so the Sages shifted the oath to the lender.<br />
<br />
Art: Earth by Hans Thoma
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/44.txt
<a id="src-00351"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/44.txt`

Shevuot 44 – Sages-Decreed Oaths
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPSNkK7fm2kmB9_ibo9zDvIIyaOCZaEBHEtILS2bWlxUrlCOecWq9-FwUxPYISGeutTviNtV26pV6QOlaHCiD5Nl5ZHoPHAYep0hxG5cxrc1OuvioxFUhQa9S2zURd2yalUuXlnBXPOyk/s1600/Thomas+Pollock+Anschutz+-+Iron+Workers+at+Noontime.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPSNkK7fm2kmB9_ibo9zDvIIyaOCZaEBHEtILS2bWlxUrlCOecWq9-FwUxPYISGeutTviNtV26pV6QOlaHCiD5Nl5ZHoPHAYep0hxG5cxrc1OuvioxFUhQa9S2zURd2yalUuXlnBXPOyk/s320/Thomas+Pollock+Anschutz+-+Iron+Workers+at+Noontime.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">All who swear an oath decreed by the Torah swear to free themselves from liability. However, the Sages have decreed additional oaths, and as a result of taking these oaths, one swears and collects the money due to him. They include a hired worker, a victim of theft, a victim of assault, one whose opposing side is a suspect regarding oaths, and a storekeeper regarding that which is written in his ledger.<br />
<br />
What is the case of a hired worker? If a hired worker tells his employer, "Pay me my wages!", and the employer says, "I already paid!", but the worker says, "I never received them" - the worker swears that he has not been paid and then collects the wages. This oath is because the employer has many workers and may think he has already paid that one.<br />
<br />
Art: Iron Workers at Noontime by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Thomas Pollock Anschutz</span>

---

### content/shevuot/45.txt
<a id="src-00352"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/45.txt`

Shevuot 45 – Sages-Decreed Oaths – Continued
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgqf4XLpi25QgogmB7uxuae8q5fpZRLFzdxuabU1KdFNrN8t-EgDXY2EUO9bnIOOjX78OgJAqXiRcc21_FEwsQxjq6Zgm04S1BlU7CTb9u5J2imWgExG-mWo5qxRbqdCpEsM_bMZv7QnZA/s1600/John+Frederick+Peto+-+The+Poor+Man%27s+Store.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgqf4XLpi25QgogmB7uxuae8q5fpZRLFzdxuabU1KdFNrN8t-EgDXY2EUO9bnIOOjX78OgJAqXiRcc21_FEwsQxjq6Zgm04S1BlU7CTb9u5J2imWgExG-mWo5qxRbqdCpEsM_bMZv7QnZA/s320/John+Frederick+Peto+-+The+Poor+Man%27s+Store.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In what circumstances does the victim of a theft swear and collect? The witnesses saw a creditor who entered the debtor's house to take something as security from him, without his permission. That is prohibited by the Torah, and one who takes collateral forcefully is considered a thief. The creditor then left with unidentified utensils under his cloak. The debtor can swear and collect his utensils. Of course, this law also applies to a full-fledged thief.<br />
<br />
Similarly, suppose witnesses saw that someone entered another's domain whole and left injured. In that case, since it is improbable that the victim would self-inflict those injuries, he can swear and collect damages.<br />
<br />
What is the case of a storekeeper with his ledger? If an employer tells the storekeeper, "Give my workers <a href="http://shmsoft.com/view/perm/talmud%20coins.jpg">two selah</a> in small change," and the shopkeeper says, "It is written in my ledger that I gave as you instructed." Still, the workers say, "We did not take anything from the storekeeper," they both swear and collect the payment from the employer.<br />
<br />
Art: The Poor Man's Store by John Frederick Peto<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/46.txt
<a id="src-00353"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/46.txt`

Shevuot 46 – Wage Dispute
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVctikwpZPCXzuv2rqdTY3Xtgs8YaEGQU26b239uXUUVhHV_I6yEX1fiMRjUFW8tYRIsPzJ7HUsnFViTkKY00m3IjH9s6wQTmMxUolgQ-7_K4cN9eQbQMtZ04CtBYpTGa3x556mO8ElGo/s1600/Jean-Francois+Millet+-+Forest+workers+in+the+wood+saws.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVctikwpZPCXzuv2rqdTY3Xtgs8YaEGQU26b239uXUUVhHV_I6yEX1fiMRjUFW8tYRIsPzJ7HUsnFViTkKY00m3IjH9s6wQTmMxUolgQ-7_K4cN9eQbQMtZ04CtBYpTGa3x556mO8ElGo/s320/Jean-Francois+Millet+-+Forest+workers+in+the+wood+saws.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a craftsman says to his employer, "You stipulated to me a fee of two sela coins for this job," and the employer says, "I stipulated to you a fee of only one sela," - Shmuel said, "In that case the employer swears that he stipulated only one sela, and the craftsman looses the contested sela."<br />
<br />
But why should this be so? Didn't we <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/08/shevuot-oaths-44-sages-decreed-oaths.html">require the worker to swear about his wages in a similar case</a>? The answer is that in this other case, the employer may have forgotten which worker he had already paid. However, in the case of a wage dispute, the employer certainly remembers the stipulation.<br />
<br />
Art: Forest workers in the woods with saws by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jean-Francois Millet</span>

---

### content/shevuot/47.txt
<a id="src-00354"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/47.txt`

Shevuot 47 – One, Who Has to Take an Oath but Cannot, Pays
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi8Tj1ZqFtOsa9DFs1nNwWhaQYvHtYtB8GybsYCr_lptF13FVDFkwqTh9zSq4tPxCNFkYGSXB7z8ZRDxGfREvQ_xtBiK3mV2m9nxbUcZhGk3zc04NMz6QZ9gZdvlX0pt9NdniEZ7Una_ek/s1600/Rembrandt+Van+Rijn+-+Anna+Accused+by+Tobit+of+Stealing+the+Kid.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi8Tj1ZqFtOsa9DFs1nNwWhaQYvHtYtB8GybsYCr_lptF13FVDFkwqTh9zSq4tPxCNFkYGSXB7z8ZRDxGfREvQ_xtBiK3mV2m9nxbUcZhGk3zc04NMz6QZ9gZdvlX0pt9NdniEZ7Una_ek/s320/Rembrandt+Van+Rijn+-+Anna+Accused+by+Tobit+of+Stealing+the+Kid.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the defendant has to take an oath, such as when he agrees that he owes half of the amount and has to swear about the other half, but cannot, because he once swore falsely, the oath is shifted to his opponent, the plaintiff. If, however, the plaintiff is also not trustworthy, then the rule is that "the oath returns to its place."<br />
<br />
What does "the oath returns to its place" mean? The Teachers in Babylon, that is, Rav and Shmuel, say it means that the oath returns to Sinai, where it was stated, "do not steal." The courts do not get involved,  and the one who is dishonest must fear Divine retribution.<br />
<br />
The teacher in Israel, that is, Rabbi Abba, says that the oath returns to the one who was initially obligated to take it, in order to free himself from liability. And, since he cannot swear, he remains liable and has to pay.<br />
<br />
Art: Anna Accused by Tobit of Stealing the Kid by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Rembrandt Van Rijn</span>

---

### content/shevuot/48.txt
<a id="src-00355"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/48.txt`

Shevuot 48 – When Borrower Dies
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgyz5iq8bNeuVonMjfxFjwc0mAaAaE2ewZJPflV-R5AqEKNJz5cXC0OrqOoIEMX7VLTpaIqDgQvKJMK1xb9j3rRZTw_iClBHcIl_tjMZXAWCb9t79YoKXiryOyE5LeinZFvZgLeJDV5KDo/s1600/Luigi+Nono+-+A+Child%27s+Funeral.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgyz5iq8bNeuVonMjfxFjwc0mAaAaE2ewZJPflV-R5AqEKNJz5cXC0OrqOoIEMX7VLTpaIqDgQvKJMK1xb9j3rRZTw_iClBHcIl_tjMZXAWCb9t79YoKXiryOyE5LeinZFvZgLeJDV5KDo/s320/Luigi+Nono+-+A+Child%27s+Funeral.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When a lender dies, the money that he had loaned out belongs to his children. Before collecting, they must take an "oath of heirs," which states that to the best of their knowledge, the debt was not repaid.<br />
<br />
However, as both Rav and Shmuel have stated, that is only true if the lender died first. If, on the other hand, the borrower died first, then the lender has to take a definite oath that the debt was not repaid. His children cannot take such a definite oath, but only to the best of their knowledge, and it is not sufficient. Thus, if their father dies, they cannot collect the money.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Elazar in Israel disagreed, "Just because the lender's children cannot take the same oath as him, must they forfeit their father's debt?"<br />
<br />
In practice, the ruling of Rav and Shmuel was followed, but, since there was not a definite decision either way, if a judge ruled in accordance with Rabbi Elazar, his ruling would also stand.<br />
<br />
Art: A Child's Funeral by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Luigi Nono</span>

---

### content/shevuot/49.txt
<a id="src-00356"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/49.txt`

Shevuot 49 –  Four Custodians Who Swear
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMZtkHH1LGTZUgzCPz2erfNYbBP_8pjeKqQIDg8nhU4MVleheWoElIaj-FGDB4apjt9viyAbaT7vbpIlCFOJAjTbcghHZ3rQTEYnmR5ZpugcVY9DYJFY0v50-W7xguQx9grzP7IoYQALs/s1600/Joaquin+Sorolla+y+Bastida+-+Oxen+on+the+beach.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMZtkHH1LGTZUgzCPz2erfNYbBP_8pjeKqQIDg8nhU4MVleheWoElIaj-FGDB4apjt9viyAbaT7vbpIlCFOJAjTbcghHZ3rQTEYnmR5ZpugcVY9DYJFY0v50-W7xguQx9grzP7IoYQALs/s320/Joaquin+Sorolla+y+Bastida+-+Oxen+on+the+beach.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Any of <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/05/bava-metzia-34-four-custodians.html">the four types of custodians</a> may swear regarding the object he was keeping. Even if he swears falsely, he is not necessarily liable for a false oath. <br />
<br />
If his oath would change his obligation from one liability to another, such as that the ox he borrowed died naturally, when actually it was captured, and in both of which cases he would be liable to pay, his oath changes nothing. If he confesses that he swore falsely, he does not have to bring the usual sacrifice nor pay one-fifth extra. The same would apply if he swore to change from one exemption to another, or from an exemption to a liability.<br />
<br />
However, if he swears to change from liability to exemption but then confesses, he needs to bring a guilt offering and must add one-fifth to the amount.<br />
<br />
Art: Oxen on the beach by Joaquin Sorolla y Bastida</span>

---

### content/shevuot/5.txt
<a id="src-00357"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/5.txt`

Shevuot 5 - Two Ways to Violate Shabbat, Which are Really Four
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipTzpj3o_VsUw1gUJX4UbWtvSX9Gun_A4gzZcvgP8cXYN4qyouZoAOWS569w2KnDzeLI-pYMBseLx-hRXQNtFQGwI8BQ4EO264HVn8B4mIUXL9q20skPZF2kJD2asWyAufrE-7mhzXRJA/s1600/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Venetian+Water+Carriers.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipTzpj3o_VsUw1gUJX4UbWtvSX9Gun_A4gzZcvgP8cXYN4qyouZoAOWS569w2KnDzeLI-pYMBseLx-hRXQNtFQGwI8BQ4EO264HVn8B4mIUXL9q20skPZF2kJD2asWyAufrE-7mhzXRJA/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Venetian+Water+Carriers.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">It is forbidden on Shabbat to take items from a private domain (like one's house) to a public domain (like the street). For example, if the owner of a house stands inside, takes an object, lifts it up, transfers it outside, and puts it in the basket of a poor person; or if the poor person takes the object from the owner of the house, lifts it up, and puts it in his basket. <br />
<br />
The Sages added two more prohibitions, where the action is done jointly. For example, if the house owner takes the object and lifts it up, and the poor person accepts it while outside, neither of them has completely violated Shabbat.<br />
<br />
There are also four cases of bringing an object in. This makes a total of eight, and is not parallel to the “two that are four!” To answer this, we count only those cases where one is liable for a Torah violation, and equate taking out to bringing in, because they are both, in essence, changing the domain, and you will get exactly two that are four.<br />
<br />
Art: Venetian Water Carriers by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">John Singer Sargent</span>

---

### content/shevuot/6.txt
<a id="src-00358"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/6.txt`

Shevuot 6 – White Spots on Skin
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhyZrNRmfbG2RirKqyhtsdXx42hPw99Mp4D48ezTrQMYgJRVGHvewulDvLZGBNOpb_QBx9D9rfBpR3EyggIlE6bzE2XTiKc4hbOH8P5ZVNGSeIjcoZSr4_iwUkg0lG8tRJP4KK4efeo0e4/s1600/Rembrandt+Van+Rijn+-+The+King+Uzziah+Stricken+with+Leprosy.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhyZrNRmfbG2RirKqyhtsdXx42hPw99Mp4D48ezTrQMYgJRVGHvewulDvLZGBNOpb_QBx9D9rfBpR3EyggIlE6bzE2XTiKc4hbOH8P5ZVNGSeIjcoZSr4_iwUkg0lG8tRJP4KK4efeo0e4/s320/Rembrandt+Van+Rijn+-+The+King+Uzziah+Stricken+with+Leprosy.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There are two shades of white on one's skin that signify that one is possibly sick with a spiritual leprosy called Tsara'at. Two are mentioned in the Torah as “white spot” and “raised white spot.” Two more are derived from the word “additional,” meaning auxiliary shades of white. They thus make “two that are four.”<br />
<br />
“White spot” is white as snow; “raised white spot” is darker and is like white wool. The shade auxiliary to snow-white is that of lime of the Temple; the shade auxiliary to white wool is the color of egg membrane. The minimal size of a white spot that is considered significant is that of a lentil bean. Two primary shades combine with each for the size of the bean; auxiliary shades combine with their primary ones. This is analogous to two kings and their governors.<br />
<br />Yehoshuah, the son of Rabbi Akiva, asked, “Why not just teach that any shade that is whiter than the egg membrane is significant?” Rabbi Akiva answered him, “To test the Kohanim, who must be knowledgeable in the shades of Tsara'at, to judge.”<br />
<br />
Art: The King Uzziah Stricken with Leprosy by Rembrandt Van Rijn</span>

---

### content/shevuot/7.txt
<a id="src-00359"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/7.txt`

Shevuot 7 – Awareness of Impurity
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhFeYkGQkGOjQ2HS0-6wTJxGEUhGyFLY5td9iHuis3EuDo_b0TdLtUQIYdrKFu4z02N44rBzqNAJ4Kli_jx0cXmM9zNo6X-LnzwSujCKpP2gz3oCdv9UBdwyU7J2WhOkn-bCJz6nFMq1TE/s1600/Theodore+Robinson+-+Girl+with+a+goat.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhFeYkGQkGOjQ2HS0-6wTJxGEUhGyFLY5td9iHuis3EuDo_b0TdLtUQIYdrKFu4z02N44rBzqNAJ4Kli_jx0cXmM9zNo6X-LnzwSujCKpP2gz3oCdv9UBdwyU7J2WhOkn-bCJz6nFMq1TE/s320/Theodore+Robinson+-+Girl+with+a+goat.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one knew that he was ritually impure, forgot about it, and then visited the Temple or ate sacrifices, once he remembers his impurity, he is obligated to bring a “variable” sacrifice, the nature of which depends on his means.<br />
<br />
If, however, he never recalls that he was impure, the goat that is brought as a sacrifice on Yom Kippur, and the day of Yom Kippur itself, suspends his punishment. When he finally finds out about his past impurity, he brings a “variable sacrifice.”<br />
<br />
But maybe the goat of Yom Kippur atones even for idol worship, prohibited relations, and bloodshed, because these are also characterized as “impure”? - No! Yom Kippur atones only “from impurities of the Children of Israel,” but not all impurities – these are the words of Rabbi Yehudah. Rabbi Shimon derives the same answer from the context of Yom Kippur – it atones only for matters related to the Temple service.<br />
<br />
Art: Girl with a goat by Theodore Robinson
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/8.txt
<a id="src-00360"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/8.txt`

Shevuot 8 – Causes of Spiritual Leprosy – Tsara'at
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjxA2RnAwGIAPQg_Pq_c1FVsc5sL6gVz69xTihf5Zrv2gYlrpxN_5vl0PAOKwCKWRDrcxvOI2WqJ730XH7h40CowP5s-GbUClo51Z9Q-YC-THTN8ZChqxUjgJceZmZZ7TR2ZPA3vHX8Sh0/s1600/Carl+von+Marr+-+The+Gossips.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjxA2RnAwGIAPQg_Pq_c1FVsc5sL6gVz69xTihf5Zrv2gYlrpxN_5vl0PAOKwCKWRDrcxvOI2WqJ730XH7h40CowP5s-GbUClo51Z9Q-YC-THTN8ZChqxUjgJceZmZZ7TR2ZPA3vHX8Sh0/s320/Carl+von+Marr+-+The+Gossips.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Seven sins lead to Tsara'at: talking badly about others, bloodshed, vain oath, forbidden unions, haughtiness, robbery, and stinginess.<br />
<br />
The goat brought on Yom Kippur suspends one's punishment for going to the Temple while impure. But if it does not erase it completely, how does the suspension help? Rav Zeira said, "By suspension, we mean that if the sinner dies before becoming aware of his transgression, he dies without this sin on his record."<br />
<br />
Said Rava to Rav Zeira, "The sinner does not need the goat sacrifice for this, for if he dies, then death itself purges him of his sin!" Rather, Rava said, "The purpose of suspension is to shield him from the suffering he deserves on account of his sin, until he becomes aware of it and gains complete atonement through his offering."<br />
<br />
Art: The Gossips by Carl von Marr<br />
</span>

---

### content/shevuot/9.txt
<a id="src-00361"></a>

**Source file:** `content/shevuot/9.txt`

Shevuot 9 – A Sacrifice for God
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEio5kExP7K54qT_dOQmYj7PRTSRp06iYgHl7RvAkvX9e-hwxggofTUfSdsGUs96Pyr7_7rsubDyL4A1r54-6vd-STEkJkwodtEXOuf7epbVYIv2d00dQhA9BmW55xdpAwJi9f14iJnZ8ww/s1600/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Man+and+Woman+Contemplating+the+Moon.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEio5kExP7K54qT_dOQmYj7PRTSRp06iYgHl7RvAkvX9e-hwxggofTUfSdsGUs96Pyr7_7rsubDyL4A1r54-6vd-STEkJkwodtEXOuf7epbVYIv2d00dQhA9BmW55xdpAwJi9f14iJnZ8ww/s320/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Man+and+Woman+Contemplating+the+Moon.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">The goat sacrifice brought on&nbsp;<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">the New Moon atones for ritual impurities that never became known to the impure person. That is why this sacrifice is called "<a href="" target="_blank">a sacrifice for God</a>" - for God alone knows of this impurity -&nbsp;</span>these are the words of Rabbi Yehudah.<br />
<br />
Additionally, as Resh Lakish explained, God said, "This he-goat shall be an atonement for something that I did." When God created the Sun and the Moon, they were initially of the same size. The Moon complained that it was inappropriate for two rulers to rule at once, and God said, "You are right, go and make yourself smaller." The Moon then reasoned that it was unjust that it should suffer just because it raised a valid point. To placate the Moon, God promised that the Jewish people would bring a sacrifice for God's sin, as it were, on every New Moon.<br />
<br />
Art: Man and Woman Contemplating the Moon by Caspar David Friedrich</span>

---

### content/sotah/15.txt
<a id="src-00367"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/15.txt`

Sotah 15 – The sacrifice of jealousy
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6trVLYYUzv-bzvrh2VMI1xjodGYv2gE6MX4mNR17ng6lSM590lweYu86CjEGKumDGyBuXEm5ycz-7UVUigZ_7fO0tqp_e6q3l2sQctkdkfXQ38yy2f6ru3x21O4fxdhgz6XyTK7Cv_q5z/s1600/The+Mirror+by+William+Merritt+Chase.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6trVLYYUzv-bzvrh2VMI1xjodGYv2gE6MX4mNR17ng6lSM590lweYu86CjEGKumDGyBuXEm5ycz-7UVUigZ_7fO0tqp_e6q3l2sQctkdkfXQ38yy2f6ru3x21O4fxdhgz6XyTK7Cv_q5z/s320/The+Mirror+by+William+Merritt+Chase.jpg" width="168" /></a>A husband who suspects his wife brings a sacrifice different from all other sacrifices. Usual flour offerings use wheat, but this one is made of barley. Regular offerings have oil and frankincense added, but this one is brought without. Why is it he, and not the wife, that brings it? – Because one should not be his or her own accuser. But why does the husband deserve this inferior sacrifice? – The wife is  unfaithful when the husband is unfaithful or gives another reason.
<br />
<br />
Proceeding, the Kohen brings an earthenware cup and pours in water from the purifying water of the priests. This large vessel stands in the Temple courtyard for the Kohanim to pour water on their hands and feet before they start their service. It is made of copper mirrors used by Jewish women in Egypt to look beloved to their husbands. 
<br />
<br />
How much water does the Kohen put in? Half a log, or about 5 ounces. Rabbi Yehudah says he takes only a quarter of a log or about 2.5 ounces. Parenthetically, Rabbi Yehudah will also require a shorter text to be erased into this water later in the preparation. The Kohen enters the Temple building, turns to the right, and finds a particular stone with a ring. He lifts up the stone, gets the dust from under it, and makes it float on the water. 
<br />
<br />
Art: The Mirror by William Merritt Chase

---

### content/sotah/2.txt
<a id="src-00372"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/2.txt`

Sotah 2 – Man deserves what he gets
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgRJWE0hLZXHdzCc8NUmM9C79oBEYZRy7P1ZW56lMXfD64xlz303ctKh4b2TQ1Fa72rFFUWMNYn5qcIhTd8uPGIF883lW4ER_kN44T9hKviHTE8pnOmVBNxXBsg-JZ0KiEemIrHcNIRAJzh/s1600/Portrait+of+a+Couple+by+French+Unknown+Masters.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="238" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgRJWE0hLZXHdzCc8NUmM9C79oBEYZRy7P1ZW56lMXfD64xlz303ctKh4b2TQ1Fa72rFFUWMNYn5qcIhTd8uPGIF883lW4ER_kN44T9hKviHTE8pnOmVBNxXBsg-JZ0KiEemIrHcNIRAJzh/s320/Portrait+of+a+Couple+by+French+Unknown+Masters.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
If a husband becomes particularly jealous of his wife in regard to a certain fellow, he can warn her not to seclude herself with that fellow. If she does, she is suspected of adultery and needs to go to the Temple with her husband to be cleared of the suspicion. The Talmud will discuss the details of this warning, but first, it asks how the previous Tractate, Nazir, is connected to this one? 
<br />
<br />
The answer is that a man who sees such strife between a husband and wife should abstain from wine because he too may become involved in similar affairs, and often through wine. However, this is not a good reason because, in that case, Sotah should come first, and then Nazir. Rather, the connection is more roundabout: in Ketubot (Dowry),&nbsp; we mentioned one who vows in regard to his wife, from there, we went to discuss Vows (Nedarim) and then Nazir, which is a type of vow, and finally, we are back to Sotah, just as we said before, but in a different order.
<br />
<br />
In truth, man should blame himself for any marital trouble since the wife one deserves is in proportion to his own good qualities; in general, finding the right spouse is as hard in the eyes of God as splitting the Red Sea. But why should it be so hard? We know that the spouse is predestined for every person when he or she is born!? – When we say that it is hard, we mean the second marriage.
<br />
<br />
Art: Portrait of a Couple by French Unknown Masters

---

### content/sotah/20.txt
<a id="src-00373"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/20.txt`

Sotah 20 – The importance of teaching one's daughter Torah
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjHqPlM4XI9rjCBjuWa3CJBRhICw2J3HOGwoqwaEqV86hBi23hOwvdWuLpWOhzpGd3WF25vsO2cfM-8bdrAgXSXxN1ipdTrVFPdW0cbVIb_HtakfV6t3hBzbgKHhDS3GLTpLYwlgcqN9pNb/s1600/Elegant+Couples+In+Interiors+by+Pio+Ricci.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjHqPlM4XI9rjCBjuWa3CJBRhICw2J3HOGwoqwaEqV86hBi23hOwvdWuLpWOhzpGd3WF25vsO2cfM-8bdrAgXSXxN1ipdTrVFPdW0cbVIb_HtakfV6t3hBzbgKHhDS3GLTpLYwlgcqN9pNb/s320/Elegant+Couples+In+Interiors+by+Pio+Ricci.jpg" width="223" /></a>In order to exonerate the wife of a jealous husband, the Kohen prepared flour sacrifice and a drink as <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/11/sotah-15-sacrifice-of-jealousy.html">described before</a>. He then copies the words of the Torah concerning this onto a separate scroll. If she refuses to drink before these words are erased into the drink, the flour is burned as invalid, and the drink is poured out. If she refuses to drink after the scroll is erased, they help her, presuming that she is blameless, as she maintains, just became scared. 
<br />
<br />
If she and her lover actually committed adultery, then he dies in whatever place he is, and she dies in the Temple. However, if she has merit related to Torah, it will protect her for a year, two, or three. Because of this, Ben Azzai said that a man is required to teach his daughter Torah – so that this will protect her, even if she has a problem with her husband.
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Eliezer, on the contrary, says that teaching Torah to women is frivolous. Incidentally, Kabbalah maintains that eventually, women will desire and get the opportunity to learn Torah. Baal Shem Tov founded a secret society for teaching Torah to women. 
<br />
<br />
Art: Elegant Couples In Interiors by Pio Ricci

---

### content/sotah/22.txt
<a id="src-00375"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/22.txt`

Sotah 22 – On falsehood
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYHDkf48cnhk7mY_P0esdBUdZwaITO5mSny-_HGlFHdxyLbBVnhy-dkMFmNtXf3eE4ITK-ycqk_EKggLywnpjRI6CV1xAC0j8rZPgRC1nVwqFcXM-eRub0EfPoRKevexcGtrlqy99axO-Z3uVGaIjy82pJUG8DXHcIH27AgVjm5oj0U603Mu_Y3UmgFA/s1200/Old%20Man%20Reading%20by%20Johannes%20Weiland.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1200" data-original-width="857" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYHDkf48cnhk7mY_P0esdBUdZwaITO5mSny-_HGlFHdxyLbBVnhy-dkMFmNtXf3eE4ITK-ycqk_EKggLywnpjRI6CV1xAC0j8rZPgRC1nVwqFcXM-eRub0EfPoRKevexcGtrlqy99axO-Z3uVGaIjy82pJUG8DXHcIH27AgVjm5oj0U603Mu_Y3UmgFA/s320/Old%20Man%20Reading%20by%20Johannes%20Weiland.jpg" width="229" /></a></div>One who learned something about Torah but did not complete his education by learning the Talmud is called progressively an unlearned person, an ignoramus, one not trusted on any issue of kosher foods, and even an evil person. Why is all that? Because such people appear knowledgeable, but in reality, their opinions are not based on accurate knowledge. 
<br />
<br />
Also despised are those who pretend to be modest and turn their eyes away from women, and as a result, they may bump into a wall or hit their foot against a stone, but it is all just a pretense. Evil is those who say, "Tell me how I can improve, and I will do it," which implies that they have already perfected themselves in their estimation.
<br />
<br />
King Yannai (who killed all members of the Sanhedrin) bequeathed this to his wife: not to be afraid of the Sages' vengeance because they are righteous and will not do wrong, and neither be afraid of the followers of King's Yannai sect, because they esteem her. She should only be scared of false people who pretend to be righteous like Pinchas, but their deeds are licentious as those of Zimri.
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Old Man Reading by Johannes Weiland

### content/sotah/27.txt
<a id="src-00380"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/27.txt`

Sotah 27 – Just as she, so is he
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfU5CzuM_w779kLr3u_ACZ9ahN1aVoKnLK2kwv8OFGMwcpADSRmY38tcbUe1UR2JHzrvXsraKb1O0RoxMcE8NpG8XWodh60EQwdEgjql2D5wdpyUeaDvK2UmLRTQBWUEiYp23rQMQO4jdn/s1600/Young+lovers+interrupted+by+Henry+John+Yeend+King.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfU5CzuM_w779kLr3u_ACZ9ahN1aVoKnLK2kwv8OFGMwcpADSRmY38tcbUe1UR2JHzrvXsraKb1O0RoxMcE8NpG8XWodh60EQwdEgjql2D5wdpyUeaDvK2UmLRTQBWUEiYp23rQMQO4jdn/s320/Young+lovers+interrupted+by+Henry+John+Yeend+King.jpg" width="252" /></a></div>
We mentioned that the paramour of the suspected wife does not go unpunished. What is the source of this statement? – In the phrase "The waters will go," the word "will go" is mentioned twice, once for her and another time for him. So whatever happens to her in the Temple also happens to him - in whichever place he is.
<br />
<br />
The other word that is repeated is "became prohibited." Why is that? The first time it tells us that after the husband warns his wife and she nevertheless hides away with a specific man, the husband cannot live with her any longer; he must either give her a divorce (Get) or take her to the Temple to be cleared of suspicions. The second repetition applies to the paramour – should he desire to marry the woman after the divorce, he cannot because she is also prohibited to him. 
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiva derives the same law from an extra "and" (letter vav in Hebrew), that is, "<b>and</b> the waters will go." Many more laws were expounded by Rabbi Akiva and others on that day. What is the story of "that day"? It is <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/09/brachot-28-that-day.html">the day mentioned in tractate Brachot</a>&nbsp;when the Sages removed Rabban Gamliel from his control over the Sanhedrin and changed the policy of allowing only strictly selected students into the study hall. Now anybody who wanted could come in. As a result, many talented students could offer groundbreaking insights.
<br />
<br />
Art: Young lovers interrupted by Henry John Yeend King

---

### content/sotah/28.txt
<a id="src-00381"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/28.txt`

Sotah 28 – Laws of purity 
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgDAoq_5WufX8szXkAOFFbuEp-gHkmPXbiZfIft3Fp9kWhs9in-L_JPvp4fpG634D2ffkzLWWy5DBUZ_KlkCn9cZRSz-AQcXL9rBshuKX3iM8GVXtcQFlfZyogTFWf9Byl86bDbzMECl8pJ/s1600/Two+Rats+by+Vincent+Van+Gogh.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="225" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgDAoq_5WufX8szXkAOFFbuEp-gHkmPXbiZfIft3Fp9kWhs9in-L_JPvp4fpG634D2ffkzLWWy5DBUZ_KlkCn9cZRSz-AQcXL9rBshuKX3iM8GVXtcQFlfZyogTFWf9Byl86bDbzMECl8pJ/s320/Two+Rats+by+Vincent+Van+Gogh.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
Laws of purity are learned from the laws of a suspected wife. Here's how. Her innocence is in doubt because she went into a private hiding place with a particular man. But her purity would not be in doubt if she was talking with him in public.
<br />
<br />
In the same way, if there is a doubt about some other purity, such as, for example, a man who might have touched a dead rat, the question now is whether he is considered ritually impure. If this happened in the street, he is declared pure; if it occurred in a cave, he is impure. This unusual law goes beyond the regular rule of "let's treat it as a doubt." There is no doubt that he is definitely pure in the street but impure in the cave.
<br />
<br />
Another law can be learned by noticing that a suspected wife is a human being who can be asked about her status. So with other situations, the distinction between happenings in the street and in a cave applies only to a human who can be questioned. For example, he is unsure whether he touched a rat. Then the rule about the street or cave applies. But if he is sure that he touched the rat, and the doubt is about the rat itself, such as whether it was alive at this time or already dead – then he is always declared pure because a rat cannot be asked.
<br />
<br />
Art: Two Rats by Vincent Van Gogh

---

### content/sotah/29.txt
<a id="src-00382"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/29.txt`

Sotah 29 – Can you ask him?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgiHlAbwII0-T8kIWVfXI4Z19nJGzE7BabU_6Yi028fEx03xSuuCPqa_pROYNh4LyNMuZbtwXlvfrHateHX7rF35esLQbWCw0dOsQfOp7_Vxz88PtuTFC-FZtU4OYAD9E3eIgtMYeP16dib/s1600/A+pottery+bowl%252C+cuts+of+meat+and+onions+on+a+table+by+French+School.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="219" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgiHlAbwII0-T8kIWVfXI4Z19nJGzE7BabU_6Yi028fEx03xSuuCPqa_pROYNh4LyNMuZbtwXlvfrHateHX7rF35esLQbWCw0dOsQfOp7_Vxz88PtuTFC-FZtU4OYAD9E3eIgtMYeP16dib/s320/A+pottery+bowl%252C+cuts+of+meat+and+onions+on+a+table+by+French+School.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
Earlier, we saw a difference in the laws of purity between humans, whom you can ask about the situation, and inanimate objects that cannot be questioned. If a doubt about purity arises in a yard (or another private area), then if it is about a human, who can be queried, he is declared impure. But if it is about a piece of meat, for example, then it is declared pure. We learned this law from the purity of a suspected wife, but there is yet another source for it.
<br />
<br />
“<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=7#P2896">If sacrificial meat comes into touch with something impure, then it cannot be eaten; otherwise, a ritually clean person may eat it</a>.”&nbsp;
<br />
<br />
The beginning of the phrase says that impure meat is not eaten. So we understand that doubtfully impure meat can be eaten. But the end talks about pure meat that may be eaten. And we can derive that doubtfully pure meat cannot be eaten. So now we have two contradictory indications, whether one can eat doubtfully pure meat. You can only explain it if you say that the doubt is prohibited when it refers to a human, who can be asked, and allowed if it refers to the meat itself, which obviously cannot be questioned.
<br />
<br />
Art: A pottery bowl, cuts of meat and onions on a table by French School

---

### content/sotah/3.txt
<a id="src-00383"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/3.txt`

Sotah 3 – Is jealousy good or bad?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2o9DnDOimbiteh1xeoI56x3_fk6RlHycB0E1iYTjxEiKrD_QLaeoHnjtOk9M-2sVtjtRqYRRX5Lpy-ngtXWrjMkvxwgKmwHwXrFSArZs8YIYanROjFjzKlSolr0La6lgl20AEx3FhTgAo/s1600/Couple+at+the+window+by+Georg+Friedrich+Kersting.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2o9DnDOimbiteh1xeoI56x3_fk6RlHycB0E1iYTjxEiKrD_QLaeoHnjtOk9M-2sVtjtRqYRRX5Lpy-ngtXWrjMkvxwgKmwHwXrFSArZs8YIYanROjFjzKlSolr0La6lgl20AEx3FhTgAo/s320/Couple+at+the+window+by+Georg+Friedrich+Kersting.jpg" width="247" /></a>Previously <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/10/sotah-2-man-deserves-what-he-gets.html">we learned</a> that a man can warn his wife not to conceal herself with a particular fellow. Is that jealousy good or bad? Some say it is forbidden for a man to warn his wife this way. He should always try to maintain peace. A warning of this sort will lead to strife between the husband and wife or a conflict between her and her neighbors. Others say jealousy is caused by the spirit of purity and is good. 
<br />
<br />A long time ago, the spiritual level of men declined. Since men were not blameless themselves, the test of a suspected wife stopped working. 
<br />
<br />
Even when circumstances warrant this, Rabbi Ishmael only permits a man to warn his wife, but Rabbi Akiva makes it an obligation. They have also disagreed similarly in another matter: a Kohen is not allowed to go to a cemetery and become ritually impure. However, he is allowed to do it for his relative. Here too, Rabbi Ishmael says that he is only allowed to do so, but Rabbi Akiva says he should insist and bury his relatives.
<br />
<br />
Art: Couple at the window by Georg Friedrich Kersting

---

### content/sotah/30.txt
<a id="src-00384"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/30.txt`

Sotah 30 – Purity, Song at the Sea, and other sundry questions
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5Qsn_MLja0P46uwswH_AcNz1AkQIl9tIjWQ9uGM8gDkeo8uWlTqc7GNWWwjWDjQGfmfROYZ2dzhpMr2T1Ouvl4MMTskqljV1FEL67dXS2hfeQsZ387rze2jUnHLEAfBhZf6YmMaOqPiAH/s1600/The+Israelites+after+the+Crossing+of+the+Red+Sea+by+Hieronymous+III+Francken.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="212" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5Qsn_MLja0P46uwswH_AcNz1AkQIl9tIjWQ9uGM8gDkeo8uWlTqc7GNWWwjWDjQGfmfROYZ2dzhpMr2T1Ouvl4MMTskqljV1FEL67dXS2hfeQsZ387rze2jUnHLEAfBhZf6YmMaOqPiAH/s320/The+Israelites+after+the+Crossing+of+the+Red+Sea+by+Hieronymous+III+Francken.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
We mentioned that <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/11/sotah-27-just-as-she-so-is-he.html">one special day saw many novel interpretations from newly-admitted students</a>. The list continues with Rabbi Akiva's rule of the degrees of ritual impurity.
<br />
<br />
Actually, a thing is either pure for Temple service or not. However, the Sages classified the impurity into six levels, from the dead body (called the grandfather of impurity) down to the "father of impurity," the first level, the second level, and all the way to the fourth. For example, some say that if you have a dough from which the priest portion (challah) needs to be separated, then this dough has the same law as the challah itself and can become impure with third-degree impurity. Others say that since the challah has not separated, the dough can only become impure in the second degree, not the third. 
<br />
<br />
Another point that Rabbi Akiva explained was the way the Israelis sang the Song at the Red Sea. He said that Moses sang the phrase, and they repeated the summary. Others – that they repeated the phrase itself. For example, Moses said, "I will sing to God," and they repeated, "I will sing to God." Then Moses said, "Since He is exalted," but they said, "I will sing to God." Others say that they repeated, "Since He is exalted."
<br />
<br />
Art: The Israelites after the Crossing of the Red Sea by Hieronymous III Francken

---

### content/sotah/31.txt
<a id="src-00385"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/31.txt`

Sotah 31 – Parrot
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjid7IBtNp1Li9A69c53Iaqak3zn2CnCLNHLI7W9FP5LyZEm8rBrJpZ3i7RKaPYOliHop__92k0OMWWDbB0dptCQkoED-0NQquRGE5DdgzGP3ITF3k-UPhgLXhdwf0lrSmYlhT7UWh_waCi/s1600/Woman+With+Parrot+by+Paul+Cezanne.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjid7IBtNp1Li9A69c53Iaqak3zn2CnCLNHLI7W9FP5LyZEm8rBrJpZ3i7RKaPYOliHop__92k0OMWWDbB0dptCQkoED-0NQquRGE5DdgzGP3ITF3k-UPhgLXhdwf0lrSmYlhT7UWh_waCi/s320/Woman+With+Parrot+by+Paul+Cezanne.jpg" width="227" /></a>A husband who jealously warns his wife not to seclude herself with a particular man is putting himself into several complications. If he hears that she did seclude herself with the man, even as told to him by a parrot, he then needs to divorce her. This is the opinion of Rabbi Eliezer, who says that we would even believe the husband himself, so once the husband is sure about the seclusion, his warning is triggered. However, he has to pay her the money of the Ketubah since he does not have any proof,  and it was his fault that he got into this situation.
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehoshua says that the evidence of seclusion must be more substantial: if the affair is the talk of the town, so that women who get together to weave and chat at night discuss this, then the situation is certain to the point that the water drinking test will not work anyway. It is not, however, certain to the point of her losing the Ketubah, so in that situation, the husband still pays. 
<br />
<br />
If seclusion is established, she gets exonerated by drinking bitter water in the Temple. However, there are also witnesses that cohabitation has taken place during seclusion. In that case, again, the water test is unnecessary; this time, she gets divorced and loses the Ketubah. This witness can be anyone who usually needs to be a better witness. Even those five close female relatives, like her mother-in-law, who would not be believed to testify about the death of her husband (because of their vested interest in her downfall) are believed here. Except if these five women testify to cohabitation, she still retains the Ketubah payment right.
<br />
<br />
Art: Woman With Parrot by Paul Cezanne

Sotah 36 – Why to learn languages
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjlQnQPG9Ys3bLkjzObug-Ku4Sp33itrHpehyphenhyphenhZSBJ0LjgA-kh9PWLVMeipG3VqT4J0GjMo38wzLGvhKBXfzz2x1CQHWBdo5BhoRh8jhonwQXXXy2oASemIkz3r4QEnbqMCpVgW2cznR9tQ/s1600/Joseph+in+the+Pharaoh%2527s+Palace+by+Jacopo+%2528Giacomo%2529+Amigoni.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="275" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjlQnQPG9Ys3bLkjzObug-Ku4Sp33itrHpehyphenhyphenhZSBJ0LjgA-kh9PWLVMeipG3VqT4J0GjMo38wzLGvhKBXfzz2x1CQHWBdo5BhoRh8jhonwQXXXy2oASemIkz3r4QEnbqMCpVgW2cznR9tQ/s320/Joseph+in+the+Pharaoh%2527s+Palace+by+Jacopo+%2528Giacomo%2529+Amigoni.jpg" width="320" /></a>The words that the Kohen says to a suspected wife can be expressed in any language because the procedure is described as "And the Kohen will say to the women," – which means that any language in which he says it is good.
<br />
<br />
By contrast, the blessings and the curses that the Jews pronounced before entering Israel, on the mounts Eival and Grizim, had to be said in Hebrew because these it is described as "And they will answer and say" – and the same words ("answer and say") are used when doing <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/10/yevamot-2-sister-in-law.html">chalitzah</a>, which has to be done exactly as written, in Hebrew.
<br />
<br />
The Talmud then describes how the blessing and curses were pronounced, what else happened on the day when the Jews crossed the Jordan River and entered the Land of Israel, and about the Torah, which had to be written on stones in seventy languages, in precise translations, for everyone to know.
<br />
<br />
It then turns to Joseph, who knew seventy languages, as mentioned in the story of his appointment to be viceroy. He was given a test by Pharaoh, and he replied in every language that Pharaoh spoke. But how did he learn all of them? – Angel Gabriel visited him the night before and taught them. Joseph would go up one step on the way to Pharaoh's throne with each language. In the last step, he spoke in Hebrew, and Pharaoh could not answer. Pharaoh made Joseph give an oath not to reveal this.<br />
<br />
Art: Joseph in the Pharaoh's Palace by Jacopo (Giacomo) Amigoni

### content/sotah/38.txt
<a id="src-00392"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/38.txt`

Sotah 38 – How to bless
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi8binNFpzTgyMZEX2MiBdzmnRwNg5_e-6vSCV2rnQWaL7F6yd_Jfaqd1tf-cVaeKs6X21_K0SdgXM93sA3x4S6Pb1sqqktRkTREwa0FIXtlqWU_IBNnGQMlGexjbrLvAt4S8AX2Ttkpfpi/s1600/Jacob+Blessing+the+Children+of+Joseph+by+Rembrandt+Van+Rijn.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="260" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi8binNFpzTgyMZEX2MiBdzmnRwNg5_e-6vSCV2rnQWaL7F6yd_Jfaqd1tf-cVaeKs6X21_K0SdgXM93sA3x4S6Pb1sqqktRkTREwa0FIXtlqWU_IBNnGQMlGexjbrLvAt4S8AX2Ttkpfpi/s320/Jacob+Blessing+the+Children+of+Joseph+by+Rembrandt+Van+Rijn.jpg" width="320" /></a><a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=6#P3843">Every day the Kohanim (Priests) should bless the people</a> and say to them, "May God bless you and keep watch over you. May God make His presence enlighten you and grant you grace. May God direct His providence toward you and grant you peace."
<br />
<br />
They say these three phrases outside the Temple, and the people answer "Amen" to each one. They also say the Name of God not as written, but using a changed form called "Adnut" and denoting ruler or master. 
<br />
<br />
In the Temple, they said the blessing as one long phrase, without an interruption for "Amen." In the Temple, people, as a rule, did not say Amen, but responded with a longer term; here, this phrase would interrupt the blessing. Moreover, in the Temple, the Priests pronounced the Name of God as it is written, in the form that implies "was, is, and will be." The exact pronunciation of it is not known today.
<br />
<br />
Art: Jacob Blessing the Children of Joseph by Rembrandt Van Rijn

### content/sotah/4.txt
<a id="src-00394"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/4.txt`

Sotah 4 – How long do they need?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgGQO8pQiCGeRzuCL6QGe9dlUbJoCbSTn1S-6_fFCPet4BBR2HZWtBjxVzONHtG57dmBnTprqo7EwfLqUuHYQAbYpsOHaS8ienqXbYzOU4to9N1pfF0clDggnFNCJfvUCb6A3mn8c2g3gwY/s1600/An+elegant+couple+on+a+bench+by+a+pond+by+Johann+Heinrich+The+Elder+Tischbein.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="303" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgGQO8pQiCGeRzuCL6QGe9dlUbJoCbSTn1S-6_fFCPet4BBR2HZWtBjxVzONHtG57dmBnTprqo7EwfLqUuHYQAbYpsOHaS8ienqXbYzOU4to9N1pfF0clDggnFNCJfvUCb6A3mn8c2g3gwY/s320/An+elegant+couple+on+a+bench+by+a+pond+by+Johann+Heinrich+The+Elder+Tischbein.jpg" width="320" /></a>We learned that if a man gets especially jealous of his wife in relation to a particular fellow, he can warn her not to hide with that fellow. The warning is really for both, and later consequences may befall both. Now if they do hide, suspicion has grounds, and the husband is not allowed to continue living with his life normally any longer but needs to clear her of the suspicions in the Temple.
<br />
<br />
How long do they have to hide? - Enough to do the thing. What thing? - Cohabitation. And what is that? – We <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/11/yevamot-56-what-is-legally-considered.html">learned before that the beginning of it</a> – the touch of the genitals – is sufficient; the disagreement was only about was is considered a touch.<br />
<br />
So how long is that? Rabbi Ishmael said, “The time it takes to mix a cup of wine.” Rabbi Yehoshuah said, “Time to drink it.” Ben Azai said, “Time to fry an egg.” Rabbi Akiva: “Time to swallow that egg.”  Chanin ben Pinchas said, “The time it takes her to put a hand into a basket and take out a bread.” The Talmud discusses these and other opinions and changes them; for example, “Time to drink” really means “Time to mix and then drink.” It also wants to know what kind of bread, wheat or barley, warm or cold, and what type of basket, but does not find an answer. 
<br />
<br />
Every opinion came from personal experience, except perhaps for Ben Azai, who was never married, because Torah study took all his time. Then how did he know? Some say he married but separated, some – that his teacher told him, and yet others – that God tells His secrets to those who are aware of Him. 
<br />
<br />
Art: An elegant couple on a bench by a pond by Johann Heinrich The Elder Tischbein

---

### content/sotah/40.txt
<a id="src-00395"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/40.txt`

Sotah 40 – The humility of Rabbi Abbahu
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhJuW-ImG1XN66J56c4hIwKQkdtE1tCgRcH_aqisILhEXyQWj79Uj9VSmJxgL8fA8COD_bZF9dBehiUZs2XC2I3QclcK8Wcac4LN2AWDMa0uJi2j5xhCm6wpfb_4eZUa0Aussv_jHpWhQC2/s1600/A+humble+question+by+Herman+Frederik+Carel+ten+Kate.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="234" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhJuW-ImG1XN66J56c4hIwKQkdtE1tCgRcH_aqisILhEXyQWj79Uj9VSmJxgL8fA8COD_bZF9dBehiUZs2XC2I3QclcK8Wcac4LN2AWDMa0uJi2j5xhCm6wpfb_4eZUa0Aussv_jHpWhQC2/s320/A+humble+question+by+Herman+Frederik+Carel+ten+Kate.jpg" width="320" /></a>While the Kohanim bless the people, the people recite phrases that support and explain those blessings. Why? Is there a servant who will remain silent and not express his appreciation while being blessed by his master?
<br />
<br />
An opposite point of view: people should be silent. Is there a servant who will keep talking while he is being blessed instead of listening?
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Abbahu said, "Initially, I used to say these phrases during the blessing of the Kohanim. But once I saw Rabbi Abba from Akko being silent, I also stopped talking." Rabbi Abbahu continued, "I thought that I had real humility. But once I observed the following behavior of Rabbi Abba. He was delivering a lecture to  a large audience, and his helper – whose task was to repeat the lesson in a loud voice and explain it – was giving different explanations for the same points as Rabbi Abba mentioned. Nevertheless, Rabbi Abba said nothing to him! Compared to him, I do not have humility."<br />
<br />
Then why did Rabbi Abbahu think initially that he had humility? Because of the following incident. Rabbi Abbahu also had a helper to loudly repeat and explain his lectures. The helper's wife told the wife of Rabbi Abbahu that her husband (the helper) had as much knowledge as Rabbi Abbahu, and he showed obeisance just to be polite. The wife of Rabbi Abbahu took affront, but Rabbi Abbahu told her, "It does not matter! Between the two of us, we ensure the people learn Torah."<br />
<br />
Art: A humble question by Herman Frederik Carel ten Kate

---

### content/sotah/42.txt
<a id="src-00397"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/42.txt`

Sotah 42 – Kohen at war
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLaPBG4ESe89wHIEjTU_QZ66VeEKs-sg4cwdkswKAFNbUciaPHleEgXZMEyG_OA6U_Pm9jlobDDpjwnO7IYYkRQrZaDiWHRxKYRwNlw0XBm_1auX_A61PFAsXswkQF6EfGdc_pNTg7XMQ_/s1600/David+beheading+Goliath+by+Michiel+van+Coxie.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLaPBG4ESe89wHIEjTU_QZ66VeEKs-sg4cwdkswKAFNbUciaPHleEgXZMEyG_OA6U_Pm9jlobDDpjwnO7IYYkRQrZaDiWHRxKYRwNlw0XBm_1auX_A61PFAsXswkQF6EfGdc_pNTg7XMQ_/s320/David+beheading+Goliath+by+Michiel+van+Coxie.jpg" width="240" /></a>A Kohen is appointed and anointed to go to war with the army. When the army approaches the enemy, he talks to the soldiers and says the following words, speaking in Hebrew. How do we know that he is talking in Hebrew? Because of the term, "he will say (vediber)." The same word describes Moses, "and Moses said, and God replied with a voice." Since Moses spoke to God in Hebrew, the Kohen at war also spoke in Hebrew.
<br />
<br />
He says, "Listen, Israel (Shema, Israel!), you are approaching an enemy." He uses the word "enemy" to emphasize that if Jews were fighting against Jews, as it happened between the tribes at times, they could expect the victors to be merciful with the captives. He then quotes historical episodes to prove the point. However, with enemies, it is not like that; they will not pity you. This understanding caused them to fight with all their might. 
<br />
<br />"They come against you with human might, as Goliath. You, however, will win, like David did, because your God is walking with you."
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai said, "Why is God walking with them? – because they say the 'Shema' prayer, just like the Kohen at war mentioned. From here, we see that if only all Israel said 'Shema' in the evening and in the morning, they would never fall into the hands of the enemies."
<br />
<br />
Art: David Beheading Goliath by Michiel van Coxie

---

### content/sotah/43.txt
<a id="src-00398"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/43.txt`

Sotah 43 - Exclusions from military service
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj4nVsE_rR7y3wxEAfbY8gs-M6qUqU5Cd-X1YLBZ4qew74UXz0cFCBjClKb0L_BIRAM-S1wMSvbFmoUhjZ7uiisJA1XPn-N-mFQJf_viQelvGd8Zslb8s7al-2IThaaLK7oMwCSVQQbuptL/s1600/The+Engagement+Ring+by+John+Shirley+Fox.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj4nVsE_rR7y3wxEAfbY8gs-M6qUqU5Cd-X1YLBZ4qew74UXz0cFCBjClKb0L_BIRAM-S1wMSvbFmoUhjZ7uiisJA1XPn-N-mFQJf_viQelvGd8Zslb8s7al-2IThaaLK7oMwCSVQQbuptL/s320/The+Engagement+Ring+by+John+Shirley+Fox.jpg" width="238" /></a>After the Kohen at war has spoken the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/12/sotah-42-kohen-at-war.html">words we discussed</a>, it is the turn of army leaders to list exceptions. Anyone who built a new house but has not lived there should return. This applies to buying a home, not only to building it, and the type of house can also be a barn, woodshed, or any other livable structure.<br />
<br />
Anyone who planted a vineyard and has not used it (this includes three years of it being "orlah" and the fourth year after that) - goes back. And anyone who has engaged to a woman but did not get married to her - goes back to his wife and spends a year with her. Finally, anyone who is scared also goes back. He may feel that he did something wrong, and therefore he does not have the merit to win in war. Other reasons are mentioned first so that people who are afraid do not have to be humiliated by admitting it.<br />
<br />
However, these exceptions apply only to voluntary wars that Sanhedrin approves for national reasons. If enemies wage war against Israel with the intent to harm, it is a mitzvah for everyone to participate.<br />
<br />
<br />
Art: The Engagement Ring by John Shirley Fox

---

### content/sotah/44.txt
<a id="src-00399"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/44.txt`

Sotah 44 – What is there to be afraid of?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9qyyyLXWuGn-3sWY8oqXbG6KJFaPUZy8u_tcTp2wiG5ydSE3S66detwMaWcxHyhYES1-DEP6w38kiShCIOVogLXs0wrt9WeAagb4PRluhiFoMz8JLqdPEoIP49egODGDJFZ-QK_nHWijx/s1600/The+Soldier%2527s+Return+by+Girolamo+Induno.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="262" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9qyyyLXWuGn-3sWY8oqXbG6KJFaPUZy8u_tcTp2wiG5ydSE3S66detwMaWcxHyhYES1-DEP6w38kiShCIOVogLXs0wrt9WeAagb4PRluhiFoMz8JLqdPEoIP49egODGDJFZ-QK_nHWijx/s320/The+Soldier%2527s+Return+by+Girolamo+Induno.jpg" width="320" /></a>We mentioned<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/12/sotah-43-exclusions-from-military.html"> that there was a special one among the exclusions from military service</a>: if someone is afraid of war and cannot face danger, he should go back. Some people are soft-hearted, and they may lead the army to lose its morale, contributing to defeat. This is the opinion of Rabbi Akiva.
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yosi HaGlili says he is "afraid and fainthearted" because of his transgressions. For example, he may have spoken between putting on the head and arm tefillin. Or he spoke between the second part of morning prayer (Yishtabach) and the third one – the blessing of Shema. This category is then placed at the end so the transgressors won't be embarrassed, and people may think they claim other exemptions. 
<br />
<br />
After that, the army should be steadfast. Strong soldiers are put in front so that if any of their brothers fall, they help him stand up. Strong soldiers are also placed in the back: if anyone wants to run away, they have authority and axes to stop him – because running away is the beginning of defeat, just as it happened when the Israelites first ran away from Plishtim and <a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt08a04.htm">then were defeated</a>. 
<br />
<br />
As mentioned before, in times of national danger, the exemptions do not apply, but everyone goes to war, even a groom from his room and the bride from her chuppah.
<br />
<br />
Art: The Soldier's Return by Girolamo Induno

---

### content/sotah/49.txt
<a id="src-00404"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/49.txt`

Sotah 49 – Losses
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhbRD-66ckgqWZ5NvD4ekQ2EsUtInC2orBOyRkBD6Q2zjjklfUj7JLxnVUpRj2G9IAGausNMkRjE58Xschva7yZQ1sTDEMmYFw656N8nELbp0ePL1o8CVA9eqITeN7VFy-egVeXxt0fkBdR/s1600/Filial+Piety+by+Jean+Baptiste+Greuze.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="248" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhbRD-66ckgqWZ5NvD4ekQ2EsUtInC2orBOyRkBD6Q2zjjklfUj7JLxnVUpRj2G9IAGausNMkRjE58Xschva7yZQ1sTDEMmYFw656N8nELbp0ePL1o8CVA9eqITeN7VFy-egVeXxt0fkBdR/s320/Filial+Piety+by+Jean+Baptiste+Greuze.jpg" width="320" /></a>After the Temple was destroyed, people of faith disappeared, and only people of small faith remained. And who are these? – Those who have what to eat for today and worry about tomorrow. Honesty, authentic learning, and filial piety were gone. On whom are we to rely? Only on God.
<br />
<br />
When Rabbi Chanina ben Dosa died, there were no more people of good deeds, and after Rabbi Akiva,&nbsp; there were no more supporters of the Torah, and the wells of wisdom were closed. 
<br />
<br />
After Rabbi Yehudah the Prince died, there was no more humility and fear of sin. However, when this teaching was recited in his academy, Rav Yosef corrected the students and told them that there was still genuine humility because he was there. Similarly, Rav Nachman said to take out “no fear of sin” since he was yet alive.<br />
<br />
Art: Filial Piety by Jean Baptiste Greuze

---

### content/sotah/5.txt
<a id="src-00405"></a>

**Source file:** `content/sotah/5.txt`

Sotah 5 – Haughty or humble?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjMT6rrc8bxTA4Wlbfb8jUnv9d8fX-9QoFe9VYhd-lnvUrMW71vQIES1aD8gFClKnINEbxEYEDUkwxmQsyilpEmfGDHuXjwoo0HhPTtf-aO30lLSsjF1dsDD45qzZnxxBFJzVE7aEBu2Aav/s1600/Old+Man+Praying+by+Rembrandt+Van+Rijn.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjMT6rrc8bxTA4Wlbfb8jUnv9d8fX-9QoFe9VYhd-lnvUrMW71vQIES1aD8gFClKnINEbxEYEDUkwxmQsyilpEmfGDHuXjwoo0HhPTtf-aO30lLSsjF1dsDD45qzZnxxBFJzVE7aEBu2Aav/s320/Old+Man+Praying+by+Rembrandt+Van+Rijn.jpg" width="267" /></a>When one is haughty – God's presence in this world sheds tears because of all the tribulations that will eventually befall him. Moreover, when someone is arrogant, God says, "This world is too small for the two of us," or more precisely, "<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt26a1.htm">One who is haughty and proud – him I cannot bear (says God)</a>."<br />
<br />
And yet, a Sage must have a small measure of haughtiness. How much? One-eighth of one-eighth. And for a Sage, it is an ornament, like the upper part of a wheat stalk. Rava said, "One who has it is damned, and one who does not is damned." But it is better to err on the side of humility.
<br />
<br />
When one prays, though, she should definitely be humble. Following this, "<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt2651.htm">Humble spirit is like God's sacrifices</a>," – which means that prayer with a humble heart is equal not to a specific one but to all sacrifices together.<br />
<br />
Art: Old Man Praying by Rembrandt Van Rijn
